Advanced Searches allow you to generate a list of contacts that share something in common. For example, you may want to capitalize on all the Surefire content aimed towards our Spanish speaking communities, or you want to quickly reference a list of people in an area that you could schedule some time with when you’re in town.
Advanced searches give you the ability to do all these quickly using Dynamic Groups or Static Groups.

Contacts
Contacts - Advanced Search
Contacts - Create a Dynamic Group
Dynamic Groups give you the ability to specify criteria for which a user must meet to be in a group instead of manually adding contacts to a group. Contacts can be saved for use when Building an Audience for Deployment.
Review the Use Audience Builder video in Video Library for additional information.
The Search Groups can be updated either dynamically or manually and also exported.
Review Export Contact Search Groups for additional information.
These groups automatically update contacts to be included when their criteria meet the specified criteria so you don't have to go through the process of adding and updating your contacts every time you add or update a contact. A Dynamic Search Group is constantly refreshing and updating its list contents.
Go to Contacts, Search..
Select Create Dynamic Group.
Enter a Name for the list or Group of Contacts that this search includes.
Enter a Description for this search group.
Complete the following fields to define the are of the CRM to limit your search.
User - Choose to search one or more specific User's Contacts. Which Users you see as selection options in the drop-down is dependent upon your Surefire account's permissions and hierarchical position within your Company Organization in Surefire.
Companies - Defaults to the highest level Company you have access to in your Organization. (Assuming you did not specify any Users.) To limit the search to specific Child Companies, type their name to search or select them from the dropdown in the field.
Include Child Companies - If you are searching from the top-level Company but also want to search all Child Companies underneath it, switch this option to Yes. If set to No, the search will be limited to only the Companies selected under Company.
Product - To include Product fields in the search results, select which Products to include here. This will expose fields of the selected Product to your Search Criteria. You may leave this field blank.
Sales Process - If you have selected a product, then you can further limit your search results to include only Contacts who have achieved up to a specified Sales Process. You may leave this field blank.
Select from the list of Available Fields. Alternatively, use the Search Field to enter all or part of Field's name in order to limit the list.
Select the Field Name to move it into the Selected Fields list.
You can return a field from the Selected Fields list by clicking on it again.
Optionally, use the Select All and Deselect All buttons to completely populate or depopulate the Selected Fields list.
Drag the Field Name higher or lower in the order to create the order in which data for these fields are displayed in your search results.
Choose from the Selected Fields list.
Choose the Condition for the search.
This condition will start with the field that you are comparing to your criteria.
Select the Contacts' Contact Tags and specify that this dynamic group requires a contact to have the contact tag such as Spanish Speaker.
Three different options exist for determining tags: Has All Tags - a contact must have all tags you specify to be added to the group Has Any Tag - a contact must have at least one tag you specify to be added to the group Not Tagged With - a contact must not have any tags you specify
Choose custom field Primary Language specify the filed is equal to Spanish.
Two different options exist for determining text field values Is Equal To - The field's value must be equal to the value you specify Is Not Equal To - The field's value must not be equal to the value you specify
Create a Condition Group.
Add Conditions.
In the case described above, we're saying that the contact must have both a contact tag of Spanish Speaker and their Primary Language must be set to Spanish. We can specify that only one of these conditions must be met for the user to be included in the group by updating the criteria so that anyof the conditions should be met instead of all. This way, if we update one field, but not the other, the user is still being added to our dynamic group.
Add a Contact Type condition.
This generates only contacts that are listed as prospects.
Search Results
Search the results and create the Dynamic Group.
Dynamic Groups - Edit or Save As You have the ability to Edit, Save As, Export, Transfer, and Format Columns for your Dynamic Groups. You can use the Save As feature to use an existing dynamic group as a foundation to build a new one so you don't have to duplicate your efforts.
Creating a Dynamic Group
A dynamic group is a collection of contacts that can be used to build an audience for a deployment of content.
Go to Contacts, and select Search.
Complete the Name field, name the group created.
Complete the Description field.
Select User from the list .
An admin user will see more choices such as specific users from specific companies and organizations.
Select Companies from the list.
An admin user will see more choices such as specific companies and organizations.
You can select multiple Companies or select all the users from all the companies, toggle the Child Companies selection to Yes.
Select a Product from the list.
In this example the product is mortgage, the system brings in the loan fields and information based on the product selected.
You can also select a sales process for that product. For instance, you can possibly sort by sales process funded, or closed.
Here, you can see all the fields that you can use to search in your report.  You can start typing in the Search field and the system will populate the drop down with some suitable suggestions.
For example, choose Contact First name, Last name, Mobile phone, e-mail, and creation date. When you make your selections, you see them in this window to the right. These are the five fields that are going to be in your report.

Contacts
Add a Contact Tag
Contact Tags are unique identifiers that can be added, like labels, in order to further categorize a Contact Record. Tagging lets you easily sort, filter, segment, and target contacts with campaigns designed around their specific interests and actions. Contacts can have an unlimited number of Tags.
Tags are great for small reminders or labels you want to associate with a Contact so that you don't have to create Custom Fields for every single variable that you want to track.
Examples:
Your contact Linda is a CPA. She is also a huge football fan. You might add a Tag for each of these attributes (e.g. Financial, and Football Fan). This will make it easy when you have reason to distribute marketing materials to all of your Contacts who are football fans, or who are in finance, or both.
Tracking Contacts who attend one of your hosted seminars. Rather than create a new Checkbox Custom Field for each new seminar in order to track attendance, you could simply create a Tag for each seminar and apply it to the attendee Contact.
John Doe attends many of your company's seminars and events. So his Contact Record would have Tags attached, one each for Fall 2024 Lunch & Learn, Mac OSX Training, and Selling with Pinterest Seminar.
Tags are displayed on the Overview tab of a Contact Record. That's also where you can add a Tag by clicking on the Add a Tag link.
Like and Dislike Tags
Tags can be classified as either Like, green or Dislike, red. Use this classification to help you visualize and remember which tags have positive and negative connotations.
Tags can be used to categorize just about any object in Surefire.
Review Manage Tags for additional information.

Contacts
Contacts Add a Note
Notes are how you record important information about a Contact or interactions with a Contact (e.g. a customer's product preference).
When a Note is in reference to a Contact interaction, like a conversation or an email exchange, you can click the Contacted Person checkbox to record that the Note indicates an actual correspondence.
Notes are managed on the Notes tab of the Contacts Details Panel.
You can use the Notes for most recent drop-down to specify whether you want to see a Contact's notes from just the last week, or from the last month or last year, or for all time.
You can use the Search field to locate notes by a keyword or term.
You can also select the Show Related checkbox to display any Notes included in Surefire Contact Records for any contacts related to this contact, such as a spouse, or any contacts listed as Secondary Owners or Tertiary Owners contacts on any deal with this contact.
If the Contacted person checkbox is checked the badge displays on the note.
If you check the Show Related checkbox the badge in the note.
Enter a new note by typing into the Note field and then clicking the Add Note button.
The Notes tab is where you can see the notes' contents. This differs from the Activity History tab where you will only see a record of a note being Added.

Contacts
Rate a Contact
Contacts can be Rated by Surefire, on a scale of Zero to Five Stars based on data collected from returned Forms, such as surveys, that have had the Rating element incorporated into them.
Forms can be accessed from Marketing, Forms and clicking on an existing or create a new Form you will see an option on the right for Rating.
For example, a Rate your experience with us survey Form might be designed to prompt recipients to rate a Surefire Contact or User. All of the rating responses received from this survey would then be averaged by Surefire and applied to that Contact or User.
You can find a Contact's Star Rating on the Overview tab of their Contact Record.

Contacts
Contacts View Text Message Archive
Go to Contacts, View All Contacts.
Search for the contact and select their name in the Contacts List panel.
Click the Text Message Archive tab in the Contacts Details panel.
You can view a sortable interactive table listing the history of all Text Messages sent to the Contact from Surefire.
You can limit the contents of the table to Texts from just Today, through this Week, Month or Year, all the way to All Time.
Each Text Message sent has the following details in the table: Time - displays when the Text Message was sent User - displays the user the Text Message was sent from Text Message Number - displays from which phone number the Text Message was sent. Contact Number - displays to which phone number the Text Message was sent. Direction - displays the Direction: either Outbound (sent FROM Surefire ) or Inbound (sent TO Surefire ) Message - content of the Text Message

Contacts
View and Manage Contacts Activities
Go to Contacts, View All Contacts.
Search for the contact you want to view.
Go to the Activities tab in the Contacts Details Panel.
You can view and manage which, Deployments, Rules, and Workflows are assigned to a Contact. From here you can also see a History of any actions that have been executed for the contact as part of a Surefire Rule or Workflow.
Add to Workflow Use to add this Contact to one of your Surefire Workflows and additionally, to select on what date you want to add them.
Current Rules/Workflows
This sortable and interactive table lists all of the Surefire Rules and Workflows the Contact has been added to.
Select the Name to be taken to that Workflow Detail Page.
Select to Remove this contact from a Rule/Workflow.
Activities
A sortable table lists all actions or Activities executed for this Contact by any Rule/Workflows they have been added to. You can filter the table by Activity type.
For each activity, the following details are shown as a row in the table: Status - each activity shows as Completed, Upcoming, Paused or Skipped. you can hover over Completed to see the date and time the activity was completed. you can hover Skipped to see an explanation for why the activity was not completed. Upcoming activities are scheduled future events. You can, as needed, Pause, Resume and Cancel individual deployments specifically associated with upcoming rule/workflow activities. For these Rule/Workflow activities, click on the upcoming status to select Pause or Cancel from the list.
Pause
– This will stop your deployment to this contact from being sent. You may choose to resume the deployment at any time prior to the scheduled send date. Prior to the send date, you will be given the option to Resume. If the send date of a paused activity passes without being resumed, the activity will be show as Skipped.
Cancel
– cancels your deployment to this contact from being sent. This activity will be removed from the contact activities and will not be able to be recovered. Resume - To resume a paused activity, just click on the Paused status for the dropdown options to Resume or Cancel.
If a rule/workflow associated with the deployment is paused, the deployment will not be sent even if resumed for the individual contact.
For Print deployments, the ability to pause or cancel will be determined by lead time and whether it has started processing. If the minimum lead time has been met, when you hover over the Upcoming status you will get the following message –
Your print item is being processed. This item can no longer be modified.
If the minimum lead time for processing of a paused print deployment has passed, the deployment will not be able to be resumed and will be marked “skipped.” Scheduled Date - the date and time the activity was scheduled for by the Workflow. Activity - the Activity type is indicated by a colored icon and a description, which in the case of deployments includes the Collection name. Activity types include:
Add a Tag Add a Task such as a To-Do or Phone Call
Add Contact to Workflow
Deploy Content
Update Contact Type/Lifecycle Status
Update Lead Score
Source
The name of the Surefire source that executed this activity. Click on the link to be taken to the original source; Rule, Workflow or, Deployment.
Event Timing
Displays the date and time that the activity occurred.

Contacts
View a Contact Activity History
A Contact's Activity History is a summary of system actions executed in Surefire for that contact. It includes both automated system activity (generated by Workflows) as well as actions that were manually executed by users.
Activity History shows when an action was executed and by whom. It does not, however, generally show further details about those actions.
Go to Contacts Details Panel, History tab.
Select History.
Choose either Type or Sort. in Type select the activity type you want to view a history of:
Types Check all - displays history for all activity types is shown. Deals - identifies when and by whom a Deal for this Contact was created, modified, closed etc. Lifecycle Changes - shows when and by whom the Lifecycle for this Contact was altered, and what to. Notes - shows when and by whom a Note was added for this Contact. Modified - shows when and by whom this Contact record was modified. Added To Workflow - shows what Workflow(s) this Contact was added to and when. Lead Score Changes - shows when this Contact's Lead Score was changed, and from what previous value to what new value. Tags - If a Tag was added/removed the name of the tag, who added it, and when will display. Contact Duplicate Updated - if the Duplication Check engine has removed a duplicate of this Contact's Contact Record in Surefire, details of that action are shown. Deal Duplicate Updated - If the Duplication Check engine has removed a duplicate Deal associated with this Contact, details of that action are shown.
Removed Contact Sent via Webhook - Shows when a contact has been sent via the Webhook Integration. in Sort order either Newest or Oldest first

Contacts Referral Tracker
Contacts Referral Tracker Surefire gives you a way either as an individual user or as a company to see a consolidated listing of the top referral partners and top transactional partners it works with.

Additional filtering options for Top Transaction Partners can be added.
Top Referrers
The results show a listing including Rank, Name, Contact Type and the number of Referred Contacts. All Referral Partner names have a link that shows a list of all referred contacts, including name, user, date and time added to the system, and the contact type of the referral.

Contacts
Transfer Contacts
At times a Surefire admin will encounter a scenario that requires them to transfer contacts. A User may leave the company, leaving behind company-generated contacts that need new owner(s).
A User's contacts may be transferred to a 'dormant' account when they leave the company for compliance purposes, and so forth. **Please note that if you use an Integrated LOS, you will need to point those contacts to the new owner otherwise, the contacts will sync and create duplicates, this is only in the case of a dormant user.
Transferring ownership is useful for active lead management. You may want to transfer a call in lead to your VA or Reverse specialist.
Transfer/Assign Owner for up to 100 Contacts
Go to Contacts, View All Contacts,
Search and select the Contacts you want to transfer.
Select Assign Owner.
Select the new owner as the contact.
Select Assign.
When the assignment is complete: the new owner of the assignment is notified in Surefire the new owner receives an email notification the transfer is logged in the contact record
You can also view all contacts and sort by assigned date in My Views:
Currently, contact assignment does not trigger the rules engine, however, marketing workflows that the contact is enrolled in will continue to work with the new contact owners' information in the footer if applicable. So for example these leads could be nurtured in a brand account and then once they are transferred to a loan officer the workflow just continues on unless changed.
The contact assignment date field is not available in advanced search, the best way to look at and see this information in a report style is in My Views.
Assigned contacts do not trigger your company's de-duplication policy, a best practice would be to assign and then use the dedupe tool to manually merge together.
Transfer More than 100 Contacts at Once
Create a Dynamic Advanced Search Group with the set criteria to capture the contacts you wish to transfer.
Examples of criteria that might include
Contact Owner IS John Smith and/or Contact Type IS Zillow Lead.
Click on the group name.
Select.
Select Transfer.
Select a user as the new owner from the list.
If you want the Dynamic Search used to transfer the contacts moved as well leave the Move this search group to above user transfer is complete box checked.
Enter an email in Add additional email field if you want to notify yourself or someone else of this transfer.
Select Add.
In the Confirm section read and check all boxes.
Select Save.
View the completed job in the Contacts, Search under Transfer Jobs. If there are thousands of contacts this could take a few minutes to complete.

Contacts
Contacts - One to One Emails
One to One Email is a feature that turns on a user to send a quick email to a contact directly from their database without leaving the system or having to create a new collection. While viewing a contact record, a user can click the contact email address, and an email window will appear in Surefire. The email can be sent directly to the contact, and a record of the activity will be captured within the system. This record tracking feature helps users maintain contact history and communication notes and is also beneficial from a corporate compliance standpoint.
Turn on One to One Emails
One to One Email is a permission granted feature. An Admin must turn on appropriate user permission for the desired role.
Go to CRM Settings, Roles/Permissions.
In the Marketing section select One to One Email .
Access One to One Emails
You can access one to one emails either from an individual contact record or from My views, or click on a contact email address to activate the email window.
Once the email window is generated, you can write the email and send. The ability to CC is available, along with the typical email toolbar. However, merge fields and graphics are not available in this feature, neither is the ability to co-brand.
One to One email always uses the default company email layout, including licensing information, company address, and a link to opt-out of communications.
If a contact has opted out partially or completely, One to One Email will not be available for that contact email address.
One to One Email can also be accessed by clicking on the Deployment icon from in a contact record. If a user clicks this icon, they will be given the option to choose to send a One to One Email or to Deploy with Content.
Choosing the One to One option will bring up the email window. Choosing the Deploy with Content option will take the user to the Deployment Center.
Track One on One Emails
One to One Emails are tracked in Surefire. Email communications can be viewed from the contact record under the Activities tab. They are also included in the Deployment Center, Audits, and Email Event Performance Reporting. If a user’s notification center is allowed, records of One to One Emails also appear in email/in-app notifications and daily/monthly summary notifications.
The One to One Email feature is intended for specific, timely and direct communication to an individual contact. As such, this feature is not subject to the Approval Manager.

Contacts
Contact Lifecycles
All Contacts in Surefire are required to have a Contact Type. This supports reporting and marketing and allows you to assign a Lifecycle to each Contact Type.
Lifecycle Phases
A Lifecycle is a series of Phases, or Stages, that move a Contact through a pre-set path as determined by your business.
For instance, you could have a Contact Type for Partner and in your relationships with Partners, you could breakout the progression of Phases in the following sequence:
Not Met Yet
Virtual Introduction
Met in Person
First Deal
Multiple Deals
Trusted Partner
This Life cycle would take your contact from the Phase of Not Met Yet all the way through to having done Multiple Deals until finally they achieve the desired goal of Trusted Partner.
Create a Lifecycle
While Creating a Contact Type, select the option to Edit Lifecycle Phases.
Select Add a New Phase.
You can select multiple lifecycle phases.
Drag the phase blocks to re-order them.
It is not required to have a Lifecycle for a Contact Type, you can leave it empty or add one at a later date.
Lead Lifecycle
Leads, the only system default Contact Type, have a slightly different concept behind their Lifecycle. You should always consider the final Phase of a Lead Lifecycle to essentially be the first step in your Sales Process.
This is because at this Phase you are Converting a Lead into another Contact Type and moving them deeper into your Sales Process.
For instance, if you are a loan officer, the final Phase of a Lead would be some indicator that the Contact is now more serious about getting a home loan. Perhaps Sent Application or Prequalify Loan Amount is your final Phase before you Convert the Lead. This will be the first stage at the top of your Deal Pipeline.
Unqualified Reasons
Unlike other types, you can also add Unqualified Reasons. When you are changing the Qualified Status of a Lead to Unqualified, you can then select the appropriate option to indicated why the Lead is Unqualified.

Contacts
Assign a Contact Type
Go to Contacts, View Contacts
In the Contacts List panel, locate contact who's Type you want to change.
Select and click Edit.
Alternatively, select the Contact's Name and then click the Edit on the Contact Details panel.
In the Edit Contact screen, expand the Contact Type list to view the contact type that are available to assign to this contact.
Make a selection.
Click Save.

Contacts
Assign a Lifecycle to Contact Type
When Creating a New Contact Type, you have the option to associate a Contact Lifecycle with it. At any time you can edit a Contact Type to adjust or add a Lifecycle.
Go to Sales Settings, Contact Types.
Click to Create New Contact Type.
Alternatively, select the desired Contact Type and select Edit.
Select Add New Phase to add Phases to the Lifecycle.
If necessary, drag the phase boxes to organize in desired order.
Select Save.

Contacts
Change Lifecycle Status
You can use these lifecycles to trigger rules and automation based on lifecycles achieved. This Lifecycle Feature helps you in robust lead management and makes Surefire a vital tool in this area of CRM / Marketing automation. This can be done by creating custom fields.
Here is an example of a lead lifecycle:
While not all leads are the same, some leads are more engaged than others, some leads come from mailing lists that are considered cold. Loan Officers can time block/segment their day based on follow-up activities for these given lifecycles.
For example, I call my cold lead list every day at 3pm. I call my pre-qualified leads every Tuesday. These lifecycle segments are managed inside of My Views.
Update a Lifecycle
Review the Change Lifecycle Status video.
Select on the edit icon in the record you want to update.
When you click on the Contact Record, the Lifecycle Status is prominently displayed letting you know at a glance what state the contact is in.
Select a status to change the lifecycle.
Select Yes, I’m Sure to confirm the change.

Contacts
Lifecycle and Marketing Automation
As part of contact types, lifecycles help you sub-segment your contacts to an even more granular level, allowing for greater personalization and engagement.
Here are a few examples of how you might use Lifecycles in your business:
Engage cold or new leads at a quicker pace.
Take recruits through a cycle that includes engagement campaigns through contract negotiation to automated welcome packages.
Engage real estate agents at the right pace for the nature of the relationship, i.e. new agents vs. agents who you have done several deals with.
To make automation happen when a lifecycle is added or updated:
Go to the Rules Engine.
Select Edit.
Review the basic information to input like Name, Library and Description.
Below that, you can see where you can use the Rules Engine to trigger rules and automation when a certain lifecycle status has been achieved.
You can set the status to trigger actions, and which actions you want to occur.
Now you can see that when a Contact Lifecycle is achieved, and certain conditions that you determine are met, and the lifecycle is in a certain status, you can trigger certain actions.
Example, here you can enter a contact on a workflow of your choosing.
Select Add Action, you can see there are many other actions you can add.
In the Choose Criteria field, you can add different criteria that you want to serve as triggers to initiate actions.
Some of the actions you can take include Assign a Contact to User, Update Contact Type/Life Cycle Status, Deploy Content etc.
In essence, this automation functionality allows you to automate actions to be taken when a certain Lifecycle Status is achieved. In this way, the lead status can be used to start or stop actions in a workflow from taking place.

Contacts Email Exclusivity
For various reasons, a contact may exist in multiple user accounts within the same company. It may not be best practice to have many different users from the same company sending duplicate emails to the same contact. Surefire allows companies to designate which user will have exclusive rights to email communications with a particular contact. This ensures contacts will receive emails from only one user within the company.
Master Settings
Only admins can set up email exclusivity for a company.
Go to Master Settings, Email.
Scroll to the Email Exclusivity section.
Turn on email exclusivity using the toggle switch.
Set the parameters for the contact types to be included.
Available Contact types will reflect what is set up within your own organization.
You can also set exceptions within a contact type using the Exclude Opt Out Lists. This allows further refinement to what is allowed to be sent and to whom. For the example in the image above, email exclusivity is set for Referral Partner type, meaning emails can only be sent to any particular referral partner by the user who has email exclusivity to that referral partner contact, unless it is In Process related. If the emails are In Process related, then Surefire will let those go through from any contact owner.
Select Enable Buying Agent Preference for Enabled Contact to award email exclusivity to the most recent buying agent on a transaction.
Select a Product for Buying Agent Preference, should be set to your mortgage product.
Select Buying Agent Field, Buying Agent.
Select an option in Newest deal Based on this Date Field; Application Date, Closing Dates or other dates on file, we recommend either application date or closing date.
Click Save Buying Agent Preference Settings.
Contacts
Once Email Exclusivity is turned on, contacts that are impacted by the exclusivity setup will show either an Exclusive Rights or an Excluded From tag below the contact’s email address.
If exceptions have been made through the Excluded Opt Out Lists in the setup, hovering your mouse over the Exclusive Rights or Excluded From tags will show the specific Email Exclusivity.
Change Exclusivity Rights for a Contact
Initially, Exclusivity rights are automatically set to the contact owner who first showed the contact in their Surefire database. However, an admin can change who has exclusive rights.
Go to Contacts, Dedupe Utility.
Select Email Exclusivity Resolutions.
Filter by contact type and contact email address.
Select Search.
Click on the contact owner you wish to have exclusive rights. The asterick indicates who has email exclusivity for a contact.
Select Set Exclusivity.
Exclusivity Rights Users
You can view a list of all contacts that you have Email Exclusivity rights to:
Go to My Account, My Settings.
Select Email.
Select Email Exclusivity to view all the shared contacts for which they have exclusivity.
If a contact is not found in the Email Exclusivity list, exclusivity may not be turned on for that contact type or another user has email exclusivity rights to that contact.
Check the Contact record for the excluded from tag associated with the email address.

has a Contact Type such as Lead, Prospect or Customer. Each contact type is also associated with a series of stages that a Contact progresses through during your relationship. This process is known as a Lifecycle.
Every new Company in Surefire starts off with only one Contact Type; Leads. All other types must be custom created as every business is different and has its own unique rules and processes.
A Lead is a general Contact. The only information you have is that they may be qualified for your product and have an interest in doing business with you. As you learn more about the Lead you can move them through the Sales Process and convert them into a Deal.
In Surefire, Leads are different from other Contact Types and have a few unique attributes:
Lead Qualification
As every salesperson can tell you, not all Leads are created equal. This is why most sales organizations go through a process of vetting, or qualifying, their Leads to see if they are a fit for that organization's products or services.
Review Qualify a Lead for additional information.
Lead Score
For Leads that are qualified, there is additional stratification. Some leads are more qualified than others and should be prioritized by sales. Surefire allows for this by assigning a numerical Lead Score to all Leads.
Review Lead Score for additional information.
Inbound Form Lead Creation
When a Form is created with the end result to create a Contact in Surefire, this Contact Type is created as a Lead. Surefire assumes that the Form is being used for lead generation purposes.
Review Create a Form for additional information.
View Leads
Leads are also handled differently from other Contacts when you are viewing a list of Contacts in Surefire. Often you will have the ability to differentiate the Contacts you are viewing from Leads and Contacts.
Review View and Filter Contacts for additional information.

Contacts
Leads
Lead Score
A Lead can be assigned a Lead Score. This is a number, ranging between -100 and 100, that indicates how important your Sales Team should consider a Lead. A Lead that you want the Sales Department to prioritize should have a high Lead Score; a Lead you want to de- prioritize should have a low Lead Score.
Update a Lead Score
As a Lead progress through your sales processes, depending on what Workflow they've been added to or which Rules they have triggered, the data input to their Fields can automatically trigger updates to their Lead Score.
For example, a Form on your website might ask potential customers questions like:
Planned Date of Purchase
Loan Amount
FICO Score
Because the answers to these questions provide strong indications of how likely potential customers are to become actual purchasers of your products, administrators can configure Rules to update the Lead Score based on said answers.
For instance, based on the above, Rules could be built with the following Lead Score criteria:
Field
Answer
Score
Planned Date of Purchase
This Month
+20
Planned Date of Purchase
Next Month
+10
Planned Date of Purchase
Next year
-10
Loan Amount
$500,000+
+25
Loan Amount
$350,000-500,000
+10
Loan Amount
$<200,000
-10
FICO Score
800+
+25
FICO Score
700-800
+15
FICO Score
500-600
-15
FICO Score
<500
-25
Therefore, a Lead entering the system who plans to buy a home this month (+20) looking for $400,000 (+10) with an 810 FICO (+25) would have a Lead Score of 55 while someone looking to borrow $250,00 (0) next month (+10) with a 550 FICO (-15) would have a Lead Score of -5.
Lead Score changes triggered by Rules can be in increments (e.g. "Change Lead Score by +5 When [X] Event Happens") or to an absolute value (e.g. "Change Lead Score to 55").
Review Create a Rule for additional information.
Manually Override a Lead Score
You can also manually change a Contact's Lead Score directly from the Contacts Details Panel.
Go to Contact Detail Panel.
Click on the circular Lead Score number.
In the Lead Score, enter a new score.
Select Save.

must have a Product associated with them. This Product represents the actual good or service that is being sold.
In the mortgage world, this could be a 30-year Fixed, 5/1 ARM or Reverse Mortgage. For a B2B SaaS company, this could be a Standard Account, Enterprise Account, Premium Support or Data Storage.
Each of these Products then has its own set of unique fields. While there likely will be some overlap — for instance, every Product that is a loan will have a Loan Amount — there will still be fields relevant to one Product Type that don't apply to another (e.g. the Initial Adjustment Cap applies to an ARM but not a 30-year Fixed.)
Creating a separate Product Types will allow you to better organize and structure your sales and operations within the CRM.

Select Product Name to view its details.
If you have permissions to edit the product, you will see an Edit button in the top right.
To add a new Product, select.

Add a Product Field
One of the key components of Creating a Product is adding Product Fields. Similar to fields in Contact, these are data fields that can be queried and accessed through other parts of Surefire, such as Advanced Search, Forms, or any other CRM section that would need access to this data.
In addition to adding Product Fields when you Create a Product, you can also add Fields to an existing Product.
Go to Sales Settings, Products.

Select Add New Question in either Column 1 or Column 2.
Scroll the bottom.
Select Add New Question.
Label the Question. This is what appears before the empty field in the Product form.
Select which data Type this field will accept in the list.
Select Required if this is a mandatory field. Deals with these Products can not be saved unless this field is completed.
Select Total Field if you want to designate this as a Sum field.
When you view this product in the Pipeline View, you will see a total rolled up for this field in each of the Sales Phases. This allows you to quickly glance at your pipeline and gauge what amount you have in each phase.

Only one field per product can be designated as a Sum Field. The data type for the field must be Currency.

Starring a field indicates that it contains critical product information and will appear on the Deal Cards in your Deal Pipeline view.

If this is a custom product select Primary Date on the Closing Date field. This is important for things like Anniversary Reporting.
Select Save Changes.

Deals
Add a Deal
A Deal represents a sales opportunity with a high probability of closing. In Surefire, it is an object associated with the Contact that you are working on the Deal with.
For instance, if you are a loan officer, a Deal would represent a Home Loan. As such, you will likely have many Contacts that you have done multiple loans with. They therefore could have multiple Deals on their Contact Record.
Deals and Products
Deals are always associated with a Product.Products represent the actual type of Deal you are doing.
Review Create a Product for additional information.
So for home loans, you could have Products for:
30-year Fixed
7/1 ARM
Reverse Mortgage
When you have been working with a Contact for a long time, you could see under their Deals the multiple Deals you have done with them in the past.
Deals and Sales Processes
Deals are also associated withSalesProcesses.
Review Sales Process for additional information.
These are the Phases or Stages that a Deal must progress through before it advances to closing.
Different Products can have different Phases. Alternatively, different Sales Processes can apply to all Products, for instance, a New Purchase versus Refinance. The former likely would have more Phases than the latter, but you could apply either to the same type of Product.
So if you are doing a Deal for a 30-year Fixed refinance, you would choose the 30-year Fixed Product and the Refinance Sales Process. A week later, you might get a deal for a 30-year Fixed new home purchase. You would again use the 30-year Fixed Product, except this time you would apply the New Purchase Sales Process.
Examples of possible Phases in a Sales Process:
Received Application
Underwriting
Processing
Pre-Approval
Approved
Closed
Add a Deal
There are two ways to add a Deal for a Contact:
Contact's Deals Tab
Go to Contacts, View Contacts or View Leads.
Locate the Contact and select their name.
In the Contact Details panel, select Deals tab.
Select a product from the list.
Click Add New Deal.
From Assign Sales Process list select a Sales Process.
Complete product details.
Select Create Deal.
Converting a Lead
Go to Contacts, View Contacts or View Leads.
Locate the Lead Contact and select their name.
In the Contact Details panel, select Convert.
In the Convert Lead screen: assign a Product, select new Contact Type, select a Sales Process (optional)
Select Convert.
A new Deal for your selected product is added to this Contact.

Deals
Primary Deal Slots
This function provide Users and Administrators a way to easily flag a Contact's Deal with a discrete label. An example of this could be something like Most Recent Deal or Primary Home. Unlike Tags, a Primary Deal Slot can only be used once per Deal per Contact.
Review Contacts, Add a Deal and Create a Tag for additional information.
Primary Deal Slots, which can only be configured by users who are Administrators of your company's Top Level Organizational Unit in Surefire, not only help users quickly identify a certain type of Deal when viewing a Contact Record with multiple Deals included on it, but they can also be used in Rules as either a Trigger (i.e. "condition") or Action. Therefore, you can create a Rule or Workflow consisting of a set of criteria that will automatically apply a Primary Deal Slot to a Contact's Deal should that Deal meet said criteria requirements.
Default Primary Deal Slots
The following three Primary Deal Slots are implemented by default:
Primary Investment Deal
Primary Residence Deal
Primary Second Home Deal
Review Set Up Primary Deal Slots for additional information.

Go to Sales Settings, Primary Deals.
A deal slot allows users to indicate which deal, on a contact by contact basis, you are working with for continued CRM actions, such as closing anniversary emails or rate monitor. All the primary slot deals that are out of the box and were loaded when your account was created, are visible in the middle of the screen.
In the Create Slot area complete the following fields: Primary Deal Slot Name - enter a name for the deal slot Product - associate the deal slot with a product
Description Optional - enter a description, not required
Select Create Slot.

Deals
Primary Deal Slots in Rules and Actions
Primary Deal Slots can be incorporated into a Rule as either a Trigger (i.e. condition) or an Action.
Use a Primary Deal Slot as a Rule Condition
In Surefire, for any Rule that is: associated with a Product and where... the trigger type is Deal-associated (i.e. the statement begins with "When a Deal...") then users can... choose "Primary Deal Slot" as a condition and make that condition equal/not equal to any of the Primary Deal Slots that were created for the associated Product.
Update a Primary Deal Slot as a Rule Action
When the conditions of a Rule in Surefire have been met (where the trigger type is Deal-associated), users can choose applying a Primary Deal Slot from among the optional Update Contact Data actions.
You can use Rules and Actions with Primary Deal Slots to create a Loan Anniversary Email
> This is a monitoring rule that display every day in the calendar for loans that have closed on that date.
To Set up a Loan Anniversary Email Rule:
Got to CRM Settings, Custom Rules.
Select Create Rule.
Enter a Name.
Select a Library to save.
Enter a Description.
Select a Product to associate this rule with.
Verify the trigger type is Deal-associated; When a deal.
Select monitored.
When using Monitored Rules, the Lead Time in Days field is generally only used when the rule is applied to print media such as postcards. However, it could be used in the case of an Anniversary Email Rule, for example, if you wanted to assign a task to occur prior to the Loan Anniversary.
Add Product Field - Closing Date as a condition.
Set the value to be between relative month/day, and then set 0 for X-days ago and 0 for X-days from now (since "0," in this context, means the current day's date).
Add a second condition:
Primary Deal Slot is equal to [the Primary Deal Slot that gets applied to Deals whose associated Contact(s) you want Loan Anniversary Emails sent to].
Select the email collection you want to send as the action in then do... section.
Select Save Changes.

Deal Anniversary Rule
This video, provides instructions on using rules and primary deal slots to send deal anniversary emails to your contact database.
This will allow you, for example, to send an anniversary e-mail to your clients on the anniversary of them closing their loan and if a contact has multiple loans, the Primary Deal slots govern which loans closing anniversary we will be using.
Go to Custom Rules.
Review the rules set up. In this example there is a rule for the loan anniversary e-mail for the primary residence deal.
This rule is set up by default when your account is created. Contact your account manager if you can not find it.
Select the rule. You can see how conditions are set up to make it work.
Select Edit.
This is a product specific rule, and that we have Mortgage selected
In the condition section complete the following fields: When select a deal is select monitored and after select all Verify or select Primary Deal Slot In is equal to field select Primary Residence deal
Verify or select Product Field - Closing Date next select between relative month/day select 0
(zero). In X days ago and field select 0
X days from now.
When all the criteria are met, the rule action is to send an e-mail.By default this rule uses the Surefire Public Library Load Anniversary e-mail.
You can either continue to use this e-mail template or click the Edit button to select another content collection from your library that you prefer to use.
You may also want to update the opt out list. But other than those two things, this rule should work just fine for you right out-of-the-box.
This rule is set up to allow your users to subscribe or unsubscribe from it, and the default setting would be all users are unsubscribed. If you want to utilize this rule to market to their database, they'll need to go to their subscriptions and subscribe to it.
Go to Deployment center and select available subscriptions.
As a User, you have the ability to either subscribe or unsubscribe from this rule.
To do this, go to a contact in your database.
One additional condition must be added that Closing Date must be before 364 days ago in order to not send a Loan Anniversary email on the exact Closing Date.

Change Deal Phase
Similar to Contact Lifecycle Phases, every Deal, depending on the nature of the product, will pass through its own series of Sales Process Phases. Each successive Phase represents an incremental step (quantified in percentages) towards the Deal being completed (i.e. Won). The higher the percentage, the more likely a Deal's chance of closing.
Review Contact Lifecycles, and Create a Product for additional information.
There are two different ways you can change a deal's process phase.
Deal's Details Page
Go to a Deal's Details page.
Review View and Edit a Deal for additional information.
On the Sales Phase Process, select Deal Phase you want the deal to be set to.
Confirm the change.
You can also change the deal's Achieved and Expected Closing Dates.
Review Set Closing and Phase Achieved Dates for additional information.
Pipeline View
Display your deal in Pipeline View.
Review View Deal Pipeline for additional information.
Drag the deal card to the new Sales Process Phase column.

Marketing
Mortgage marketing is the process of educating and motivating potential borrowers to use your mortgage services in lieu of your competition. Marketing includes corporate brand management and advertising to individual loan officer activities such as generating referral partner relationships and calling or texting prospective customers. Surefire creates a powerful competitive advantage for loan officers by automating key marketing tasks and follow-up communications with everyone from prospects and clients to referral partners.

Text messaging is a potent marketing and communication tool. Power Messaging provides the ability to text directly from Surefire.
Using Power Messaging you can…
Chat with your contacts
Send one text message
Send many text messages at once (blast)
Send text messages over time (campaign or workflow style, day 1, day 2 and so forth)
Send a picture
Send links and interactives
Auto-respond to form submissions
Auto-respond to leads from 3rd parties such as Zillow
Nurture leads
Send in-process updates to borrowers
Send in-process updates to transaction partners
Solicit reviews
Send post-close communication such as mortgage review reminders, birthday greetings and more!
Review Power Messaging Part 1 and Power Messaging Part 2 videos for additional information.

Marketing
Power Messaging
Acquire a Text Messaging Number
In order to engage your database with Text Marketing or use any other Surefire Telephony features, you must first acquire a Text Messaging Number for use.
Complete the following steps to locate the number:
Go to My Account, My Settings.
Click Telephony/Text Messages tab.
In theMy Text Message Numbers section, click Add New Number.
The Purchase new number screen appears.
Expand Search and select phone number list and select one of the following: Search by area code - enter your preferred 3-digit area code Contains - search for a set of consecutive numbers or letters contained anywhere in the number. e.g. 1776 brings up (631) 776-4538 and (929) 296-1776 and LOAN (760) 49L-OAN0 and (424) 353-LOAN Starts with - helps you find a number that begins with specific letters or numbers. When searching please take note that the search will start with the area code. So if you are in the 353 area code and want your number to start with LOAN you should search for 353LOAN, not just LOAN Ends with - helps you find a number that ends with specific letters or numbers. To search for number that ends in 1776 and LOAN it would only return (929) 296-1776 and (424) 353-LOAN, respectively.
Your search only returns a limited amount of numbers at a time. If you don't see a number you like, click More to refresh the search to bring up more results based on availability.
Click Search.
Click Select.
Complete the following fields on the Purchase new number screen:
Name
* - If you have multiple numbers, give each number a unique Name for better organization. Text Message Priority - If you have more than one number, this Priority ranking determines the order the system will send texts in the event that your chosen number exceeds the monthly allowance of text messages. Forward to My Cell - Select Yes, for any direct responses to a Text Message initiated from your Text Number you can choose to have them forwarded to either the Mobile Number or Private Mobile Number designated in your User Profile.
Private Mobile numbers set in this field are not visible to customers. Incoming Call Options - Select which phone option on file you want inbound calls to ring. Outbound Call Options - turn on or off the ability for outbound call usage.
Click Buy Number.
Currently there is no charge for buying a number (subject to change).
Port an Existing Number from Another Service
If you already have a text message number that you would like to utilize within Surefire, you can have that number ported into Surefire. To get the porting process started, please email Surefire support@ice.com. This process may take up to four weeks for completion.
When a number is ported from another service into Surefire, the previous service no longer has access to the number, and the number will only able to be used in Surefire.
Therefore, it is not recommended to port an existing cellular number, as this would cause the number to no longer be available on your mobile device through another carrier. It is recommended to only port numbers from an existing service you plan to discard during your transition to Surefire for text messaging.

Marketing
Power Messaging
Text Messaging in Master Settings
If you have purchased any Text Messaging Numbers for use, you can manage their settings from the Text Messages tab under CRM Settings, Master Settings.
The screen is divided into several sections:
Allow Text Messages to be sent to Text Message Subscriptions
Text Message Opt-Out Frequency Control
Zapier - Assume Text Message Opt-In (trusted source)
Allow Text Messages to Be Sent To As a way to limit the potential ramifications of unsolicited marketing by text, some organizations may want to limit which phone numbers Surefire users are able to send text messages. Surefire provides the following options: All contacts not unsubscribed - This selection will allow Surefire users to send text messages to all contacts except those that have opted out by replying STOP to a text received from Surefire.
Only contacts who have opted in - This selection will allow Surefire users to send text messages only to contacts who have opted in to receive text messages via one of the three possible ways outlined below.
Ways to Opt-In
Form Opt-In
– Surefire has created the option to add the field for Text Message Opt-In to any custom form created by an organization. This field option provides the organization with the ability to capture Contact Opt-In’s with any form submission. This option is the only native way for the Surefire system to capture and monitor contacts that have opted into receiving text messages.
Data Import
– An Organization can create an import map in Data Management that is unique to contact opt-ins.
Standard dedupe protocols should be considered so as not to create duplicates should the list include existing contacts.
Zapier
– An organization can set up a Zap that will assume text message opt-in for all contact mobile phone numbers added or edited in this manner based on specified conditions. Those users and conditions that are set up using this method will be listed in the Zapier – Assume Text Message Opt-in (trusted source) section.
Text Message Opt-Out Frequency Control
This section allows your organization to choose a standard Opt-Out layout/footer to be used for all text messages. In addition, the frequency for how often the Opt-Out layout/footer will appear for text messages can be set. This frequency control is intended to eliminate the Opt-Out language appearing with every single outbound message. This can be especially useful if you text a particular contact frequently.
To set the frequency, select the number of days between appearances of the Opt-Out layout in any text message. The Opt-Out layout will appear in the first message sent and then not appear again until at least the selected number of days has elapsed. For example, if 10 days is selected, the first text message will contain the Opt-Out layout. Then, that layout will not appear again until at least the 11th day from the initial message, no matter the number of messages sent to that contact in the intervening timeframe.
Text Message Subscriptions
This section provides a cumulative total of contacts who have actively opted in or opted out using one of the above-described methods.
Once populated, the quantity number can be clicked on and opened to view a table showing the username, contact name, mobile phone number, and date/time added to the list.

Power Messaging
Create a Text Message for Content Collection
When you create a Content Collection, the first Media Type that it defaults to is Email. If you want to add a Text Media Type, click the + Add New Media Type tab next to Email and select Text Message.
Prior to using Deploy a Text Message, you must have a Text Messaging Number in your User Profile.
Setup
The following are part of the basic setup for all Media Types in a Content Collection and are managed in the left column.
Name
Description
Tags & Use Tags
Save & Delete
Layout
While a Layout is not required for Text Media, you can still apply one if you want to append a fixed Footer to your Text. Select the applicable Layout from the dropdown and you can see a preview in the Message Footer section.
Merge Fields
You can merge database fields into your Text Message by choosing the Merge Fields dropdown and either selecting the desired field from the list or typing the name of the field to filter/search.
Once you choose the Merge Field from the list, the merge shortcode is automatically inserted into your message.
You can merge fields from the following objects: Contact - The Contact who is receiving the Text Message User - The User who is sending the Text Message
Note: This is the User sending the Text Message, not the Owner of the Contact. So in a situation where a Rule or Workflow is triggering a Text Message that is sent from a Team Member, the Team Member's information would merge into the Text Message. Organization - The Company of the User who is sending the Text Message
The fields will then be dynamically generated whenever a Text Message is deployed based on who is sending (User) and who is receiving (Contact or User).
Message
Type the content of your Text Message in Message. As there are character limits to Text Messages before they are broken into two messages, there is a limit of 1600 plain text characters to include in your entire message.
This includes any characters in the Footer as part of your Layout. (Merge Fields are an estimated average of seven characters)
If you exceed the 1600 character limit, you cannot Save your Text Message Media.
You can see a counter of the Estimated Text Count at the bottom.
Insert an Image
In the next section, you can add an image from your Media Collection.
If you are using a Toll-Free Text Message Number you will not be able to send images via Text.
Preview
You can Preview a sample of the Text Message to see what it looks like.
Select Save Media to save the latest version of your Text Message.
Select Preview.

The contact account must include a mobile phone number

Power Messaging
Create a Text Message Layout
Use Text Message Layouts to create a footer that you can add to the end of any Text Message Content Collections that you create.
Unlike Email, Text Message Content created in Surefire does not require a Layout; however, it can be helpful if you want to include opt-out language such as:
Reply with STOP to unsubscribe
Or similar prompts that will allow Contacts to unsubscribe from Text marketing.
The Text Message system used by Surefire will recognize a response of STOP as an unsubscribe and add the phone number to an Opt-Out List so they no longer receive Text messages in the future.
Creating a Text Message Layout is done from the Media Library:
Go to Marketing, Media Library.
Select + Create.
Select New Layout.
In the Layout Type list select Text Message.
Enter a Layout Name and Description.
Select the folder to save it to in the Media Library.
You can set the Layout as Company Default.
Enter in the Footer text you want to include.
It is best if the Footer text is under 75 characters.
Select Save Text Message Layout.
Enter a Text Message Footer
The Text Message footer is automatically appended immediately after the Text Content Collection text ends.
There is an option to include Merge Fields. Find the field you want in the Merge Field dropdown by scrolling or typing a search term. When you select the field, it will insert in your Footer where the cursor is.
Because you are limited to the number of characters you can include in a text message before it splits into two separate messages, it is advised to keep the length of your Footer to under 75 characters.
There is a counter that will automatically calculate the number of characters for the footer. If you include Merge Fields, the counter will estimate each field at 7 characters.
Set as Company Default
By toggling Yes for the Set as Company Default option, you set the Text Message Layout as the standard Default for your Company. This automatically applies the Layout to any Text Message Content created by your Company.
If Users have the appropriate Permissions, they can edit and change to another Layout Option.
Use Tags
After you have saved your layout, you have the option to add Use Tags to it. This helps you limit which Users can and cannot access the Layout.
To add or edit Use Tags, click on the Use Tags box to bring up the Use Tags Editor. This will display existing Use Tags as well as let you add more or remove existing.
Opt-Out Commands Surefire currently supports the following Text Message opt-out commands:
STOP
UNSUBSCRIBE
REMOVE ME
If you prompt recipients to respond with any of these commands, they will automatically be added to your Text Message Opt-Out List. No further Text Messages from your Surefire marketing Deployments are sent to them.
You can review your Text Message Subscription Lists, including how many opt-outs you have, by going to My Account, My Settings and viewing the Telephony/Text Messages tab.

Marketing
Power Messaging
In-App Text Message to Multiple Contacts
You have the ability to select multiple contacts in their database and send a single text message to all of them at one time. This message will appear to each contact as an individual text message sent only to them, and the recipient can reply to the user directly. Any resulting back and forth text messaging will be one-to-one.
Initiate Text Message
From any of the Surefire contact views, you are able to select the contacts you want to include in your text message blast by clicking the box to the left of the contact name. Once at least one box is marked, a text message icon appears at the top of the column.
After all your selections have been marked, select choose the number you want to use for texting and then select Text Message.
A text box generates allowing you to create your text message and send. The names of the contacts who will receive your text message are all shown at the top of the text box. Only contacts with a valid phone number appear in the text box.
Once sent, any contacts that are on the Do Not Call List or who have opted out will not be text messaged. A list of names displays with explanation in a pop-up indicating Message not delivered to.
Reporting Contact Database - All text messaging initiated from a multiple contact text message blast will still report in each individual contact's archive and Last Activity panel on the contact's overview tab. Marketing, Archive - Text messages will show for each contact separately in the archive table. Notifications - If the user is utilizing email notifications for text messages, notifications will be received as expected.

Marketing
Power Messaging
Phone Number Reassignment
To ensure that no ongoing text communications with clients get dropped when the associate user is deactivated in Surefire Admins can reassign any purchased telephony/text messaging numbers from a deactivated account to an active user. The newly assigned user can follow up and respond to any incoming messages and ensure no potential client is lost.
Deactivate a User Account
When an Admin turns off or deletes a user account that contains a telephony/text message number(s), a workflow is be presented with the options to reassign phone numbers or delete phone numbers.
Reassign Phone Numbers
– Choose this option for a work flow that allows the Admin to choose an existing, active user either by typing in their name or utilizing the list option. Once a new user is selected, complete by clicking Reassign.
Delete Phone Numbers
– Choose this option for a work flow that allows the Admin to confirm the decision to permanently remove this number.
If no choice is made at this time, the numbers will move to Master settings, Telephony,
Unassigned User Numbers.
When multiple users are deactivated in bulk, no work flow displays and all associated user telephony numbers will automatically move to the Unassigned User Numbers section in the Telephony tab in Master Settings. Reassignment and/or deletion will need to be done from this area.
Unassigned User Numbers
Admins can manage any unassigned user numbers from the Telephony tab in Master Settings.
This section shows all numbers, previous user, and an expiration date for each number. Each number is available for reassignment for up to 10 days from user deactivation before expiring and automatically deleting from the system. You can select on the applicable line item to either reassign or delete the number.
Notification Center
You can get notified either daily or weekly via email of any unassigned user numbers. In the notification center and select the appropriate boxes to receive notification.

Marketing
Image Specifications
The following image specifications are recommended based on the asset:
Emails
Images, generally, should be no bigger than 600 px wide. There is no limit on length. dpi isn’t a concern (outside of print)
Images can only be png/gif/jpg/jpeg format
Text Messages
Images can be of any size, however, once sent via Text, the image will auto adjust to a max height and width of 300 x 300 respectively.
Images can only be png/gif/jpg/jpeg format
Flyers
Print – 300 dpi (8 mg limit)
Mobile – 600 px wide. There is no limit on height.
Social – Landscape is 1200 px X 628 px, Square is 1080 px X 1080 px
Images can be jpg/jpeg/gif/png/bmp or imported psd
Logo - set by system
Company Logo – max width is 1305 px and max height is 390 px
Secondary Logo – max width is 480 px and max height is 270 px
User logo – max width is 300 px and max height is 250 px
Postcards
File size will support roughly 300 dpi
Image size – 2700 px X 1800 px (9x6 inches), this includes a 1/8” bleed on all sides
Only JPEG file type with CMYK color space
Social Posts
1200 px X 628 px for link image -- minimum 560 x 292
Signatures
User Photo, User Headshots: 375 px X 450 px (1.25x1.5 inches), 300 dpi Smaller resolution images will trigger this image may be unsuitable for print warning message. This message is just a warning, smaller images may be used but keep in mind they may not appear crisp on postcards if a smaller image is chosen.
Landing Pages
Images should be re-sized responsively, so no set guidelines on size. Don’t upload a much larger picture than needed to prevent slow downloads.
Background image – normally 1500 to 2000 px wide
Flyers
Flyer templates are designed to be completely customizable. Therefore, there is no specific size the original artwork needs to be because it can be adjusted to fit the space available. If an image is adjusted proportionally (not stretched or shrunk abnormally either lengthwise or widthwise) then for Print it will generally fill the top 7.5 inches of the Flyer, leaving a 3.5-inch rectangular section at the bottom for the signature block (see the below image.) Given the variation in customer signature blocks, however, it is recommended that the signature block be designed first to determine the necessary space needed and then to build your flyer content image block based on the remaining available space.
The Surefire Content team produces all Public Flyers with the pixel size of 1800 W x 1534 H. This produces a Flyer with content image blocks approximately 8.5” W x 7.5” H, leaving all Public Flyers with a 3.5” H for a signature block.
For Print, the image should be 300 dpi for quality and no larger than 8 mg.
For Mobile, the image will be 600 px wide by unlimited height.
For Social sharing, the image will be 900 px wide by 450 px height. Note: social platforms change often, but these measurements are current.
Custom images can be JPEG/JPG/GIF/PNG/BMP format.
Landing Pages
The Multi Column Design Landing Page has a set default background image for the Headline area.
This background image, though, can be changed to suit your needs through the following steps.
Select Page Style
Icon in the left side vertical black box
Select Inline CSS Editor.
Scroll to line 25, background-image.
Replace the asset image URL located between the parenthesis (---) with the desired asset image URL Click Apply.
Detail of Page Style CSS code:
The Responsive Web Design used to build this Multi Column Design Landing Page, adjusts the image in the background based on the viewer’s device and screen size. See below for examples on how the view of the chosen image given the device.

Crop an Image
You can crop an Image while you are Uploading it or after by Editing it. While you have the Crop Window open, there are several ways in which you can work with your Image: Drag Corners/Centers - You can zoom in on an area of the Image by dragging the corners inward to reduce the size of the image. Conversely, you can drag the corners outward to increase the size of your Image. Move Crop Rectangle - If you click and hold the crop rectangle you an move the rectangle around the canvas area to adjust the crop area on the Image Zoom In - Click the Zoom In button to maintain the height & width of your crop rectangle while zooming in on your image Zoom Out - Conversely, click the Zoom Out button to maintain the height & width of your crop rectangle while zooming out on your image. This effectively shrinks the size of the actual image while keeping the canvas size of the cropped area the sam Reset - If it all gets a bit out of hand and you're not happy with your cropping, just hit the Reset button to bring everything back to its original state

Hover over the Image.
Select Edit button.
Select Crop Image button.
Crop as applicable.
Select Save Image.

Select Copy Image Address.
Paste this into your browser address bar.
This takes you to the actual Image file itself. You can then use this image URL anywhere.

You can access the Single Property Sites in Marketing, Single Property Sites.

You can filter by the following fields:
Town
Zipcode
Price Minimum
Price Maximum Date - This is the Date the Property was created in Single Property Sites
Status -
Select a listing status of Active, Inactive, Sold, In Contract or Off-Market. A listing defaults to Active.
Select View All to revert to an unfiltered view.
Sort the Master Property List Table
You can sort by Master Property List table by column type (i.e. Agent, Listing Info, Created By, Created Date or Status) in alphabetically ascending or descending order. Do so by clicking on the column heading once or twice respectively.

You can manage each Single Property Site in the table by clicking on the following action Icons located on the far right of the listing's row:
Status
Use the drop-down menu to change the listing's status
Choose Active, Inactive, Sold, In Contract or Off-Market

Copy Link - Select to copy the link for the completed Property Listing site to your computer's clipboard. Delete - Select to delete the Single Property Site. Deletions are permanent; they cannot be undone. PDF - Select to download a custom PDF flyer of the property. View and Manage Single Property Sites (SPS)
Adjust Program Rates By State
For nationwide lenders (or even those who operate in multiple states) that use regional pricing, you can make state-level adjustments for Loans Programs on a state-by-state and program-by-program basis.
From the Single Property Site main page, selec Program Settings to be taken to the Program Setup page. From there, you can click the State Adj. button next to a Loan Program to make upwards or downwards adjustments to the Program Rate.
The adjustment that you enter will be a relative amount (e.g. 0.05 or -0.10) so that whenever the Base Program Rate is changed the State Adjusted Rate will also fluctuate its set adjusted amount.
For example, if you have the Base Program Rate of 3.500% for 30-year Fixed and California has a 0.15 positive adjustment and Florida has a -0.05 negative adjustment, their rates would be 3.650% and 3.450%, respectively.
If the base rate changes to 3.750%, then California will adjust to 3.900% and Florida will adjust to 3.700%.
Loading Adjustments
If you are setting up your Loan Programs and tend to use the same adjustments per state regardless of Loan Type, you can easily load previously set Loan Program adjustments by selecting them from the dropdown and clicking Go.
Download Adjustments
You can also choose to download a .csv file of your collection of state adjustments by clicking the Download File button on a Loan Program State Adjustment window.
This allows you to manage the rates offline in an Excel spreadsheet. When you need to update the rates, you can easily copy and paste the rates you have updates offline into the appropriate state.

Marketing
View and Manage Single Property Sites (SPS)
APR Calculations in SPS APR Calculations in SPS A loan’s Annual Percentage Rate (APR) is calculated based on the values from the original created program and property data, many of these values are used to calculate the APR. The APR reflects the true yearly cost of borrowing, including interest and fees, expressed as a percentage.
Loan Comparison Calculator
On the SPS potential customers can adjust multiple fields to obtain the APR.
Adjusting the Purchase Price ($) and/or the Down Payment fields changes the loan amount. It subtracts the fees from the loan amount to get the net amount received:
Net loan amount= $201,400−$4,000=$197,400
Use the monthly payment - the Monthly Payment is $1,207/month based on the full $201,400 loan.
The APR is calculated based on the interest rate that makes the present value of all payments equal to $201,400 (the actual amount received). This is done using the Internal Rate of Return (IRR) formula.
Example of a manual APR calculation using a simplified example. Loan amount: $201,400 Interest rate: 6% (fixed) Loan term: 30 years Upfront fees: $4,000 (e.g., origination, underwriting, etc.) Monthly payment (principal + interest): $1,207 (based on standard amortization)
Field or Function and Description
Field/Function
Description
APR
Calculated based on values from the Program's Terms in Months, First Loan Payment, Total Loan Amount, and Cost for APR.
Prepaid Interest
Calculated based on the Base Loan Amount, the Program's Rate, and the Prepaid Interest Days field.
Cost For APR
Calculated value based on the calculated values the Closing Cost, Cost of Monthly MI PMI, and Prepaid Interest. Each of the values are added together to produce the Cost for APR.
Terms in Months
Taken directly from the Program, no calculations are made.
First Loan Payment
Calculated value based on the Program's Rate, Terms in Months, and Total Loan Amount entered in the payment (pmt) function in the SPS application.
Base Loan Amount
Using the Property Sales Price, it is calculated based on the Loan to Value (100% minus the Down Payment %) and entered as a percent function.
MI/PMI Amount
This field is calculated based on the values for Base Loan Amount and the Program's MI/PMI value.
Cost of Monthly MI PMI
Calculated based on the MI/PMI Amount multiplied by the Continuance in Months data.
First Loan Average Estimated Costs
Calculated based on the selected option for the field.
If $ is selected, the field is the value entered into the First Loan Average field.
Otherwise, it is calculated based on the Total Loan Amount and First Loan Average field as the rate.
Other Amount Total
Calculated based on the selected option for the field.
If $ is selected, the field is the value entered into the First Loan Average field.
Otherwise, it is calculated based on the Total Loan Amount and Other Rate field as the rate.
Point Rate
Calculated based on the Base Loan Amount for the Program's Loan Amount and the Program's Point Rate, uses the calculation function calc_discount_rate.
Lender Credit Amount
Calculated based on the selected option for the field.
If $ is selected, the field is the value entered into the First Loan Average field.
Otherwise, it is calculated based on the Total Loan Amount and Lender Credit Rate field as the rate.
Continuance in Months
Calculated based on the value for Continuance in Years and the Continuance Type from the Program..
If the Continuance Type is set to years, then the value is 12 multiplied by the Continuance in Years field.
Otherwise, it is the value for the Continuance in Years field.
Closing Cost
Calculated value based on the calculated First Loan Average Estimated Cost, Other Amounts Total, Point Rate, and the Lender Credit Amount.
Prepaid Interest
Calculated based on the Base Loan Amount, the Program's Rate, and the Prepaid Interest Days field.
VAFF Amount
Calculated value based on the Base Loan Amount and the Program's VAFF (VA Funding Fee) Rate entered in the percent function.

View and Manage Single Property Sites (SPS)
Setting Your Sites' Theme Colors
Single Property Sites are published using a Theme Color which appears as the dominant color for graphic and text accents throughout the site.
A default Company Theme Color is set by Single Property Site administrators.
Standard Users have the option to customize the Theme Color for their Single Property Sites so that it echoes or compliments their company or brand's official color(s).
Once a custom color has been selected and applied, it does not get reset, even if Single Property Site Administrators change the default Theme Color.
To Customize the Theme Color for All Sites:
Go to Marketing, Single Property Websites.
Select Company Settings tab.
Select Company Settings.
Select the colored bar.
A color picker map from which you can select a theme color for your sites is displayed.
Use the color picker interface to choose your color or, alternatively, enter the HTML / CSS Name, Hex Code (#RRGGBB) or RGB Decimal Code (0,0,255) for the color directly into the field.
Select Save Settings.
Users Theme Colors
If a user has adequate permission you can set the colors of your own SPS sites.
Go to Marketing, Single Property Sites.
Select My Settings tab.
Select the colored bar.
A color picker map from which you can select a theme color for your sites is displayed.
Use the color picker interface to choose your color or, alternatively, enter the HTML / CSS Name, Hex Code (#RRGGBB) or RGB Decimal Code (0,0,255) for the color directly into the field.
Select Save Settings.
