's Markets in a Minute content provides a weekly video update on the current climate of the housing market so that you and your contacts can stay up-to-date on the rate environment, the economy, and news impacting the mortgage industry. There are multiple ways to distribute this content to your contacts.
Your organization may have created a recurring deployment that subscribe to and receive the Markets in a Minute content. You can subscribe to the deployment by clicking the Markets in a Minute deployment.
When you subscribe, you will see.

Marketing
Markets in a Minute
Markets in a Minute Drip Campaign
If you want to set up a drip communication for a group of your contacts, you can create a recurring deployment. You can set up a recurring deployment that shares Surefire 's Markets in a Minute content as a social media post or you can choose to directly email your leads the weekly update as well.
Create a New Recurring Deployment
Navigate to the Deployment Center located within the Marketing tab and click on the button to Create Deployment.
When prompted select to create a recurring deployment.
Select Frequency for Deployment Surefire updates our Markets in a Minute content every Thursday by 2:00 p.m. eastern time. To take advantage of these updates, the deployment sends out every Thursday at 2:30 p.m. so you and your contacts can keep up-to-date as you head into your busy weekend!
If you are an administrator for your organization, you can also choose to make this recurring deployment available for your company by choosing For My Company instead of For Myself.
Select your Media and Distribution Method
The next step is to select the media you want to send in our communication. Go to Public Folder > Markets in a Minute, and select Markets in a Minute Video Recurring.
This link is updated every week with the current week's content.
Once you have selected the media, you can select the method with which you want to reach your contacts. We're going to choose to send this deployment via email and we will also create a new social media post on our business' Facebook account. Check out the link to learn how to connect your company's social media accounts. Connecting your Facebook
You may choose to use your Contacts Media Preference using the toggle. If your contact has their preference set to text, and text is not an available media type, those contacts will not receive the deployment.
Build Your Audience
The next step is to choose the contacts that will receive the recurring deployment you've created as well as the opt out list. We're going to select the marketing opt out list to not include any contacts that have requested to not receive marketing content from Surefire. We may choose to Target All Valid Contacts that we have in our system if we wish.
Admin Note. If you previously selected to have this deployment For My Company, you do not have to select a target audience. You may simply select your Email Opt Out list and save for your users. Once saved, this deployment will appear as an available subscription for the users of your organization.
Dynamic Target Groups
In this situation, we're going to choose to only target our contacts that are listed as a referral partner contact type as these are the individuals that we believe will find this information most relevant and useful. The great thing about this target group is that as we add referral partners to our contact list in Surefire, they'll automatically be added to our distribution list without any extra effort. Surefire is going to do all the time intensive work for you to keep your contacts up-to-date and engaged.
Review and Deploy
Our Markets in a Minute deployment is all set! We've successfully created a deployment that will engage our referral partners with new and relevant content every Thursday at 2:30 pm. We could have 2 referral partners today or 100 in two weeks, but Surefire will ensure that it's directed to those we've updated in our contact list without us having to worry about anything.

Marketing
Markets in a Minute
Markets in a Minute Landing Page
The Markets In A Minute landing page can be a bookmarked as a favorite for your referral sources, leads, and clients.

Marketing
Markets in a Minute
Markets in a Minute Social Posts
To better align with Facebook best practices, the message that accompanies the Markets in a Minute video and interactive social posts is updated weekly (beginning 6/13/2024).
The message describes rate movement, using the text from the video's voiceover and adding the date. Example: Rates moved lower during the week ending 6/7/24 due to signs of weakening in the economy and labor market.
The last sentence in the message is: {Company Name} is an Equal Housing Lender.
Timely messages are applied each week in the public versions of the Markets in a Minute video and interactive, located in the Public>Markets in a Minute folder.
If you want timely weekly messages in a cloned version of the Markets in a Minute video or interactive, you'll want to update the social posts yourself each week. If you wish, you can copy the verbiage we use in the public collections, which we publish by 2 p.m. ET each Thursday.
If you or your organization uses a recurring deployment subscription, you do not need to recreate or adjust the subscription. If it points to a public Markets in a Minute collection, the recurring deployment will reflect the Surefire changes each week. If it points to a cloned collection and you wish to make weekly updates, you’ll need to make those changes in your cloned collection as described above.
The impacted collections are found in the Public>Markets in a Minute folder. They include: Markets in a Minute Video, Markets in a Minute Recurring Video, Markets in a Minute Interactive, and Markets in a Minute Interactive Landing Page Recurring Deployment.
Here’s another best practice to consider:
Facebook discourages using links that prevent people from getting directly to the linked page, such as pop ups. While Surefire configuration panels allow companies to add a pop-up disclaimer to their Markets in a Minute landing pages, it’s possible that Facebook will discourage this practice.
An alternative is to use a cloned Markets in a Minute landing page and to add disclaimer verbiage on the page itself.

Markets in a Minute
Sample Color Branded Markets in a Minute Newsletter

The Media Library is where different types of marketing media and assets are stored in a standard folder directory system. You can come to the Media Library to view and access existing Media as well as to create your own new Media.
It is located in Marketing, Media Library.
The different media types in the Library currently include:
Content Collections
Content Collections are bundles of different types of marketing media templates, including:
Email
Text Message
Social
Postcard
Assets
Assets are different from Content Collections in that they do not represent an outbound message that you would send to a Contact. Rather, they are items that can be utilized as a part of a Collection.
Images
Standard image files that can be used in any HTML, either for an Email or a Landing Page.
Forms
Web forms to capture Contact of Deal data. These can be embedded on a Surefire Landing Page or any other live webpage.
Landing Pages
Web pages whose links can be inserted into Content Collections. These can contain a Form to capture Contact or Deal data.
Layouts
Layouts are fixed Header and Footer content that can be attached to the following media:
Email
Text Message
Landing Page
Postcards
After creating these media types, you must choose what Layout to apply. This can be a helpful way to standardize content and ensure, for example, that you are including the same disclosures on every Email.
View Library
You can navigate through the Media Library in a similar way as you would navigate through the folder directory on your computer.

Marketing
Media Library
Media Content Collections
Content Collections are at the heart of your marketing efforts in Surefire. They are a bundled batch of media templates, Email, Text, or Social, or Postcards, with a similar message or theme.
For instance, you could have a Happy Birthday Collection that contains an Email and Text wishing someone Happy Birthday. Or you could have an Easter Collection which has an Email, Text, and Social post all celebrating Easter.
When you go to the Deployment Center and select what Collection you want to send, you have the option to select which media you want to include or exclude. This way, you can Create a Deployment across different media all at the same time.
Alternatively, if you are creating or editing a collection in the Media Library, you will have the option to Deploy directly through the Deployment Wizard.
If you are just creating a new collection, the Create Deployment button does not appear until after the collection is Saved.
Create a Content Collection
Go to Marketing, Media Library.
Click + Create.
Select the New Collection button.
Complete the following: Collection Name - enter a name Description - enter a description Folder - select the applicable folder
Select Create Collection.
Tags and Use Tags
You can Tag your Collection for easy categorization. You can also apply a Use Tag to limit the visibility of the Collection to certain Users and Companies.
Save and Delete
You must Save any changes to Media by clicking the Save button. Alternatively, select Delete to remove the Media.
It is important to note that the Save and Delete buttons correspond to the Media type you are working with in the Collection itself and not the entire Collection. So if you are working with a collection that uses email and text but decide to delete the email collection you will still have the text media in that collection.
If you want to change the folder that the Collection is saved in, you can move the collection from the Media Library. If you want to Delete the Collection, this is done from the Media Library.
Add New Media Type
The main tabs across the page are used to add Media to your Collection. By default, the only Media Type created is Email.
To add more Media, click + Add New Media Type and select Media.
You can only have one of each Media Type per Collection.
Add a Layout
For each of the Media Types, you must apply a Layout. This is the static Header and Footer that will be applied to the Media when it goes out.

Marketing
Media Library
Media Assets
Assets are elements of the CRM that can be included in outbound media, such as Emails, Social Posts or Landing Pages. These differ from Content Collections in that individually they cannot be Deployed to your Contacts. To locate your assets navigate to Marketing, Media Library and select the Assets tab.
Assets are modular blocks that you insert into Collections. For instance, an Image that is a JPG of a polar bear that you insert into a Happy Holidays Email. Or a Contact Us Form that you insert on a Landing Page. And that Landing Page itself is an Asset when you insert it into an Email.
Currently, the types of Assets you can create and use are:
Images
Forms
Landing Pages
You can also Insert Dynamic Video into a Landing Pages; however, you are currently limited to Surefire created dynamic videos.
Images
Standard image files that can be used in any HTML, either for an Email, Text Message, Social or a Landing Page. Currently, you can use JPG, GIF (non-animated), PNG and JPEG.
Forms
Web forms are used to capture Contact, Lead or Deal data that is in turn automatically entered into Surefire when the Form is submitted. These can be embedded on a Surefire Landing Page or any other live webpage.
Landing Pages
Web pages whose links can be inserted into Content Collections. These can contain a form to capture Contact or Deal data.

Marketing
Media Library
Media Layouts
Layout is a static Header and Footer that can be appended to certain Media Types. They can be used to quickly and easily standardize the design and branding of your Company's media.
Whenever you are creating a Content Collection with Text Messaging or Email, you are required to select a Layout to apply to the template you are creating.
This can help you to ensure that your marketing materials remain compliant by forcibly adding any required disclosures to the outbound messaging.
Email Layout
Design different collections of Header and Footer's that will be applied to the top and bottom of the HTML Email Content that you create.
Text Message Layout
Create a simple text message footer to apply to Text Content.
Landing Page Layout
Landing Page Layouts are not require but can save you lots of time if you have elements like standardized Footers that you want to add to all Landing Pages.
Default Layouts
For each Layout Type, you have the option to set one Layout as the Company Default. This will automatically apply that Layout to each new Media that is created. The creator still has the option to change it.

Assets
Layouts

Folders - used to find the actual Media View All - This is the default and will display all of the contents of your Company and Personal folders
This does not include the contents of the Public Folder Public Folder - Contains Surefire created public content. Media cannot be saved or moved to this folder. Company Folder - View and access any Companies you have permissions to as well as the underlying User folders. Personal Folder - Accessible and viewable only by you or Admins above you in your Company

Use HTML Editor
You can create content across the CRM, using two options:
Design with Surefire HTML Editor
Design Offline and Copy in HTML Code
Basic Design Tools
If you have used any type of email or HTML editor, the format of the Surefire HTML Editor will be familiar.
Using the Editor, functions similarly to a desktop word editing program, you can perform several simple editing operations, including but not limited to:
Text formatting (e.g. bold, italics, etc.)
Font size & type
Text & background-color
Bullets & numbered lists
Text alignment
Indent margins
Insert a table
Insert Merge Fields
You can merge database fields into your Email by choosing the Merge Fields dropdown and either selecting the desired field from the list or typing the name of the field to filter/search.
You can merge fields from the following objects: Contact - The Contact who is receiving the Email User - The User who is sending the Email
This is the User sending the email, not the Owner of the Contact. So in a situation where a Rule or Workflow is triggering an email that is sent from a Team Member, the Team Member's information would merge into the Email. Company - The Company of the User who is sending the Email
The fields will then be dynamically generated whenever an email is deployed based on who is sending (User) and who is receiving (Contact or User).
Conditional Merge Fields
The Conditional Merge Fields offer a way to eliminate a segment or line item in a Merge Field. A particular use case would be if phone numbers are labeled as Office and Mobile, and a user does not have a value for one of these in his or her profile. This function allows the label in the HTML to not be displayed with an empty value.
Insert Image
Select The Asset Browser opens, where you can browse through your Media Library for the Image you are looking for.
You can Upload a New Image if it isn't in the Media Library yet; click the Upload Image button from the Asset Browser.
Select the Folder you want to access, default is View All.
You can search for the Image in the Search Assets box
Toggle between List View and Thumbnail view by clicking the icon in the top right
Select the checkbox next to the Image you want to insert. Only one Image can be inserted at a time.
Select Apply.
Insert Link
You can insert a hyperlink into your Email by clicking.
You can either highlight an existing word in your Content that you want to hyperlink and then click the icon, or you can insert the link by itself.
Either way, when you Insert a Link, you have the following options: URL - The HTML page you want to link to. Must start with http://. If you don't add the http://, the system will ask if you want to append it.
Some pages use https:// so to be safe, instead of trying to type it the website address you want to link to, you should copy & paste the URL from your browser address bar. Text to Display - If you don't want to display the actual URL in the body of your email, you can add display text here. e.g. A link formatted with a URL and Text to Display of our website would look like this: Title - This is the alternative text that will display when you hover over the link in your email. Target - Choose if you want the link to open in a New Window. Otherwise, when the link is clicked, the native behavior of the user's email client or browser will dictate if a new window or tab opens.
View the HTML Code
You can paste your own HTML code into an email, or edit the existing code you have created with the editor, by clicking the HTML button.
This opens the Source Code window where you can either paste your HTML text or edit the HTML code created by the Editor.
Select OK to save any changes you made.

Marketing
Media Library
Create an Email Layout
Use Email Layouts to create different sets of Headers and Footers that are applied to the top and bottom of the Email Content Collections that you create.
All Email Content created in Surefire must have an Email Layout assigned to it in order to Save it. This helps to ensure that Email remains compliant from both a legal disclosure perspective (depending on your industry) as well as for CAN-SPAM requirements.
The major CAN-SPAM requirements that Layouts address are:
Include the physical address of the company
Include clear & conspicuous opt-out mechanism
Creating Email Layouts is done from the Media Library:
Go to Marketing, Media Library.
Select + Create.
Select New Layout.
In the Layout Type list, select Email.
Enter a Layout Name and Description
Select a folder to save it to in the Media Library.
You can set the Layout as Company Default.
Use the HTML editor to design a:
Header
Footer
Insert Merge Fields in the Footer for:
Company Mailing (or Billing) Address Block
Company Link - Unsubscribe
If created in Company Logos you can:
Add the secondary logo merge field {{Company Image - Secondary Logo Thumbnail}} to your email Layout to include industry logos to populate on the footer of your emails.
Select Save Email Layout.
You can either insert each individual Address Block merge fields (e.g. Company - City, Company -State, etc.) or you can insert the Address Block which combines all of these fields into one block of text for you.
HTML Editor
Review Create an Email for Content Collection for more information on using the HTML Editor.
Set as Company Default
In the Set as Company Default field select Yes to set the Email Layout the standard Default for your Company. This automatically applies the Layout to any Email Content created by your Company.
Only Users with the appropriate Permissions, can edit and change to another Layout Option.
Use Tags
After you have saved your layout, you have the option to add Use Tags to it. This helps you limit which Users can and cannot access the Layout.
To add or edit Use Tags, click on the Use Tags box to bring up the Use Tags Editor. This will display existing Use Tags as well as let you add more or remove existing.
CAN-SPAM Requirements
Below is an excerpt from the FTC.gov website's
CAN-SPAM Act: A Compliance Guide for Business which summarizes CAN-SPAM's main requirements:
Don’t use false or misleading header information.
Your “From,” “To,” “Reply-To,” and routing information – including the originating domain name and email address – must be accurate and identify the person or business who initiated the message.
Don’t use deceptive subject lines. The subject line must accurately reflect the content of the message.
Identify the message as an ad.
The law gives you a lot of leeway in how to do this, but you must disclose clearly and conspicuously that your message is an advertisement.
Tell recipients where you’re located.
Your message must include your valid physical postal address. This can be your current street address, a post office box you’ve registered with the US Postal Service, or a private mailbox you’ve registered with a commercial mail receiving agency established under Postal Service regulations.
Tell recipients how to opt-out of receiving future emails from you.
Your message must include a clear and conspicuous explanation of how the recipient can opt-out of getting an email from you in the future. Craft the notice in a way that’s easy for an ordinary person to recognize, read, and understand. Creative use of type size, color, and location can improve clarity. Give a return email address or another easy Internet-based way to allow people to communicate their choice to you. You may create a menu to allow a recipient to opt-out of certain types of messages, but you must include the option to stop all commercial messages from you. Make sure your spam filter doesn’t block these opt-out requests.
Honor opt-out requests promptly.
Any opt-out mechanism you offer must be able to process opt-out requests for at least 30 days after you send your message. You must honor a recipient’s opt-out request within 10 business days. You can’t charge a fee, require the recipient to give you any personally identifying information beyond an email address, or make the recipient take any step other than sending a reply email or visiting a single page on an Internet website as a condition for honoring an opt-out request. Once people have told you they don’t want to receive more messages from you, you can’t sell or transfer their email addresses, even in the form of a mailing list. The only exception is that you may transfer the addresses to a company you’ve hired to help you comply with the CAN-SPAM Act.
Monitor what others are doing on your behalf.
The law makes clear that even if you hire another company to handle your email marketing, you can’t contract away your legal responsibility to comply with the law. Both the company whose product is promoted in the message and the company that actually sends the message may be held legally responsible.

Marketing
Media Library
Create a Text Message Layout
Use Text Message Layouts to create a footer that you can add to the end of any Text Message Content Collections that you create.
Unlike Email, Text Message Content created in Surefire does not require a Layout; however, it can be helpful if you want to include opt-out language such as:
Reply with STOP to unsubscribe
Or similar prompts that will allow Contacts to unsubscribe from Text marketing.
The Text Message system used by Surefire will recognize a response of STOP as an unsubscribe and add the phone number to an Opt-Out List so they no longer receive Text messages in the future.
Creating a Text Message Layout is done from the Media Library:
Go to Marketing, Media Library.
Select + Create.
Select New Layout.
In the Layout Type list select Text Message.
Enter a Layout Name and Description.
Select the folder to save it to in the Media Library.
You can set the Layout as Company Default.
Enter in the Footer text you want to include.
It is best if the Footer text is under 75 characters.
Select Save Text Message Layout.
Enter a Text Message Footer
The Text Message footer is automatically appended immediately after the Text Content Collection text ends.
There is an option to include Merge Fields. Find the field you want in the Merge Field dropdown by scrolling or typing a search term. When you select the field, it will insert in your Footer where the cursor is.
Because you are limited to the number of characters you can include in a text message before it splits into two separate messages, it is advised to keep the length of your Footer to under 75 characters.
There is a counter that will automatically calculate the number of characters for the footer. If you include Merge Fields, the counter will estimate each field at 7 characters.
Set as Company Default
By toggling Yes for the Set as Company Default option, you set the Text Message Layout as the standard Default for your Company. This automatically applies the Layout to any Text Message Content created by your Company.
If Users have the appropriate Permissions, they can edit and change to another Layout Option.
Use Tags
After you have saved your layout, you have the option to add Use Tags to it. This helps you limit which Users can and cannot access the Layout.
To add or edit Use Tags, click on the Use Tags box to bring up the Use Tags Editor. This will display existing Use Tags as well as let you add more or remove existing.
Opt-Out Commands Surefire currently supports the following Text Message opt-out commands:
STOP
UNSUBSCRIBE
REMOVE ME
If you prompt recipients to respond with any of these commands, they will automatically be added to your Text Message Opt-Out List. No further Text Messages from your Surefire marketing Deployments are sent to them.
You can review your Text Message Subscription Lists, including how many opt-outs you have, by going to My Account, My Settings and viewing the Telephony/Text Messages tab.

MBS Highway
MBS Highway Surefire CRM supports the MBS Highway integration featuring the Real Estate Report Card.
Users with an MBS Highway account can set up their Surefire account to share the Real Estate Report Card in email and text messaging communications with their contacts.
Admin Setup
The use of MBS Highway in Surefire is permission based. Permission must be granted by an Admin prior to a User’s ability to integrate their account.
User Setup
To add your MBS Highway integration:
Go to My Account, My Profile.
Select Integrations tab.
Select Add Integration button.
Select MBS Highway Report Card option.
If the option is not present, then the necessary permission hasn’t been set. Check with your company’s Admin about access.
Enter your MBS Highway Username.
Select Save to add your integration.
Usage
Use the MBS Highway Real Estate Report Card in communications with your contacts to showcase analytics relative to a contact’s designated zip code. Add an MBS link in email collections and text messaging that when clicked will present the recipient with their specific report card.
When creating an email collection, you can set up and insert the MBS Highway link to the Real Estate Report Card in your email.
Click to display the configuration.
Select an option in Contact Zip Code Field *:
Mailing Address Zip
Physical Address Zip
Company Address Zip
This information will pull directly from the contact record.
Complete the required fields:
Domain *
– choose your preferred domain
Link Display *
– either Text Only or Image
Text Only, allows you to use clickable Link Text in lieu of showing the actual URL.
Image, allows you to upload/add a clickable image in lieu of showing the actual URL.
Select Insert.
When creating a Text Message Collection, you will have the option to Insert MBS Highway Report Card Link in your text message.
When clicked to insert, you are presented with a configuration panel to designate the Contact Zip Code Field and the Domain. The link is not configurable and will show as the actual URL in the text message.

Marketing
Media Library
Deal Merge and Primary Deal Fields
Deal fields are available product-related merge fields that can be utilized within Surefire functionality to include product deal information contained within the Primary Deal Slots. These Deal Fields are available for use within many Surefire features including Rules and Workflows, Email, Text Messaging, Landing Pages, and Postcards. The incorporation of these fields within different features will allow Surefire to pull in very detailed deal information to be included in content communications with specific contacts.
If the rule or workflow that associated with the deployment is triggered by a deal update, that deal's merge fields will be utilized. If the deployment is not triggered by a deal update, the system will utilize Primary Deal Fields as the merge fields. More information can be found about Primary Deal Slots.
Primary Deal has rank for each contact. Unless otherwise noted below, if the Primary Residence Deal Slot is fulfilled, then that slot is utilized for Primary Deal Fields. If not, then the Primary Investment Deal Slot is used. If neither the Primary Residence nor the Primary Investment Deal Slots are fulfilled, then the Primary Secondary Deal Slot is utilized.
Deal fields include:
Dates – Application, Estimated Closing, Closing, Creation
Credit Scores – Borrower, Co-Borrower, Combined
Address Information
Property Type
Loan Information – Product, Amortization, Term, Amount, Property Value, Rate
File Number
Type
Lien
Purpose
Occupancy
Loan Status
Custom Fields
Rules and Workflows
For Rules and Workflows, when a product is included and a deal is used as the trigger, the deal that is referenced in the rule will be the deal data that will populate the merge fields in the content. If a product is included in a rule but a contact is being used as the rule trigger (no deal reference), then the primary deal fields will default to the Primary Deal Slot. If the Primary Deal Slot is empty, then there is no deal to reference and the deployment will be skipped. *This will be noted in the contact deployment record as “Skipped”.
Workflows are already deal aware. When adding a contact to a workflow that includes a product, the user must identify the deal to reference to complete the workflow setup.
Emails, Postcards, and Text Messages
For Media Library content, the inclusion of a product in the Create Collection panel will allow for the availability and access of primary deal fields to be used in the newly created content collection.
If applicable, Product related merge fields are located in the editor merge field list.
Recurring Deployments
The Deployment Center is cognizant that the content/media included contains deal fields and that there is a primary deal for the Audience member.
Landing Pages
Landing Pages, both Dynamic and Permalink, will use the Primary Deal Slot as the default deal record when importing merge field related data. Primary Deal Fields can be found in the Text Editor merge field list.

Product Fields and Conditional Formatting
Product Merge Fields
Email collections can display loan information using product merge fields. Loan information shown will always be for the email recipient’s primary deal.
Select a product from the list to include product deal fields in an email.
To place a product merge field in the body of the email, place your cursor where you want the merge field to appear.
Select the merge field from the list.
Conditional Formatting
You can use conditional formatting to show or hide text based on whether a certain product merge field is present. To apply conditional formatting, highlight the text you want to show/hide conditionally, then select Conditional from the editing toolbar.
The Conditional Block appears, you can use the editing tools to continue editing your content block in the top section.
In the Condition Based On This Field Having a Value dropdown, choose the merge field that must be present in the recipient’s contact record so the conditional text will appear. This can be any merge field, whether a product field or not.
In the Conditional Block Behavior dropdown, choose whether the conditional area is in a line with other items or is its own section/line.
In the Add Trailing Whitespace dropdown, choose whether or not you want to add white space to replace the conditional section if the condition is not met. Save to add your condition, and the section will now appear highlighted in the email template. To edit or delete the condition, hover your mouse over the highlighted area, and a box will appear giving the option to edit or remove the condition.

Implement Pro Series Video Presentation Interactive
The Pro Series Video Presentation Interactive offers a one-step landing page for sharing Pro Series In Process and Guide to Real Estate videos with your agent partners.
Surefire Located in the Public, Referral Partner Collections folder, the interactive contains clickable thumbnail images for each video in the Pro Series in-process purchase and refi series videos plus the similarly styled Guide to Real Estate videos.
Here are two ways to share this interactive:
1. Easiest and fastest implementation: Share the collection and interactive as they are.
PRO: No setup required. Your name and information will appear at the end of each video.
CON: Doesn't highlight the ability to cobrand or to show deal information within the videos.
Directions: Navigate to the Media Library and locate the Pro Series Video Presentation collection in the Public>Referral Partner folder. Create a deployment. Alternatively, navigate to one partner's contact record and deploy through a One to One email.
2. Best practice implementation: Set up sample deal teams and generate a link to share.
PRO: Referral partners will experience the full impact of cobranding and personalization for the borrower's deal.
CON: Requires more setup time.
Directions:
•	Create sample data.
•	Add contact records for a sample borrower (using your own email address), listing agent (optional) and buying agent. If you choose, add a contact record for a processor within your company or a sample processor.
•	We’ve provided a variety of stock photos in the Public>Referral Partner Collections folder so you can give your sample team professional headshots. Simply locate the image you would like to use, right click and Save as to download it onto your computer, then upload it when editing your sample contact.
•	Add a deal to your borrower’s contact record. Add your sample Deal Team member contacts to the deal in their appropriate slots.
•	Generate a link to share in conversations, presentations or electronically.
•	Navigate to the contact record for your sample borrower. Click on the rocket icon to deploy a One to One email. Select the collection titled Pro Series Video Presentation, located in the Public>Referral Partner folder. When it arrives in your inbox, click the play button. This is the link you can share with your prospective partners. Bookmark it so you'll always have it handy.
•	Send your link in an email.
•	Clone the collection titled MUST BE EDITED Pro Series Video Presentation, found in the Public>Referral Partners folder. Click on the words “Play Sample Videos” in the box at the bottom of the email. Click on the link image in the editor window, paste your URL into the dialogue box, and save. Click on the left side of the screen to Save Media.
•	Navigate to the contact record of your prospective partner and click on the rocket icon to deploy a One to One email. Select and send the cloned collection you just edited.
•	Want to take it a step further? Create a contact record for the agent partner you’re approaching and add him/her to the deal team!

•	Clone the landing page to adjust the background color or edit the text that appears at the tops of the landing page. (Click on the three dots next to the landing page name and select "clone" from the drop down.)

•	Color on videos within the series
•	Included series (purchase, refi, agent)
•	Included videos within the series

You can create website Forms that can be used to capture Contact, Lead or Deal data that is in turn automatically entered into Surefire when the Form is submitted. These Forms can be either embedded into any existing website or be inserted into Surefire created Landing Pages.

Marketing
Forms
Create a Form
You can create website Forms that can be used to capture Contact, Lead or Deal data that is in turn automatically entered into Surefire when the Form is submitted. These Forms can be either embedded into any existing website or be inserted into Surefire created Landing Pages.
Create a New Form
Go to Marketing, Forms.
Select + Create.
Click New Form.
Enter a Name.
Enter a Description
(optional).
Select a Product from the list if applicable.
When you associate a Form with a Product, you will be able to add Elements and Contact Fields specific to that Product.
Select a Folder from the list.
Where a Form is saved in your organizational hierarchy determines which users will have access to it.
Select Create.
Build Your Form
On the Build tab, start by organizing the layout of your Form by dragging Section and Page Break elements from the right side of the screen and dropping them into the Build area.
Contact & Product Fields
There are two types of Fields a Form can have: Contact/Product Fields - pre-existing fields in that, when the Form is submitted, will populate with the submitted value. Form Fields - default Form Fields, identified in the bank of Field Types in the right column of the Builder, are non-database fields. This means any data entered in these Fields will only reside in the Form Results page and will not be attached to a Contact or Deal (This is useful for things like surveys).
Transitions
You can use Transitions to direct the order in which users move through the Pages of your Form. A Transition is a command telling the Form what to do when a user clicks a Form navigation button sucah as next or submit.
Note: You'll be able to make building and editing your Form a lot easier by managing how many of your fields are displayed on the build page at once. Do this by using the Expand/Collapse Sections and Expand/Collapse Pages buttons, both located at the top of the Build Area.
Configure Your Form
Go to the Configure tab to make changes to global Form attributes (e.g. Name, Description and Product association) and functions (e.g. Navigation Style, whether to assign Point Values to Form Fields and if/how Form submissions are reviewed).
Distribute Your Form
Go to the Distribute tab to generate an embed code that will allow your Form to appear on any external website.
Integrate your Form with other providers Surefire can deliver Form results via a post URL. When turned on you will see several additional fields you can fill in from your provider to sync your Form information. You will need to enter your integration authentication details such as the Service Name, External Service URL, Authentication Mode and the fields you want to map over. When any Form is submitted Surefire will have your results and the integration you set up will also get a push of the information you indicate.

Marketing
Forms
Theme and Styles in Forms
If you want to style your Form so that it is different from the default version you can create and apply a form theme. A Form Theme will allow you to change the Colors, Labeling, Fonts, as well as Buttons.
Access Form Themes
Go to Marketing , Forms.
You can narrow the list of Forms that's displayed, specify the Folder that includes the Form you want to design.
Locate the Form you want to style.
You can either sort the table by displaying all your selected Forms, or by using the Search function.
Select the Form's Name, in the Name column of the table.
On the Build screen select the Distribute tab.
For every embeddable version of your Form here, you can apply a Theme.
For the Domain you want to customize, click the link under the Theme column.
This will be Default for any Form you have not applied a Theme to.
On the Design Tab, a preview shows your Form. It dynamically updates as you make changes to its style. The Design menu is divided into four sections:
Display
Fonts
Navigation
Colors
Display
This section shows styling selection options for how specific form elements appear or behave.
Display is divided into four category groups:
Form Show form name - Toggle to Yes if you want to display the Name of your Form (as defined under the Configure tab) at the top of the Form Show form description - Toggle to Yes if you want to display the Description of your Form (as defined under the Configure tab) beneath the Form Name at the top of the Form Vertical padding - Refers to the amount of space moving down from the top margin and up from the bottom margin, in pixels, that will be kept empty of content. Horizontal Padding - Refers to the amount of space moving inward from the left and right margins, in pixels, that will be kept empty of content.
Pages & Sections
You have the option to designate whether (Page and/or Section) Titles and Descriptions are displayed on the published Form.
Review Add Form Pages and Sections for additional information.
Questions Label placement - Choose whether the Question/Label for each Form Field appears either above or to the left of the Field. Hint Placement - For Question/Labels on the Form, if a Hint has been added, select whether the Hint appears as a clickable question mark icon above the field, or in a pop up window that appears when the Form user hovers their mouse pointer over the field, or as text permanently displayed below the Field. Label spacing - Refers to the amount of space, in pixels, between a Form Field's Question/Label and the blank part of the Field that will be kept empty of content. Choose a value between 0 and 30. Question spacing - Refers to the amount of space, in pixels, between Form Fields on the Form that will be kept empty of content. Choose a value between 0 and 30.
Label font size
-Refers to the size, in pixels, of the text for Question/Labels on the Form. Choose a value between 12 and 30. Field font size - Refers to the size, in pixels, that text entered into Form Fields will be rendered in. Choose a value between 12 and 30.
Image Option Default
Fonts
Select the Font the Form will be rendered in from the list. This will apply to all text on the Form, including text entered by Form users into Form Fields.
Navigation
In this section you can customize the appearance of the navigation buttons, defaulted as Continue, Back, and Submit, that appear at the bottom of your Form's pages.
You are given the option to change the text that appears on the buttons. So, for example, instead of saying Next, you could change it to Proceed.
Alternatively, you could choose to replace the buttons and their labels with images, for example, pictures of arrows.
Colors
Apply the selection options on this tab to add color to your Form in one of two ways: Pre-Configured Color Palette - Select Pallets to see a list of pre-configured color combinations, each displayed as a square icon. Click on an icon to select that color combination.
Select Custom Colors - Select Custom to customize various elements by hex code color.
If you choose to use custom colors, you can change the following Form elements:
Background
Border
Question Text
Answer Text
Primary Button
Secondary Button (e.g. Back button)
Highlight (e.g. active Form field.)
Required Text
Selected Text
To change the color, you can either use the color palette picker or enter a hex code.
Save a Theme
Once you have made your Design edits, you can save this styled version of a Form as a Form Theme. You can then apply this Theme to other Forms to automatically format them.
Select Save to Library.
Use the list at the top to select the folder location you want to save your Theme to.
Identify if themes exist and complete the applicable action:
If no Themes are stored in the selected folder,
Enter a name for your Theme in Name your theme field.
Select Save.
If there are already Themes stored in your selected folder:
You can overwrite the most recently saved Theme (regardless of what name you've entered). Select Save.
You are prompted to confirm that you want overwrite the existing Theme.
You can save your Theme as a separate new theme ( regardless of what name you've entered). Select Save as New.
Apply Theme to Form
Once you have created one or several Form Themes, you can easily apply them to new or existing Forms.
On the Design screen, select Choose a Theme.
Use the list to locate the Theme you want to use.
Stored themes in your selected folder are display as square icons.
Select the icon corresponding to the Theme you want to use.
Select Apply Theme button.
Confirm that you want to use this Theme.

Marketing
Forms
Add Form Fields
A Field is where you store an independent piece of data. An easy way to visualize a data Field is to think of it as an individual cell in a spreadsheet.
Form Fields are created independent of Surefire Contact or Product attributes. In other words, once configured, they are data fields that are only associated with this one particular Form and can be found nowhere else in Surefire By contrast, Contact and Product Fields on a Form are mapped to the corresponding Surefire database fields. This means that when a Form is submitted using these Fields, content that was entered into them is used to create a Product or Contact and populate the corresponding fields in those Surefire records.
Add Fields to Sections
Form Fields must reside in Form Sections.
Form Fields are added to a Form by dragging them from the Elements area on the right side of the Form Build screen and dropping them into the Build area.
Field Settings
When you add a Form Field into a Section in a Form, you are presented with the Field's Details screen. This is where, by making Field Setting selections and customizing Field Parameters, you define how the Field appears, what content it presents and requests, and how it functions on your Form. It's also where a Field's placement order in your Form's layout is displayed. Question/Label - This is the text that appears next to the Form Field in the published Form. Its purpose is to indicate to the Form user what type of response data the Form Field is supposed to capture. This is required. Hint - When you set this option to Yes, a text field is displayed in the Form Field Details screen where you can enter a more detailed explanation about what type of response data the Field is supposed to capture. Then, upon publication of the Form, a question mark icon will appear next to the Field. When a Form user clicks on the question mark, the explanation is displayed in a pop up window.
Required -
When this option is set to Yes the field must be filled out, the user is not to be able to proceed to the next Section or Page of the Form until they complete this field. Use Current Value as Default - When this option is set to ON, upon Form deployment to a Surefire Contact, the Form Field will be pre-populated with the corresponding content for the Surefire Contact to whom the Form is sent
Example, if you created a Form where the Fields for First and Last Name were configured to "Use Current Value as Default," and then you deployed the Form to your Contact Jane Smith, when Jane accessed the Form the First Name and Last Name fields would be automatically filled in with "Jane" and "Smith," respectively.
Note: Form users will still be able to change the value and any change will overwrite the existing Field Value on their Contact when they submit the Form. Default Value - Upon Form publication, the Form Field will be pre-populated with any content entered here. Form users will be able to change the value.
Not available when Use Current Value as Default is set to Yes. Placeholder - Upon Form Publication, content entered here will be displayed as a suggested entry in the Form Field
Visibility
-Use this list to select whether the Field is Visible to or Hidden from the user
Hidden Fields do not appear on the published Form. They are used to store a default value or to submit data that is not entered by the Form user but is instead auto-generated. For example, on your company website lead form, you might want to have a hidden field for Lead Source and populate it with a Default Value or Website Variable Name - review Adding Form Field Variable Names
Field Label versus Value
For Field Types that supply pre-defined options , such as Radio or Dropdown, you must set both a Field Label and Value for each answer. The label is how the answer is viewed on the Form; the Value is how it is stored in the database. e.g. You can have a Radio Button question with answers for "California" and "Florida" as the Labels, but if you set the Values to "CA" and "FL", respectively, the state abbreviations are what will actually be stored in Surefire.
Field Placement
Form Fields are always labeled, both in the Build area as well as on the title bars of their Details screens, to indicate that Form Field's order of placement within the Form. They are numbered, in alphabetically ordered lower case letters, in the order in which they appear within the section they reside.
Form Fields can be moved within your Form layout by dragging and dropping them within your design. Placement order labels are updated automatically whenever a move occurs.
Field Types
Any of the Form Fields defined below can be added to any section of a Form. Additionally, a few of the Form Fields defined below include definitions of customization options that are in addition to those described above.
Short Text
-The text field that is published as a single line; cannot be re-sized by Form user to show more lines of text Long text - Text field that can be re-sized by Form users so that they can see up to as much as all of their entered text at once Number - Only positive and negative numbers, including decimals, can be entered into this Field. Decimal - Only positive and negative numbers, including decimals, can be entered into this Field. Currency - This Field is published in Forms with a dollar sign displayed at its far left. Only positive and negative numbers, including decimals, can be entered into this Field.
Percent -
This Field is published in Forms with a percentage sign displayed at its far right. Only positive and negative numbers can be entered into this Field. Checkbox - Form users click Checkboxes when they want to submit one or multiple selections from a set of options. e.g. Which of the following flavors of ice cream do you like?
Vanilla
Chocolate
Strawberry
Coconut
Pistachio
Rocky Road Radio - Form users click Radio Buttons when they want to indicate a single preference selection from a series of options. e.g. Which of the following is your favorite flavor of ice cream?
Chocolate
Vanilla
Strawberry
You can also use Images as the answer options.
Dropdown
-Displays a list menu of selection choices directly underneath it. This list menu remains visible until a single selection is made or it is dismissed by the user clicking elsewhere on the Form screen. This is similar to Radio but better used when you have more options to choose from. Date - Contents of this Field are formatted as mm/dd/yyyy. When a Form user clicks on the field, an interactive calendar pop-up is displayed.
When non-valid entries are made in the field (e.g. letters), and there is not a default of placeholder value defined, the system corrects the entry to a default of the current day's date. Date/Time - Contents of this Field are formatted as mm/dd/yyyy HH:MM PM. When a Form user clicks on the field, an interactive calendar pop-up and clock are displayed.
When non-valid entries are made in the field (e.g. letters), and there is not a default of placeholder value defined, the system corrects the entry to a default of the current day's date and the current time.
Email
-Text entered into this field must conform to standard email address format, i.e. name@domain.name
Website
-Text entered into this field must conform to standard URL address format, i.e. www.domain.name. The system will accept forward slashes plus further address specifications appended to the URL.
Phone Number
-This field only accepts an entry in the form of 10 digits, representing a US phone number, including area code, of xxx-xxx-xxxx.
Rating
-This is a star rating for a Contact. Use the Associate With Contact Field dropdown to dynamically assign whom the rating the Form user's response will be associated with. CAPTCHA - A CAPTCHA is a visual or audio perception task intended to distinguish human from machine input and is typically employed to thwart automated interaction with websites such as spam and abuse.
When a CAPTCHA Field is added to a Surefire Form, it will appear in the published Form as a checkbox with the words I am not a robot next to it.
When a CAPTCHA field is added, in order for a Form User to progress to the next Section or Page of the Form, they will need to click the checkbox which will, in turn, launch a pop up containing an interactive visual perception test (e.g. "Select all squares with pictures of cars").
Signature
-When a Form user clicks on this Field, they will be able to use their mouse like a stylus, by clicking and holding, to "handwrite" their signed name.
When the Field is active, two buttons appear below it: Clear (reset the Field) and Accept.
Statement
-Non-interactive Field. Used to place a text block on the Form that has been written by the Form author. Text Message Opt-in - This Field appears in a published Form as a checkbox with the words Text Message Opt-in next to it. A Form user selects the checkbox to indicate that they wish to receive Text Message communications sent from the Company.
Add Image Answers to Radio Button Form Fields Radio Button Form Fields, allow you to show images as an alternative to text for each selected option. When this option is selected, you will still have the option to identify your image selections with text. This text label and the value must be one and the same.
Refer to "Field Labels versus Values" earlier in this article for a description of this concept.
For example in the Question/Label "Which of the following is your favorite flavor of ice cream," instead of seeing the words "Chocolate," "Vanilla," and "Strawberry" next to three separate radio buttons, you could choose to upload image files of Chocolate, Vanilla, and Strawberry ice cream. Furthermore, should you decide to, you could additionally enter text labels (say "Chocolate," "Vanilla," and "Strawberry") for each image.
Then, in the published Form, users would simply click on the image corresponding to their preference. Instead of seeing a black dot in the middle of a circle (i.e. a selected radio button) next to their preference, the system outlines their selected image in color and a checkmark is displayed in the image's upper right-hand corner.
Use images to define Radio Button selection options:
Access the Details pop up screen for the Radio Button Form Field you want to use images for.
The third option down from the top is Image Options, set this to Yes.
You will now be presented with an additional option switch, Show Image Labels, set this to Yes if you want to have a text label corresponding to each option selection's value to appear below each image.
Under the Options* section of the Details screen, for each Selection Option (i.e. Radio Button), click the Choose Image button.
You can either use an existing image or upload a new one:
Existing Image, present in Surefire:
Locate the image through any combination of navigating through the Asset Browser Folders, Sorting the Asset Browser Table by Column or by Using the Search function
Click the checkbox next to the image you want to use and then click Apply in the lower right corner of the Asset Browser pop up
Add new image
Click Upload Image at the top of the pop-up.
In the ensuing New Image Asset pop up, designate:
The folder where you want the image to be stored in Surefire The Image Asset Name
A Description of the image (optional)
Click Add Image.
Click Select Image File.
A File Selection screen appears where you can navigate through your local system's files to the image you want to use. Only PNG, GIF, JPG, & JPEG files can be selected.
A preview of your selected image appears where, in the cases of images that are larger than 2.81" x 2.81" (562px x 562px), you can re-center and re-size a selection of a sub-section of the image.
Select Save Image.
Select Add Image.
In the Asset Browser window, locate the image file and click on the checkbox to its left.
Click the Apply button in the lower right-hand corner of the Asset Browser pop up window.
Edit the Value Field to reflect what text data will be submitted to Surefire when this Radio Button is selected in a published Form. If Show Image Labels has been set to Yes (see step 3 above), then whatever text entered here will appear below the image for this Radio Button Form Field in the published Form.
It is recommended that you use images of at least a 185px x 185px size as in desktop view the system will scale up anything smaller, which will cause some pixelation.

Marketing
Forms
Add Contact and Product Form Fields
Add Contact and Product Form Fields Contact and Product Fields are fields that can be added to Forms that correspond to actual fields.
You can create two scenarios:
New Contact Completes Form - A new Lead or Contact is created and populated with whatever fields were completed on the Form
Existing Contact Completes Form - If you send an Existing Contact a link to a Form (e.g. for a survey or maybe you are collecting additional Lead or Product information), the new information they submit to the form will be appended to their Existing Contact Record
There are settings on your Form where you can dictate how to handle Existing Contact Form Submissions.
Contact Form Fields
When you add a Contacts Field element, the Details screen is generated there are two fields:
Select Contact - When a Form user submits data into this Form Field, it will be associated in Surefire with the Contact or Contact Relationship selected here.
In addition to the available default selections of Primary Contact and Spouse, when a Product has been associated with the Form, any Deal Team Members defined for that Product will also appear as available Contact Type selections. Contact Form Field - Select from the list of all Contact Fields in (e.g. Contact First Name or Contact Phone - Home
). Any Custom Fields you have made for Contacts are also available.
Once you have selected a Contact Form Field type and for which Contact any Form user-provided response data will be submitted into Surefire, you can then define how the Field will appear and function in your Form by editing the Field's settings and parameters.
Certain Field parameter and setting options (e.g. Question/LabelField, Field type, Field Options etc.) are automatically selected depending on which Contact Form Field type you've selected.
Product Form Fields
Product Field only appears as an available Form element when a Product has been associated with the Form you are building, either when the Form was created, or by going to the Configure Your Form tab.
When you select a Product Fields element, you are presented with a Details screen.
You must select which Product Field you want to add. Product Fields were defined when the Product you've associated with this Form was originally setup in Surefire.
Once you have selected for which Product Field type any Form data will be submitted into Surefire, you can then define how the Field will appear and function in your Form by editing the Field's settings and parameters.
Certain Field parameter and setting options (e.g. Question/LabelField, Field type, Field Options etc.) are automatically selected depending on which Product Field type you've selected.
Review Add Form Fields for additional information.

Marketing
Forms
Add a Form Transition
A Transition provides instructions, setup by a form's author, which tells a Form where to direct the user next. It directs the user that completes a Form Section or Form Page by either filling out Form Fields or by clicking a Form navigation button such as Next or Back.
Transition Logic
To ensure that users get to the end of filling out a Section or Page and the system knows exactly where to go next, the following logic rules must be observed:
Every Form Page must have a Transition defined for it (unless each and every Section on that Page has its own Transition defined).
If a Page does not have a Transition defined for it, then each and every Section on that page must have a Transition defined for it.
If any Section on a Form Page has a Transition defined for it, then no Transition can be defined for the Page. This is because a Page Transition could conflict with the Section Transition, thereby confusing the system as to where (i.e. to what field) the Form user should be directed to next.
Form Transition Visual Indicators
In the Form build area, to the left of each Page or Section header, you'll see Label Squares. In addition to indicating a Page or Section's placement order in the form, by employing the following visual cues, these Squares also indicate what Transitions, if any, have been defined for that page or section:
The Label Square for a Page that does not have a transition defined for it will appear outlined in green.
When a Label Square is pink, a transition has been either applied to (i.e. a Transition defined earlier in the Form points to this section or page) or configured for that Section or Page (i.e. the system has been directed to point a Form user to somewhere else in the Form upon completion of this section or page).
An arrow in the Upper Left of a pink Label Square indicates that a Transition configured earlier in the Form points to this page or section; An arrow in the Lower Right indicates that this page or section has a Transition configured pointing to a page or section later in the Form.
When you hover your mouse pointer over a pink Label Square, it will expand to show you Transition details (e.g. "Jumps to [Page or Page/Section number]" and/or "Comes from [Page or Page/Section number]")
Form Page Transitions
A Form Page Transition dictates where in the Form a Form user is sent after they have filled out the minimum required fields on that Page and have clicked the "Next" navigation button at the bottom.
The last page of a Form does not have a Transition defined for it
The first page of a Form will not have a "Back" Transition option
"Next" and "Back" buttons can be re-labeled with different words (e.g. "Continue" instead of "Next," or really any other word you want)
Because of the possibility of conflict, a Page Transition cannot be defined if any Section on that Page has any sort of transition defined for or to it
Configure Transitions
In the Form Build area, click either the Label Square to the left of the Page Break or the Transition icon that appears on the Page Break when you mouse over it.
The Configure Form Page Transitions screen is generated. .
Configure Form Page Transitions
The configure page transitions screen is where you define your Form Page Transition.
In this screen you can: add General options
Jump to selection drop down menu.
Remove Transition
General Options
Check the Override default 'Next' button and Override default 'Previous' button checkboxes to reveal a text field where you can re-label the Next and Back buttons with different words such as Continue instead of Next, orany other word you want to use.
The first page of a Form will have only a "...default 'Next'..." option, and the last page of a Form will have only a "...default 'Previous'..." button.
If "Allow user to go back" is checked, then a navigation button allowing the user to go back to the previous page or section (which page or section that is will depend on what transition brought them to this page) will be present.
If unchecked, no such button will appear, and a Form user will, upon being navigated to this page, not be able to return to previous pages or sections.
Jump to Selection Drop Down Menu
Choose where a Form user will be sent to upon completing the minimum required fields on the current page.
Form Section Transitions
A Form Section Transition dictates where in the Form a Form user is sent after they have filled out the minimum required fields on that section and have clicked the "Next" navigation button at the bottom.
Adding a transition to a Section means that that Section's contents will be displayed on their own screen as a user progresses through the Form (since the section will have its own navigation button(s)).
To configure a Transition for a Section, in your Form Build area, click either the Label Square to the left of the Section Break or the Transition icon that appears on the Section Break when you mouse over it. This takes you to the Configure Section Transitions Pop Up.
General, Jump To options and Remove Transition options behave the same way as they do for Form Page Transitions.
Add Conditions to Form Section Transitions
For Form Section Transitions, you can add "IF [operator] VALUE then JUMP TO [a destination]" conditions to fields in the section.
Applying conditions allows much more intelligent direction of how Form users are navigated through your Form because it can be based on the responses they supply in Form fields.
Multiple conditions can be applied to the same field within the section.
Click on the Add Condition button, located in the upper center of the Configure Form Section Transitions screen.
Use the drop-down menus to define:
Which field in the section you want to apply a condition to Define an operator
Section_Transition_Conditional_Operator_Drop_Down_Expanded.png
Define a Value
Define the destination in the Form the user will be navigated to if the condition is met

Marketing
Forms
Add Form Pages and Sections
In order for Forms to be easy to read, understand and navigate through, it's important to visually group related content (i.e. labels and fields) into Form Sections. Form Sections are then in turn contained in Form Pages.
Any Form Page must contain at least one Form Section (since Fields must reside within Sections).
A Form user will be presented with one Form Page on their screen at a time and will have to click navigation buttons to move between Pages.
Upon completing a Form Section and/or Form Page, the configuration of that Section or Page's Transition will determine which Form Section or Page the user is directed to next.
Add Pages and Sections
By default, a new Form will have a First Page and Final Page, each will contain one section.
Pages and Sections are added to a Form by dragging them from the Elements area on the right side of the Form Build screen and dropping them into the Build area.
Page and Section Details
When you drop a Page or Section, you are presented with that Page or Section's Details screen where you must provide the Page or Section with a Title and, optionally, a Description. Both Titles and Descriptions are displayed on the published Form.
Placement and Labeling
Form Pages and Form Sections are always labeled, both in the Build area as well as on the title bars of their Details pop up screens, to indicate that Page or Section's placement order on the Form.
The following format is used to outline Pages, Sections and Fields (see image below):
Pages
Roman numerals (e.g. I, II, III, IV)
The final page is always labelled End
Section
Whole numbers (e.g. 1, 2, 3, 4)
Fields
Lowercase letters (e.g. a, b, c, d)
Form Sections and Pages can be moved in your Form layout by dragging and dropping them in your design. Placement order labels are updated automatically whenever a move occurs.

Forms
Configure a Form
Access the Configure Form tab to edit a Form's overall attributes.
Here, you can also make changes to some of the initial settings that were selected and/or applied when the Form was originally created.
To Configure a Form:
Go to Marketing, Forms to display all the Form-type assets saved in your media library.
You can narrow the list of Forms that's displayed, specify the folder that includes the Form you want to favorite.
Either by sorting the table or by using the Search function, locate the Form you want to configure
Select the Form Name
On the Form Build screen, select the Configure tab.
The Configure tab is divided into two sections, each devoted to a different class of configuration type: General and Restrictions.
General Section Name - How this form is identified in Surefire. Description - A short sentence describing your Form. For internal use in Surefire. Folder - Where a Form is saved in your Surefire organizational hierarchy determines which users will have access to it. Product - You can optionally associate a Form with a Product. By doing so, you will be able to add Elements and Contact Fields to the Form that are specific to that Product. Tags - Tags are unique identifiers that can be added, like labels, in order to further categorize a Form. Tagging lets you easily sort, filter, and associate Forms with campaigns designed around specific interests and actions. A Form can have an unlimited number of Tags. Assign Point Values - Choose whether or not to assign point values to submitted forms. Override Existing Contact Type - For data submitted into the Contact Form Field "Contact Info - Contact Type," if, when the data is merged into Surefire, it turns out that there is already an existing, duplicate Contact record, this option tells the system whether the Contact Type submitted in the form should replace the Contact Type already present in Surefire or not.
Send Email Responses
-Here, the Form's author chooses whether or not Surefire sends additional email responses received via this Form.
If Yes is selected, this Form's author can then, optionally, also select additional roles to be cc'd on those email responses. E.g., whether Surefire CCs all "admins" and "marketing admins" on all submissions received via this Form.
If No is selected the form will send the responses only to the user.
Restrictions Section Submission Approval - Refers to the automation of data submitted by Forms being entered into Surefire. In some cases, you'll want data submitted from Forms to be entered into Surefire automatically. In other cases, you'll want to review and approve the data first before it's entered into the Surefire system.
All Form Submissions and related Reviews are done from Marketing, Forms Reporting. Org Default - Whether or not Form data submission is automatic or requires approval is not set for this Form, but rather will depend on the Form Submission Policies defined for each organizational unit in Surefire.
All form submissions must be approved before being added as contacts - Addition of any data submitted from this Form to Surefire will be pending until it is reviewed and marked approved from the Forms Reporting Pending tab.
Only public form submissions must be approved before being added as contacts - Currently all Responses are Public. This functionality will be applicable once Surefire includes a Secure Forms feature: Data submitted from "Secure" iterations of this Form will be entered into Surefire automatically.
All form submissions are added to the contact database immediately - Any data submitted from this Form will be entered into Surefire automatically, with no review or approval required.

Marketing
Forms
Distribute a Form
Access the Distribute a Form tab to generate a code that you can use to embed the Form (via link to Surefire ) on a website or anywhere else you can insert HTML.
Generate Embed Code
Go to Marketing, Forms to display all the Forms in your Media Library.
Optionally, in order to narrow the list of Forms that's displayed, specify the folder that includes the Form you want to distribute
Locate the Form you want to distribute; use either sorting the table or the Search function.
Select the Form Name.
Select the Distribute tab.
Use the Embed a form on field, to generate the embed HTML code by:
Entering an asterisk (*) wild card, which will allow the embed code to be posted anywhere;
Or, if you want to specifically limit which domain a Form can be accessed from entering a specific domain name
Select Add.
Click </>Get the Code to initiate a window containing the HTML code you can use to embed this Form.
Select Copy to Clipboard to copy the code.
Paste the code to a website or anywhere you can insert HTML.
The embed code itself does not change if you specify for which domain(s) the Surefire system should grant access to the Form. Rather, specifying a domain or domains indicates to Surefire that it needs to confirm that access requests are coming from those domains before granting access to the Form.
Wild Card vs. Specific Domain
Generally, you will always want to enter an asterisk (
*
) wild card in the Embed a Form on field when generating your Form embed code. This is because using the asterisk tells Surefire that it should grant access to the Form regardless of what domain or website the Form resides on.
The only time you would enter a specific domain name in the Embed a Form on field is when you want to completely control what domain a Form can be embedded on.
For Forms used on internal Company websites, the use cases for this type of stricter security are likely rare. However, if you are sharing Forms with outside partners for lead generation or other purposes, you might want to give them an embed code that can't be shared or posted anywhere other than the agreed upon website.

Forms that have been Favorited are displayed here. This is useful when you have a large number of Forms in Surefire with only a few generating most of the activity.
You can view the following data and perform the following actions from the Favorite Forms tab: Total Submissions - Shows the total number of Form Submissions. By clicking on the number, you are taken to the Submissions Summary for this Form.

Date Submitted
Name - The name of the person who submitted the Form.
User
Source - The domain that the Form was embedded on Points
Additionally, by clicking on the [Date Submitted] you can further drill down into the specific answers the Contact submitted.
This Response Summary provides the following information: Form Info - Includes Form Name, URL and Source Type (e.g. Embedded) Result Info - Date/time of submission as well as IP address
Captured Data
-Summary of all the fields on the form as well as their Captured Value
Most Recent Submission
The Date/Time of submission and Contact who submitted the most recent Form entry.
Answer Breakdown
This is an aggregate summary of all Form questions that are of a data type that can be properly summarized, such as Dropdown, Radio, and Checkbox. (In other words, it can't summarize field types like Text or Number.)
The Chosen/Total column displays the number of submissions for that answer over the total number of Form Submissions and the Percentage column then displays this as a percent of overall answers.

This Year
This Month
This Week
Last Week
Last Month
Today
Yesterday

-The contact that submitted the Form Form - The name and link to the Form Source - The domain that the Form was submitted from Location - The IP address that submitted the Form with a link to a Google Map of the location

The main purpose of this section is for you to review and Approve or Reject the submissions. View - Select View to see the detailed Form answers Approve - Click the Green Checkmark to Approve the Form Submission and move the Contact into your Surefire database. At this point, any Rules or Workflows that might be triggered by the Contact's attributes will be executed. Reject - If the Form looks like a bogus Lead, spam, a duplicate, or otherwise undesirable, click the Red X to Reject the Form Submission. This quarantines the record in the Rejected tab.
Approved
Any Form Submissions that you Approved can be viewed here. Also, any Submissions for Forms where the Submission Approval setting has been configured to:
All form submissions are added to the contact database immediately
Will immediately enter Surefire and be visible in the Approved tab. You can view the same information as from the Pending tab as well as utilize the same date filters.
Rejected
Any Form Submissions that you Rejected can be viewed here. If you change your mind, you can also Approve a Rejected Submission.

Forms
Capture Single Property Site Data In Forms
You can capture the purchase price, the address, or the zip code of a Single Property Site when the SPS form on that site is submitted.
This could be helpful for segmenting your contacts by leads over or under a certain purchase price. Such as leads who are interested in properties with purchase prices of 500,000 or greater. Or you may want to segment your contacts by shopping in a given zip code. Such as leads who are interested in properties with zip codes 98037 or 98036. Or even by city, like contacts shopping in Atlanta.
To start gathering that data you will need to create 5 custom fields.
SPS_prop_address_1
SPS_prop_city
SPS_prop_state
SPS_prop_zip
SPS_prop_price
Create and Add Custom Fields
Go to CRM Settings, Custom Fields.
Select Short text in Field Types and drag it to the Custom Fields section.
In the Label field enter SPS_prop_address_1.
Select Save.
Repeat this with SPS_prop_city and SPS_prop_zip.
Select States field and drop it in the Custom fields section name it: SPS_prop_state.
The Purchase Price field is a Currency field, drag the currency field type to your list of types and name it: SPS_prop_price.
Once the fields are established, you edit your existing SPS form or create a new form which you will embed on your SPS.
Go to Marketing, Forms.
Locate the form you want to add SPS addresses.
Select select Edit.
In the forms editor, select Contact Fields.
In the Which Contact? select Primary Contact.
In the Contact Form field, scroll to Custom field - SPS_prop_address_1.
In the Question/Label* field select SPS_prop_address_1, right-click and copy the value.
Chang Visibility field to Hidden.
In the Variable name field, right-click and paste SPS_prop_address_1.
You may have to click on what you pasted to get it to stick.
Select Apply.
Repeat this process for the remaining custom fields you have created.
Select Save for your form.
You can now embed your code on your Single Property Site.
If you've edited the SPS form that is already live on the site, the changes that you made to the form will appear and you do not need to re-embed the form.

Add Signature Block for Co-branding
Once you have set up your Co-brand Partner, your next step is to add their Signature Block to any outgoing email deployments that you are co-branding with them.
Your co-brand partners Signature Block is added next to yours in the email footer.
Open the Email Content Collection you want to use.
In Cobranded, select Yes.

Alternatively, choose an Email Layout where you have already inserted the Email Signature merge field.
Select Save Media.
To edit your signatures both personal and co-brand navigate to My Account, My Profile and click on Signature Blocks.
Now, when you send a Content Collection to a Contact who is associated with a Co-Brand Partner, they will receive the co-branded version of your signature.
Any Contact without a Co-Brand Partner will receive your Standard Email Signature.
