Add a Co-Brand Partner
Create a Co-Brand Email Signature
When working with a Co-Brand Partner, it's important that both parties have their own unique email signature so customers are clear that both partners are working with them.
Add A Co-Branded Email Signature
Go to My Account , My Profile.
Verify the Co-brand option is selected in a Content Collection, your Co-Brand Partner's signature is displayed alongside yours for your outgoing Email Deployments.
Select Signature Blocks tab in your profile summary.
View your Signature Block. If you have a combined Signature Block with your Co-Brand Partner it is available.
Your Co-Brand Signature Block lists your Email Signature side by side along with your Co-Brand Partner's Email Signature. The information in the Signature Blocks can be inherited from your company's Default Email Signature or can be customized by the user.
Edit the Co-Brand Signature Block
You can edit the Signature Blocks with a standard HTML editor interface allowing you to add text or merge fields into your email signature.
Select Edit Co-Brand Email Signature.
Click inside the box to put your cursor on the line just above where you would like to merge a new field.
Press the return key to add a new entry.
Using Merge Fields, you can add additional information fields to your email signature.
Choose or search for a field you want to merge from the Merge Field list.
Select the field from the list you want to edit.
The new field is added to your Co-Brand Partner's email signature.
Click Save Changes.
Standard Email Signature vs. Co-Brand Signature
Your email signature will always appear in any Content Collection where you use the Signature Block - Email merge field.
Using this merge field, your Co-Brand Partner's email signature appears on any Content Collection where you set the Co-Brand option to Yes.
Any contacts that are associated with your Co-Brand Partner will then see both signatures in the footer of your email deployments; any contacts without a Co-Brand Partner will see your standard email signature.
In order to co-brand a landing page, use the {{Signature Block - Email}} Merge field in both the email used to distribute the landing page and the landing page itself.

Referral Partner Deal Tracking
When viewing a Contact Record, you can review the Deals that the contact has been a Deal Team Member on by going to the Referral Tracker tab. This is useful when you want to see the Deal history of one of your Co-Brand Partners.
The Referral Tracker tab displays a list of Deals, presented in a sortable table, that can be filtered so that results are limited by Product and Deal Team Member Slot.
You can view a summary list of all your Co-Brand Partners by going to Contacts, View All Contacts then filtering by Co-Brand Partners.
Alternatively, you can navigate to Contacts, Referral Tracker to see a list of your Top Transaction Partners or your Top Referral Partners.
Review Deals a Contact has been a Deal Team Member
Go to a specific contact's
Contact Record.
Click, select Referral Tracker.
This generates a summary table of all the Deals the Contact is a Deal Team Member on.
Use the Product list to select for which Product you want to see the Deals where this Contact was a Deal Team Member.
Alternatively, you can enter a Date Range in which this Contact was added as a Deal Team Member. The results listed in the table are limited to that date range.
Use the check boxes to select which Deal Team Member slots you want to be included in the table.
Results listed in the table are limited to Deals where this Contact was added into one those slots.
The sortable table is populated with an entry for each Deal associated with the Product, selected in step 3, where this Contact was a Deal Team Member (added within your selected Date Range and filling the selected Deal Team Slot(s)).
Each entry in the table includes the following details: Name - First and Last name of the contact for that Deal, hyperlinked to their contact record in Surefire Association - Name of deal team slot(s) filled for this deal. An example of where this contact might fill more than one Team Member Slot on a single Deal might be where they were both a buying and a selling agent on the deal Closing Date - The date the deal was closed Address - Deal address Product Metric - Varies by Product. An example might be for a Mortgage product where this field would be the Loan Rate Amount - Field value, if any, for the sum field for this product. An example might be for a Mortgage product where this field would be the Loan Amount

Workflows function similarly to Rules in that they represent a series of CRM Actions that can be automated, either immediately or on a fixed schedule.
The main difference with Workflows is that, unlike Rules, on their own they cannot be automatically triggered with Conditions and Criteria. Instead, a Contact must be added to a Workflow in two ways:
Via a Rule Action
Manually by User from Contact Record
To Create a Workflow:
Go to Marketing, Workflows.
Select Create a Workflow button.
Add:
Name (required)
Library Folder Location (required)
Description
Handbook Description
Product
If you select a Product to associate with the Workflow, it will expose the selected Product's field when using the Update Contact Data Action.
After you add Actions, select Create Workflow .
The Workflow becomes active.
If you need to make changes, you can select View & Manage Your Workflow.

Marketing
Workflows
Add Actions to your Workflow
Once you have created your Workflow, your final step is to define what Actions you want Surefire to take when a contact is added to the workflow.
The current list of Actions is similar to those for Rule Actions:
Add a Tag
Add a Task
Add Sale Process
Deploy Content
Deploy Print Content
Remove Tag
Send Data Via Webhook
Update Contact Data
Update Contact Type/Lifecycle Status
Update Lead Score
To add an Action to a Workflow, Select Add an Action button. There are no limits to the number of actions you can add and all actions can be set to occur immediately or can be set for varied times into the future.
Action Timing
Each Action has the same Timing Setting Options. This tells Surefire when you want the Action to occur:
Delay For Static Date
Dynamic Date
Day of Week
Delay For By default, the system will run the Action automatically with the Timing Type set to Delay for 0 Minutes. If you want to delay the Action, you can assign a whole number (e.g. 1, 3, 10, etc.) and choose a time increment type from:
Minutes
Hours
Days
Static Date
This Action Timing option simply sets a specific date and time for the action to occur, independent of any other dependencies, with one exception: Year. The year setting is relational and is based on when the Workflow is run.
Dynamic Date
This Action Timing option sets a Contact-attribute-specific date for the action to occur.
The currently available contact-attribute-specific options are Contact Birthday and Contact Spouse Birthday.
Time of Day for the deployment is static and manually set.
The year setting is relational and is based on when the Workflow was created.
Day of Week
This Action Timing option specifies for that action to occur at a static, manually set time of day on a selected day of the week, X-number of weeks after the rule runs.
Action Summary
If you have added any Actions with delayed timing, the Action Summary section shows all Actions with their respective timing:
Add a Tag
When adding a Tag, type the name of the Tag in the Tags box. When you locate the tag you are looking for, select it from the list.
After you click Apply, the Workflow adds the Tag to whatever Contact it applies to.
You cannot Create a Tag from this section. If you want to apply a new Tag with this Workflow, you will first need to Create a New Tag.
Add a Task
You can use a Workflow to assign a Task to yourself or another User in Surefire. This will appear in the My Tasks section of the Calendar for the assigned User.
After entering a Name and Details, you can complete the following other Action fields:
Priority
-Choose between High, Medium and Low Priority for your Task.
Days Until Due (required)
-This is the number of days from when it is created that the Task is marked due. 0 indicates it is due the day the Task is created, 1 is the day after it was created and so on.
This date is not the date the Workflow is started but the date the Task is created.
Chronological example:
Workflow starts (9/1)
Action is set for a Task to be created 3 days after Workflow starts (9/4)
The Task Days Until Due is set to 2 (9/6)
In the example the Task Due date is set to 9/6 as that is two days after the Task Creation (9/4) and the Workflow Start date (9/1). Activity - Select between the Activity Type options of To Do, Phone and Other. Assignee (required) - The most critical element is assigning the Task to the appropriate User. You can select from these options:
Contact Owner
-This assigns the Task to whatever User owns the Contact at the time the Task is created. Specific User - Choose a User from a list of all Company Users from Companies you have access to. Team Member - If you have Team Member Slots created in your Company you can select from among them here. The Team Member Slot will always be the one associated with the Owner of the Contact on the Workflow. If a triggering User has an empty Team Member Slot, the Task will be skipped.
Add Sales Process
You can use a Workflow to trigger a change in the Sales Process and Sales Process Phases for a Deal that a Contact has.
Select the Sales Process and the Sales Phase that you want the Workflow to set the Deal to. Deploying Content as a Workflow Action is very similar to Creating a Deployment in the Deployment Center only without the Audience Builder element.
You are presented with a version of the Media Library from which you can follow these steps to Deploy Content Collection.
Navigate or search to find the Content Collection you want.
Under the Media Type column, click the Media icon to Preview. This is optional.
Click Select next to Content Collection to use.
In the Available Media Types section, select Use under the Media Type you want to Deploy.
For Content Collections with multiple Media Types, you can only Deploy a single type per Action. If you want to Deploy more than one Media Type from the same Collection you need to create a separate Action.
The following steps are specific to different media types. You currently cannot Deploy Social as an Action.
Email Recipient Type - Choose from among the following to receive the email:
Contact
Contact Relationships (e.g. Spouse, Co-Brand) Specific Contact - This may allow other Users running this Workflow to send Deployments to your selected contact. Team Member - If a triggering User has an empty Team Member Slot, the Task will be skipped. CC Recipient - You can use the same Recipient selection options above to choose to copy someone on the Deployment. After you choose the CC Recipient, click the Add button. You can continue to add more than one CC Recipient. To remove a CC, click the Red Trash Can icon. Sender - Choose to send the Email from Contact Owner or a Team Member.
Text Message Recipient Type - Utilize the same options as for Email. Text Message Number Priority - For Users with more than one Text Message Number, this Priority setting allows you to rank the order in which you would prefer the Text Message Numbers be used to send the Deployment.
Text Message Options Do not deploy overflow texts - Using this option, if you exceed your daily number of Text Message sends, the overflow will not be sent.
Deploy my other Text Message numbers in order of priority - This option will use your alternate Text Message numbers in their specified order to handle any overflow.
Deploy Print Content
The action option to Deploy Print Content is only available if Print is turned on for company use. If allowed, this action works the same as Deploy Content, but when clicking on the Media Library you are only presented with the Postcard collection options to choose from.
Remove Tag
To remove a Tag, type the name of the tag in the Remove Tags box. When you locate the applicable tag select it on the list. You can also remove a tag(s) through category. Select Remove By Tag Category and select the tag category. Then select Apply.
The workflow is now set to remove the designated tag from the Contact once the conditions that trigger the workflow are met.
Send Data Via Webhook
Webhook must be turned on and properly configured by your account administrator in order for this action to successfully process. If unavailable, webhook actions are skipped.
Update Contact Data
This Action allows you to update any Contact Field with a new value. After you select the Field to Update, you will have two options for the Value Type of the Field: Field Value - Choose another Contact Field from the Value From Existing Field dropdown. This will update the previously selected field with the current value of your newly selected Existing Field. Manual Value - Enter in a value to update for any Text or Number fields. For Dropdown and other fields with preset values, choose from the existing options.
You can also add more than one Field to Update from within the same action by clicking the Add More.
Delete any additional updates by clicking and confirming.
Update Contact Type/Lifecycle Status
You can change the Contact Type and/or Lifecycle Status using this option. You have two settings on this Action: Contact Type (required) - Choose from the dropdown the Contact Type to change to. Lifecycle Status - Depending on the Contact Type selected, you will have available all of the Lifecycle Statuses associated with that Type. Choose the one to update to.
If you just want to change the Lifecycle Status, select the Contact Type that the Contact should already be in and then set the Lifecycle Status.
Update Lead Score
You can use a Workflow to automatically update a Lead Score on a Lead. Simply use the slider to indicate the amount that you wish to increase/decrease the Lead Score by.
Remember, this is the number of points you are changing the score by, not the actual Lead Score.
For example:
A Lead has a Lead Score of 25
A Contact is added to a Workflow with an Action of Update Lead Score by 10
The New Lead Score is 35 (25 + 10); not 10
Workflow Action Views
As you add Actions to your Workflow, you will be able to see them summarized in two views:
Action Summary Table
Workflow Pipeline View
The Pipeline view will show all of your actions in a timeline while the Action Summary Table will list the details of each Action step in the order they were entered.
The only costs that are associated with a Workflow is for physical mail. All digital deployments are free. Any Text Message costs are separate and are not summarized here.

View and Manage Workflows
You can view and manage all of your Company's current published and paused Workflows by going to Marketing, Workflows.
Workflows are presented in a summary table.
Additional columns are:
Status
Published - Live Worflow
Paused - Workflow that has been Paused so that it is not currently running. Any future Actions on this Workflow will not execute. Library - Indicates where in the Company folder structure the Workflow is saved and is accessible Live - Counts the number of Contacts who have been added to the Workflow. Clicking on the number will take you to a Workflow Member Summary (see View Workflow Member section below) Actions - The total number of Actions that are part of the Workflow are totaled here Cost - Any associated costs with Workflow Actions (usually for Direct Mail) are summed here
Search and Filters
You can search for any Workflows by Name or Tag. You can also Filter by Status.
View Folders
By default, you will view all of the Workflows that reside in the top Company you belong to. To drill down to see Workflows saved on the Company level, click the Toggle Folder View to see a Company Library View.
View Workflow Members
By clicking on the count under the Live column for a Workflow, you can view what Contacts have been added to the Workflow.
You can review or perform the following actions: View Upcoming & Past Actions - Click on a Contact name to view the Past and Upcoming Actions for this Workflow Add New Contact to Workflow - Click the Add Contacts button to Add Contacts to the Workflow Remove Contact - Click the menu option on the row to Remove a Contact from the Workflow which will terminate any Upcoming Actions for this Contact
Added
-The Date you Added the Contact to a Workflow
Start Date
-The Date where the first Action occurred, which could be later than the Added Date
View Workflows on Contacts
From the Activities tab of a Contact Record, you can view what Workflows they have been added to.
Edit, Clone, Pause/Resume
From the main Workflow page, you can select at the end of the row to manage Workflows.
The following menu options are available:
Edit
Clone
Pause
Delete
Pause and Resume
If you have a live Workflow that you want to stop working, you can use the Pause option in the menu. You can also go to the Workflow Detail for a Workflow and select Pause. When Paused, no Actions will execute for any Contacts who are on the Workflow.
When the Workflow Status is currently Paused, this option changes to Resume.
You can select it to have the Workflow resume running under its current conditions.
While a Workflow is Paused, not only will no Actions run, but if it is Resumed, the Workflow will not go back and search for any Contacts that should have Run while Paused. All of these Actions will behave a Status of Skipped and can be viewed as such on a Contact's Activities tab.
Grace Period
While Actions will be skipped while on Pause, there is a small 30-minute Grace Period window for when you Resume a Paused Workflow. The system will run all Actions that were scheduled for the preceding 30 minutes.
Example: You have a Paused workflow with the following Actions set for Today:
Send Email #1 at 2:00 PM
Send Email #2 at 2:30 PM
If you Resume the Workflow at 2:45 PM, Email #1 (meant to run 45 minutes ago) will be skipped while Email #2 (meant to run 15 minutes ago) will Deploy as it is within the Grace Period.
Save and Publish
While you are building a Workflow, once you click Create Workflow you will Publish the Workflow and it is live. If you still have more work to do on your Workflow, you can immediately Pause the Workflow and then Edit to continue making changes.
When the Workflow is ready, select Resume.

Marketing
Workflows
Nudge Workflow
A nudge workflow is a workflow with one focus, to get a response from the contact. The workflow continues until the contact replies via text.
The reason why nudge workflows are used is to ensure that the lead or contact is engaging with you before you begin a longer drip workflow.
A nudge workflow could work like this:
Prospect fills out a form and becomes a lead.
Instantly, text message 1 goes out to the lead: “Thank you for filling out our form, would today at 4 work for a call?”
No response
The next day, text message 2 goes out the lead: “Good morning! So sorry we didn’t get to touch base yesterday would today work for you?”
No response
3 more days go by, text message 3 goes out to the lead: “Hi again, so sorry to bother you, I just want to make sure I answered your home buying questions, are you available today to talk?”
The contact replies: “I am, I’m sorry for the late reply. I was on vacation with spotty service.”
Now, this lead is engaged, and a regular drip workflow can begin.
If we would have started the regular drip workflow before the contact got into communication with us, it could have felt impersonal.

Marketing
Workflows
Text Messaging in Master Settings
If you have purchased any Text Messaging Numbers for use, you can manage their settings from the Text Messages tab under CRM Settings, Master Settings.
The screen is divided into several sections:
Allow Text Messages to be sent to Text Message Subscriptions
Text Message Opt-Out Frequency Control
Zapier - Assume Text Message Opt-In (trusted source)
Allow Text Messages to Be Sent To As a way to limit the potential ramifications of unsolicited marketing by text, some organizations may want to limit which phone numbers Surefire users are able to send text messages. Surefire provides the following options: All contacts not unsubscribed - This selection will allow Surefire users to send text messages to all contacts except those that have opted out by replying STOP to a text received from Surefire.
Only contacts who have opted in - This selection will allow Surefire users to send text messages only to contacts who have opted in to receive text messages via one of the three possible ways outlined below.
Ways to Opt-In
Form Opt-In
– Surefire has created the option to add the field for Text Message Opt-In to any custom form created by an organization. This field option provides the organization with the ability to capture Contact Opt-In’s with any form submission. This option is the only native way for the Surefire system to capture and monitor contacts that have opted into receiving text messages.
Data Import
– An Organization can create an import map in Data Management that is unique to contact opt-ins.
Standard dedupe protocols should be considered so as not to create duplicates should the list include existing contacts.
Zapier
– An organization can set up a Zap that will assume text message opt-in for all contact mobile phone numbers added or edited in this manner based on specified conditions. Those users and conditions that are set up using this method will be listed in the Zapier – Assume Text Message Opt-in (trusted source) section.
Text Message Opt-Out Frequency Control
This section allows your organization to choose a standard Opt-Out layout/footer to be used for all text messages. In addition, the frequency for how often the Opt-Out layout/footer will appear for text messages can be set. This frequency control is intended to eliminate the Opt-Out language appearing with every single outbound message. This can be especially useful if you text a particular contact frequently.
To set the frequency, select the number of days between appearances of the Opt-Out layout in any text message. The Opt-Out layout will appear in the first message sent and then not appear again until at least the selected number of days has elapsed. For example, if 10 days is selected, the first text message will contain the Opt-Out layout. Then, that layout will not appear again until at least the 11th day from the initial message, no matter the number of messages sent to that contact in the intervening timeframe.
Text Message Subscriptions
This section provides a cumulative total of contacts who have actively opted in or opted out using one of the above-described methods.
Once populated, the quantity number can be clicked on and opened to view a table showing the username, contact name, mobile phone number, and date/time added to the list.

Implement Calculator-Based Prospect Workflows
The Calculator-Based Purchase and Refi Prospect workflows contain a series of email and text communications aimed at educating prospective borrowers and persuading them to take action. This is an admin only function.
English-language workflows are available to deploy over various timeframes.
Spanish versions are available in the 90-day timeframe for refi prospects and 1-year timeframe for purchase prospects.
You can edit them to fit a schedule that suits your process.
They are located in the Public, Prospect Collections folder.
The following is a list of Best Practices to use in implementing the Calculator-Based Prospect Workflows and a list of email collections that contain landing pages. If you typically clone landing pages for your company, you’ll want to clone these emails then replace the links with your cloned landing pages.
Best Practices for Implementing a Prospect Workflow
Review each piece of included content. You can see them by going to the Media Library and searching Purchase Prospect Workflow, Refi Prospect Workflow, r Spanish or by downloading a PDF handbook of the workflow.
The Spanish workflows differ slightly from the English versions. To view the English translation of the Spanish Refi Prospect Workflow, click here. To view the English translation of the Spanish Purchase Prospect Workflow, click here.
If your company clones landing pages, be sure to clone the emails and replace all links with your cloned versions. See below for a list.
If you are using the Spanish workflows, check the landing pages to ensure the Spanish toggle is turned on for each. If one is not turned one, you can adjust it by using the configuration panel.
If you have created configuration panels to attach to any of these landing pages previously (either the public version or your cloned version), those configurations are carried over automatically.
You can make edits to the emails and text messages. Clone them, make your changes, and save. Edit the workflow to replace the public email or text message with your own.
After you’ve reviewed and updated the emails/text messages:
You’ll find the workflows in the Prospect Collections folder. All have calculator-based in the description, or you can type calculator in the search box to locate all options. You can narrow down to the Spanish versions by typing Spanish into the search box.
If you don’t allow users to access the Public folder, clone the workflow and put it in a folder your users can access.
If you have edits, clone and make your changes, including timing and collections to deploy. If you cloned emails, replace the public versions with your company versions.
Prepare rules so contacts can be assigned to the workflow. Typically, an “Activate Prospect Workflow” rule is used. If you have an existing one, edit it to point to your new workflow. You can give your users a choice of workflow by cloning it and editing one for the new workflow. If you do not currently have a rule, please reach out to the Help Desk.

Implement the Agent Workflows
The Agent Workflows are a series of events intended to introduce real estate agents to the benefits an LO can offer, specifically related to marketing through Surefire tools. The workflows include emails, phone calls and surveys. The print workflows also include two mailed postcards. The workflows last approximately 6 months.
There are four Agent Workflows in the Public, Referral Partner folder, covering print or digital-only and new or existing relationships.
The following is a list of Best Practices to use in implementing the Agent Workflows for your company and a checklist of included email collections that contain landing pages you may want to update to your cloned versions.
Best Practices for Implementing an Agent Workflow
Review each piece of included content carefully to ensure the information represents the way your company uses Surefire. You can see them by going to the Media Library and searching “Realtor Workflow” or by downloading a PDF handbook of the workflow.
The messages assume your company does the following:
Uses workflows, including prospect, credit repair, rent vs. own and trade-up buyer workflows
Allows cobranding on your emails and landing pages
Has a post-close workflow (the print messages assume your post-close workflow includes some mailed postcards)
Uses Text Messages according to a customer’s preference
Sends cobranded in-process videos during the loan process
If you choose, create a sample in-process video branded for your company and replace the general sample included in the collection titled
04 Agent Workflow – In Process Videos.
Create a rule to subscribe workflow recipients to your Markets in a Minute recurring deployment.
Review the Content Sharing Template 1 layout (saved in the Public folder—no subfolder). If necessary, clone and make changes, then switch to your cloned layout in each of the pieces.
Create a separate Opt-Out list for this workflow. This way, if a real estate agent unsubscribes from the workflow, they won’t be automatically unsubscribed from all marketing or transactional emails the LO sends.
Review Create an Opt Out List additional information.
If your company clones landing pages, be sure to replace all links in the emails with your cloned versions.

Graphic

Purchase Prospect Workflow – Neighborhood
Subject: You’re buying more than just a house, Name
Greeting: Take a look around before you choose your home, Name
When you’re looking for a home, remember that you are shopping for far more than a house. You’re also choosing your neighborhood.
Here are a few things to consider before you make an offer:
What will your commute be like? Don’t trust your favorite app on this one. Take the time to drive the route between the home and your place of work during rush hour.
Where will your children go for school or childcare? Are you happy with the available choices and their locations?
Consider the places you visit regularly—from the grocery store to medical offices to a house of worship. Will you have convenient options?
Look around at neighboring properties. Are yards well-kept and homes in good repair? Are more homes for rent or for sale in the neighborhood? Generally speaking, having more owners living in and caring for their homes is better for values.
How will you access utilities? Are there public options for water, sewer and trash collection?
And what about public safety? Is there a local police force or does the community rely on state troopers? Is there a full-time or volunteer fire department?
Remember that a neighborhood is not just a collection of homes. It’s also about the people who may become your neighbors. Don’t be bashful when it comes to introducing yourself to people outside their homes, in a local park or at the corner coffee shop. Ask them what they like and perhaps don’t like about living there.
Remember, it’s far easier to get a good sense of the neighborhood before you buy than to realize you may have made a mistake after closing!
Thank you for allowing me to send you information related to buying a home. Please reach out any time I can answer questions or be of service.
Purchase Prospect Workflow – Free Annual Credit Report Reminder and Credit Hints
Subject: Here are some things to do in preparation for a home purchase, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}
Greeting: Hi, Name!
Many of my clients who are preparing for a home purchase start thinking about sprucing up their credit score. After all, your credit score impacts the interest rate you secure on your home loan, which affects the amount of your monthly payment and the overall cost of your mortgage.
To keep your credit in top shape, please remember the following:
Do NOT close old credit accounts. Many homebuyers like to get their finances in order by paying off credit cards. If you do this, please keep the accounts open. The length of time you've used credit is important to your score. Keep your balances low. The percentage of available credit you use counts more toward your score than the total balances on your cards. While it's tempting to move all balances to one low-interest-rate card, you will get closer to the limit on the one card, and it could negatively impact your score. Opinions vary, but experts say you'll help your score by using only 10% to 30% of your available credit. Avoid new credit inquiries. Department store credit cards may save you 10% at purchase, but applying for one could cut points from your credit score and cost you thousands in extra interest on your home loan. Make your payments on time. Payment history accounts for 35% of a credit score, and even one late payment could knock off up to 110 points.
Obtain a free copy of your credit report from AnnualCreditReport.com, the official website established by the Fair Credit Reporting Act. You'll want to get reports from all three repositories (Experian, Equifax, and Transunion). You may purchase your "credit score" as an option, but please keep in mind these scores can differ from those typically used by creditors.
This is extra important: If you find errors on your report, please reach out to me. We can talk about the potential impacts—good and bad—of credit disputes. For example, a forgotten, unpaid account from many years ago may impact your credit less as it is than by settling it now and making the "problem" seem current.
{{Recipient Name - Nickname}}, thank you for letting me help you as you prepare for your home purchase. If I can answer any questions, please reach out. I'll be glad to help.
Purchase Prospect Workflow – House Payment Calculator
Subject: {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}, this is the number you need to know
Greeting: Look past the price tag, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}.
Did you know that price may not be the most important number to consider when you’re shopping for a home?
A home with a lower price could end up costing more each month!
If the lower-priced home has higher taxes or associated costs (like homeowners association or condo/co-op fees), you could end up with a higher monthly payment than you expected.
Here’s a quick House Payment Calculator to use while you’re shopping. It will help you estimate a monthly payment for the homes you like.
Keep in mind the other costs of ownership as you shop, too. Be sure to ask about monthly energy expenditures. Budget for maintenance, repairs and replacements, too. If you choose a home that is likely to need a new roof, HVAC system or even a paint job within just a few years, its monthly cost to own may be more than that of a higher-priced new or newly remodeled home.

Purchase Prospect Workflow – Planning Ahead
Subject: Prepare now for your perfect application, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}
Greeting: Save yourself some time, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}.
One thing you can do now to prepare for the day you're ready to make an offer on a home is plan for the accounts, documentation and resources you'll need when you file a mortgage loan application.
Below, I’ve spelled out some actions you can take now and some documents you will need when you apply.
As always, if you have any question or would like to move forward, please reach out. I'm here to help!
Preparing for Your Mortgage Application
Income
Provide your last two paystubs along with your W2s and Federal tax returns for the last two years (include all schedules). State returns are not needed.
If you are self-employed, ask me for the additional documentation requirements.
If you receive bonus or commissions or have changed your job or position, let’s talk.
Assets
Combine all the funds needed to close into one account at least two months prior to your application.
Document any other deposits here as each could be scrutinized.
Deposits
Deposit checks individually.
Don’t deposit cash without clear proof of the source.
Liquidation
If you are going to sell stocks, bonds, investments or borrow against a retirement account, do it now. Cashing out now may cost you a few dollars in additional gains, but it also protects against losses.
Current Housing
If you own and are selling, provide a copy of your Closing Disclosure.
If you own and are not selling, you'll need to qualify for both homes or meet the requirements for renting the current.
If you are renting, show 12 months of canceled checks demonstrating timely payments and/or written verification from your management company. Ideally, pay your rent on the same day each month on or prior to its due date.
If you live with family, you may need a letter stating that you live rent-free.
Credit
Check your credit report at www.annualcreditreport.com. Identify any errors now and consult with us for the correct action to take.
If you co-signed a loan or are being reimbursed for a loan that’s in your name, you’ll need at least six months of checks to exclude it.
Avoid new credit or inquiries. These can lower your score and increase your rate.
Employment Stability
Ideally, you’ll have two years or more with your current employer.
Consult with us before changing employers, position or method of compensation. For example, don't switch from salary to commissions.
Purchase Prospect Workflow – Cost of Waiting
Subject: Could waiting cost you, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}?
Greeting: How could waiting to buy affect your payment, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}?
Waiting for just the right time to buy a home can be tricky. Should you save more money first? Wait for the new job to come through?
Waiting can mean you miss the home you really want. And it can bring a monetary cost, too.
Interest rates can be volatile, and they can have a big impact on your payment. Follow the link below to find out how much.
If you're not ready to take action yet, remember these truths:
Today’s prices and rates are known. Tomorrow’s are not.
If rates fall yet prices continue to rise, a payment tomorrow could still be higher than what it is today.
If both rates and prices rise, a payment tomorrow could be even higher and harder to qualify for.
Rising prices can also mean larger required down payments. It can be difficult to save money faster than prices rise.
Are you ready to end the wait? Please reach out. I’ll be happy to help.

Purchase Prospect Workflow – Rate Education
Subject: Find out what influences YOUR interest rate, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}
Greeting: Welcome to the world of rates, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}.
Securing the lowest possible rate for your home loan has less to do with scouring ads and more to do with the particulars of your transaction.
Lenders typically pick the best scenario as the basis for advertisements.
Unfortunately, best-case doesn't apply to every loan.
Here are some factors that impact the interest rate for a specific loan: Loan Level Price Adjustments (LLPAs) - Offered rates are based on LLPAs or risk factors. A high loan to value ratio (LTV) or low credit score, for example, carries higher risk and, therefore, a higher price. Loan Type - An adjustable rate mortgage (ARM) can provide a lower starting rate vs. a fixed rate loan.
Loan Terms
– Shorter terms equal lower rates as equity builds more quickly, reducing the lender's risk.
Combined Factors
– The combination of certain factors work together to impact final pricing. For instance, as credit scores improve, the rate differential for LTV changes are less pronounced.
Securing a good interest rate requires balancing the different factors for your particular scenario.
Fortunately, we excel at balancing acts. Let’s work together to discover the options for you.
Purchase Prospect Workflow – Trade Up Now
Subject: Is now a good time to trade out for a new home, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}?
Greeting: Let’s talk about what you’re leaving behind if you move, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}.
Whether you’re looking for a larger home, considering a downsize, or transitioning from renting to owning your home, making a move is a big decision.
You’re probably in a comfortable spot with your home payment right now. Why risk shaking that up?
Here are some tools to help bring the financial aspect of a new home purchase into focus.
Do you currently own your home?
If so, don’t be discouraged by the price of a new home. Look at the payment instead.
Consider this scenario:
First Loan:
Amount: $200,000
Interest Rate: 5%
Principal & Interest: $1,073.64
New Loan:
Amount: $300,000
Interest Rate: 3%
Principal & Interest: $1,264.81
That's less than $200 extra a month for a loan that's 50% larger!
Plus, if you purchased your current home using a small down payment, you are probably paying for PMI, or private mortgage insurance. You may be able to access enough equity from the sale of your current home to place a larger down payment on your next home. Avoiding PMI can save you several hundred dollars a month.
Finally, tax-free capital gains exclusions are still available on the sale of a home. That means if you make money when you sell, you’re not likely to owe taxes on the profit. And who knows when tax laws might change? If you’ve built up a lot of equity in your current home, selling it while it’s still favorable tax-wise may make sense. (Always consult with your tax professional for advice on tax matters.)
Wondering how much you might make off the sale of your home? Here’s an easy calculator to help.
Button: ESTIMATE HOME SALE PROCEEDS
Sample link: https://sf3.tomnx.com/permalink/homesaleproceedssimple?userId=nGVmhB
Do you currently rent your home?
If you make a rent payment now, chances are you can afford a monthly mortgage payment. Most of my clients are surprised at how far their rent payment can go when they purchase a home.
And remember—when you put your money toward a home payment rather than a rent payment, you’re building equity and earning advantages for yourself instead of your landlord.
Here’s a simple Rent to Mortgage calculator that will help you see how much home you may be able to purchase for a payment that’s comparable to what you’re paying now.
If you want, you can drill down a bit further to see how your down payment can affect your possible purchase price and the income you might need to qualify for the loan.
No matter the home you're leaving behind, it never hurts to take a look at other opportunities, especially if that opportunity is a new home to call your own.
I’ll be glad to help you to take a closer look at your specific scenario and the options that may be available to you. Please reach out, and let’s discuss.

Purchase Prospect Workflow – Love the House
Subject: {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}, If you love the house, don’t lose the bid.
Greeting: In the housing market, the best deal doesn't always come with the lowest price, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}.
If you've found the house you love, think twice before walking away.
When you purchase a home, you're buying more than the four walls. Before you choose a less expensive home than the one you really want or decide not to offer a higher price against another bidder, here are some things to consider. Price vs. Payments - If you're financing your purchase, you'll probably never come close to paying the actual price. You're making a comparatively small down payment and then paying interest on the loan until you refinance or sell. Yes, you will have a higher payment if you pay more for the home, but an extra $10,000 of mortgage money can add less than $50 per month on a low-rate, 30-year loan. Relative Prices - Our natural tendency to pay as little as possible is not as meaningful for an investment, such as a home, as it is for a consumable. In this case, what you pay now can affect your sales price later. There may be little difference in total earnings if you pay less and sell for less or pay more and sell for more. Influencing Value - For appraisers, the last sale or "comp" in an area sets the value for similar homes. Whatever you pay helps to establish what your home and comparable properties are considered to be worth. Setting the Trend - If you pay less for your home than was paid for the last similar home, you may be contributing to a downward price trend, which can be difficult to reverse. Conversely, helping to maintain a trend of price appreciation can end up paying you back many times over. One Chance - No two homes are ever exactly the same. Even when structure matches, your land, your view, your address and your immediate neighbors will always be different. You truly may have only one chance at just the right house.
Industry professionals have all seen buyers lose out on what they really wanted. We don’t want that to happen to you. Nor do we want you to pay more tomorrow for something less than what you could have had today as a result of increasing prices and rates.
If you have concerns about purchasing the home you really love, please reach out. I'll be glad to help you weigh your options.
Purchase Prospect Workflow Pre-Approval
Subject: {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}, Here's how to gain a Buyer's Advantage when home shopping
Greeting: This will help you win the bid, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}.
Recently, the housing market has become more competitive, with bidding wars occurring in many transactions. Plus, mortgage guidelines have been tightened. Documentation requirements have been expanded and are being followed more closely.
A pre-approval gets you through the much of the loan process and uncovers potential pitfalls long before you become obligated by a contract to purchase.
What advantages will I have once pre-approved?
You'll be certain about the price range that's best for you. You'll know how much cash you'll need to close, and you'll know your maximum monthly payment. Understanding your limits will help you negotiate with confidence. Plus, since sellers like a sure thing, you'll have an advantage over buyers who may not have been through the process.
How long is the pre-approval valid?
Your pre-approval is typically good for the "shelf life" of the documents used. These will include a credit report, pay stubs, bank statements, W2s, tax returns, etc. The usable life of these documents will vary, yet it's usually safe to say that your approval is good for up to three or four months. During this time, it pays to keep all important financial documents so they're readily available for future updates.
What if I change my mind?
That's perfectly fine. There's no obligation to purchase a home or use a particular loan program once you've been pre-approved. In fact, pre-approval simply helps to assure you know exactly what's involved, that you are comfortable in a particular price range, and that you are truly ready to make your move.
The process of purchasing a home is easier when you have financing in place before you make an offer.
We're here to help get you started, and it's never too early to do exactly that. Give us a call when you’re ready.
Purchase Prospect Workflow – Home Inspections
Subject: {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}, Should you skip the home inspection?
Greeting: Is an inspection really needed, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}?
As you're preparing for a home purchase, here's something to consider.
We're often asked if a home inspection is required.
The answer is usually no, but that doesn't mean you shouldn't have one done.
You're making a large investment. Having a professional inspector alert you to potential problems can save money and surprises in the long run.
There are other reasons to have a home inspection, too.
If the appraiser sees an apparent deficiency in the condition of the home, an underwriter may ask to see the related section of the home inspection (sometimes called the engineer's report). In this instance, having secured an inspection up front can save you valuable time. Additionally, identifying problems early in the process may mean the seller will remedy them prior to sale.
Purchasing a home with the assurance of good condition—or at the least the knowledge of any potential issues— makes for more accurate pricing and cost expectations. Both of these are clearly to your benefit. By comparison, the cost of an inspection is small.
I hope you're finding the information I'm sharing helpful as you prepare for your home purchase. Please reach out when you have questions or if you're ready to move forward. I am here to help.
Purchase Prospect Workflow Cash On Hand, Down Payments, and PMI
Subject: {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}, How Much Down Payment is Enough?
Greeting: Wondering how much to save, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}?
When you get ready to purchase, you'll definitely need to have some cash on hand.
Not only will you need money for your down payment, but most buyers pay upfront expenses that may include an appraisal fee, earnest money to put down when you make an offer on your home, the cost of an inspection, and prepaid home expenses, like taxes and insurance.
In most cases, you'll want to allow for 2% to 5% of your purchase price for these types of expenditures. This number varies greatly, though, so let's be sure to talk about your particular situation before you buy.
For now, take a look at how low down payments can go:
ZERO
The VA and the USDA both offer a zero down loan program for individuals and/or properties that meet their criteria. Sometimes, loans require little or no cash out of pocket. Some HUD properties are available with as little as $100 down.
3%
Fannie Mae/Freddie Mac conventional loans are available with down payments as low as 3% on single-family homes, including eligible condos, co-ops, and some manufactured homes. Fixed-rate mortgages with up to 30-year terms and ARMs are available.
3.5%
The Federal Housing Administration (or FHA) loan program can allow as little as 3.5% down, and it is more lenient than most other programs on minimum credit scores and other factors.
Are you surprised at how low you may be able to go? While many believe a 20% down payment is required, you can see now that it’s far from the only option.
In most cases, when you purchase with a low down payment, you will be required to purchase private mortgage insurance (PMI). The cost is typically added to your monthly mortgage payment. You'll be able to stop paying it after you gain more equity in your home, often through an appraisal process or by refinancing your home.
Whether you’ve saved a little or a lot, reach out today, and we’ll work on finding a loan that works for you.
Purchase Prospect Workflow – Opt Out Today and Credit Tips
Subject: {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}, Here are a few more tips and reminders as you prepare to buy a home.
Greeting: Is this the end, {{Recipient Name - Nickname}}?
This is the last email in our series about purchasing a home, so I want to leave you with some tips and reminders to make sure you're ready to act when the time comes.
First, I recommend that you go ahead and put an end to the unsolicited credit offers that will probably come when you apply for a mortgage.
My clients are sometimes surprised when the credit bureaus share their information after their credit is pulled for a home loan application and they get multiple calls from other lenders. Sometimes, the companies who call are not reputable or engage in bait and switch tactics.
You can stop the unsolicited credit offers before they start by opting out at www.optoutprescreen.com.
We've already discussed tips for managing your credit, so here are a few reminders that may come in handy as we close out our email series:
Continue making your payments on time, even after your credit has been pulled for your home loan.
Payment history is the largest factor in your credit score, and your credit may be pulled again as your closing date approaches.
Do not open new store credit cards just to save on a purchase.
New accounts can lower your score. Saving 10% on a $300 lawn mower means little if it costs you even just fractionally more on a $300,000 home loan.
Do not open new accounts just to transfer balances for an introductory rate.
In addition to possibly lowering your score, these offers often have traps. Instead, use them to leverage a lower rate from your existing card company.
Do not close old accounts.
If you have a good record of payments on old accounts, these will benefit your score. Using them occasionally and conservatively will keep them active and contribute toward a good score.
Keep a high credit line and a low balance. Credit utilization ratios measure this relationship, and lower is better.
Thank you for allowing me to send you information about purchasing a home. Of course, this does not have to be the end of our conversation. I'll occasionally touch base with you. And when you're ready to make a move, I'll be here to help. Best wishes to you!

Refi Prospect Workflow – Refinancing Benefits
Subject: Name, Refinancing Means More Than Monthly Savings
Greeting: There are many ways a refi can help you, Name
People most often refinance their mortgage loans to reduce their interest rates and save on their monthly mortgage payment. But that's far from the only reason to pursue a refinance. Reduce your balance faster. With a lower interest rate, you pay more principal with each payment, especially in the first years of the loan. Example: After five years of payments on a 30-year loan of $200,000 at 4%, you would pay $19,706 in principal vs. $17,105 on the same loan at 5%. That's an extra $2,601 in benefit on top of the $7,052 of interest savings. Total advantage = $9,653
Own Free and Clear Sooner.
There are two ways to make this happen:
Pay extra principal.
Apply your monthly savings toward principal to shorten your loan term by several years. Example: Using the same loan terms from above, pay your $118/month savings as extra toward principal and cut the loan from 30 to 24.33 years.
Refinance for a shorter term.
Rates on 15-year loans are typically lower than 30-year loans, so a payment on a shorter term may still be within a comfortable range for you.
Maximize Your Rate of Return Through Investments.
If you deposit the $118 monthly savings from the example above into a tax deferred account earning 6% over time, it will grow to $81,852 in 25 years. If you use the savings to increase your 401K contribution with a 50% employer match, that figure would equal $122,782. Earning 6% on your money may be tough right now, yet historically, returns on a properly balanced and diversified portfolio are 7% or better. Always consult with a properly licensed financial advisor when making investment decisions.
Tap Into Your Equity.
If you need to make repairs or improvements, you may be surprised at how much cash you might be able to free up without increasing your monthly payment. The same can be said for financing college educations or purchasing a second home or investment property.
Enjoy Peace of Mind.
There’s comfort in making a prudent decision and putting a plan into action.
We're here to review your options and help you decide what might be right for you.
Refi Prospect Workflow – Refi Hurdles
Subject: Name, What’s standing in your way?
Greeting: What’s keeping you from saving money with a refi, Name?
Here are some common statements I often hear from clients who are hesitant to refinance their loans. Do any of these ring true for you?
"I've read that the rate needs to be 1% or 2% lower than my current one."
When average loan amounts were much lower, it took a much bigger drop in rates to achieve tangible savings. Today, even small rate differences can make a big impact. The best way to determine value is to simply divide your costs by your savings. This provides a "break-even" period, and if you know you'll be using your loan past this point, the rest is pure benefit.
"I haven't yet reached the break-even point from my last refi."
That may be okay. Refinancing again will require additional investment, but it could get you to an overall break-even point—and greater savings—more quickly.
"I don't want to add years back to my loan."
The new loan term created when you refinance is only on paper. You determine the actual length of the loan by how much you pay. If lowering your interest rate saves you $100 per month, add that money to your new payment. You will reduce your balance more quickly and reach free and clear ownership faster than you would by keeping your current loan.
"It's too expensive. I'd rather save my money."
Refinancing is all about saving money! The historically low interest rates that make refinancing such a good deal right now also make “saving" your money in the bank a lousy one. Banks are paying just fractions of a percent to hold your cash, but investing in a refinance could save you hundreds of dollars per month for a far greater yield on your cash.
Example: If closing costs = $3,600 and annual savings = $1,200, that's a 33% rate of return on your money ($3,600 x 33.3% = $1,200).
Even better, you can often refinance without using any funds "out of pocket."
Refinancing can have other benefits, too.
A lower rate may mean not only a smaller payment but more paid toward principal each month, too. You may be able to free up cash for renovating your home, financing a college education, purchasing a vacation home or investing in property without adding to your monthly expenditures.
Are you ready to explore your refinancing options by the numbers? Reach out. I'm here to help.
Refi Prospect Workflow – Principal and Interest Calculator
Subject: What will your payment be, Name?
Greeting: Here's a way to compare different rates and loan amounts, Name
When you refinance your home loan, the monthly principal and interest payment is the amount that will vary when you're considering different interest rates, loan amounts and loan terms.
Your monthly expenses for taxes, insurance and fees will likely remain the same as your current payment (though it's possible you will eliminate private mortgage insurance, or PMI).
You can use this simple Principal & Interest Calculator to play around with different loan amounts, terms, and rates. It will be easy to see how changes to either will affect your monthly cost.
Thank you for allowing me to send information on refinancing your home. Any time you have questions or are ready to move forward, please reach out. I’m here to help!

Refi Prospect Workflow – Debt Consolidation
Subject: How much can you save by consolidating, Name?
Greeting: Here’s another way a refi can pay, Name.
Mortgage interest rates can be an amazing bargain compared to consumer and installment rates. Total interest, total term and cash flow savings can be significant with the right plan.
Consolidating multiple debts into one home loan is not for everyone. For instance, using your equity to have the equivalent of a 30-year car loan is rarely a great idea. But it may work if you have the discipline to take advantage of a low rate to speed up—rather than slow down—payment terms.
Consolidation can make debts disappear with less total interest expense than they would otherwise.
Want to explore what a good consolidation plan could mean for you? Reach out, and we'll be happy to help.
Refi Prospect Workflow – Annual Credit Check Reminder
Subject: Here are some things to do in preparation for a refi, Name
Greeting: Hi, Name!
Many of my clients who are preparing for a refinance start thinking about sprucing up their credit score. After all, your credit score impacts the interest rate you secure on your home loan, which affects the amount of your monthly payment and the overall cost of your mortgage.
To keep your credit in top shape, please remember the following:
Do NOT close old credit accounts. Many homeowners like to get their finances in order by paying off credit cards. If you do this, please keep the accounts open. The length of time you've used credit is important to your score. Keep your balances low. The percentage of available credit you use counts more toward your score than the total balances on your cards. While it's tempting to move all balances to one low-interest-rate card, you will get closer to the limit on the one card, and it could negatively impact your score. Opinions vary, but experts say you'll help your score by using only 10% to 30% of your available credit. Avoid new credit inquiries. Department store credit cards may save you 10% at purchase, but applying for one could cut points from your credit score and cost you thousands in extra interest on your home loan. Make your payments on time. Payment history accounts for 35% of a credit score, and even one late payment could knock off up to 110 points.
Obtain a free copy of your credit report from AnnualCreditReport.com, the official website established by the Fair Credit Reporting Act. You'll want to get reports from all three repositories (Experian, Equifax, and Transunion). You may purchase your "credit score" as an option, but please keep in mind these scores can differ from those typically used by creditors.
This is extra important: If you find errors on your report, please reach out to me.
We can talk about the potential impacts—good and bad—of credit disputes. For example, a forgotten, unpaid account from many years ago may impact your credit less as it is than by settling it now and making the "problem" seem current.
Name, thank you for letting me help you as you consider a refinance.
If I can answer any questions, please reach out. I'll be glad to help.
Refi Prospect Workflow – Fixed vs ARM Calculator
Subject: There’s more than one way to refinance your home, Name
Greeting: Have you considered a different kind of loan, Name?
Did you know that you may be able to lower your payment even more if you finance to different kind of mortgage?
When many of my clients think of financing a home, they think only in terms of fixed-rate mortgages, where the interest rate will stay the same for the full term of the loan.
Adjustable-rate mortgages, or ARMS, are another option that may help you lower your monthly payment even more and pay down your principal faster.
Some ARM loans are actually a hybrid. They have a rate that’s fixed for the first 3,5,7 or even 10 years. You’ll pay a lower interest rate in the first years of the loan, so you’ll have a lower monthly payment. You’ll also put more money toward principal in the early years of your loan, so you’ll build equity faster than with a higher rate, fixed-for-the-full-term loan.
This calculator will help you compare the payments, costs and savings available with fixed vs adjustable mortgages. Give it a try to see if a helping ARM is right for you.
If you have questions or are ready to make a move, please let me know. I’m happy to help.

Refi Prospect Workflow – Refi Savings
Subject: 5 Smart Things You Can Do with Refi Savings, Name!
Greeting: What will you do with the money you save, Name?
Most people refinance their mortgages so they can save on their monthly payments. Have you thought about how you'll spend that money if you pursue a refi? Here are some options to consider—and some reasons you may want to move forward now.
Establish or enhance your emergency cash reserve.
If your income is interrupted or if an opportunity or need arises, your emergency fund lets you avoid interest costs from borrowing or tax consequences from cashing out investments.
Pay down non-tax deductible/high rate debt.
Paying off high rate credit cards or other debts will free up your cash flow so you can invest it for growth.
Invest, Invest, Invest.
Max out your 401K contribution. Even a partial match from your employer yields an amazing, instant rate of return. Got kids? Start or ramp up a college savings plan. Tuition costs are rising faster than inflation. Invest now to help beat the trend.
Make sure you are protected.
Do you have sufficient life, disability and property insurance? Doing everything else right matters little if tragedy strikes and you lose it all due to lack of coverage. Why not set up a review with your insurance pro today? Call me if you need an introduction to someone who can help.
Pay off your loan faster.
This is not always the best thing to do with your cash (see above), but for some, peace of mind has the best rate of return.
One more thing:
How about buying your vacation/retirement home today?
Subsidize your payments by renting it out when you aren’t there. Then, when you do retire, you will have already built memories in your new home, and you will be well on your way to paying it off. Plus, when you sell your main residence later, the proceeds can fund living expenses. This is not for everyone, but it may make sense for some.
Never hesitate to reach out with your questions, and please let me know when you're ready to access your monthly savings!
Refi Prospect Workflow – Refi Traps
Subject: Name, What refi traps could catch you?
Greeting: A little preparation goes a long way, Name
I've seen clients get tripped up in a few common traps. Let's work together to make sure they don't ensnare you.
The automatic payment trap
– It can take up to two weeks to have automatic payments canceled. If your payments are made this way, be sure to turn it off before closing. You don’t want to pay for the same month twice!
The missed or late payment trap - Believe it or not, lots of people think they don't have to keep making payments once they apply to refinance. Missing a payment could damage your credit and even preclude closing. Just be careful regarding your very last payment, as it should be made in time to assure it's credited toward your payoff balance. The tax escrow trap - The funds in any existing escrow account will typically be held until after the current loan is paid off. Since this money will not be available at closing, you need to be able to establish a new escrow account and/or pay any upcoming taxes from savings or the new loan proceeds. The insufficient funds trap - The tax escrow trap can contribute to this, and so, too, can many other factors. For example, a low appraised value could limit your loan amount. As many loans are set up to cover all closing and escrow funds, it's important to know that any necessary or unexpected adjustment could change the cash to close requirements accordingly.
I want you to be aware of these potential pitfalls before they have a chance to occur. Of course, I will work with you and on your behalf to prevent and avoid them.
Reach out whenever you have questions, and I'll be happy to help!
Refi Process Workflow – Refi Process
Subject: Name, Here’s what you can expect in refinancing
Greeting: From app to close, let’s look at the process, Name
As you're considering a refinance of your home loan, you're probably wondering about the steps, what you'll need to do, and what we'll be doing. Here's a quick breakdown. Application. After we determine that a refinance will be beneficial for you, we start the application. Much like your original mortgage application, this one collects general information and asks for documentation of your income and assets.
Processing.
Next, we’ll gather property information with an appraisal, title reports and proof of property insurance. We’ll also request a credit report and verify your income and assets.
Underwriting & Approval.
The underwriter makes sure all loan guidelines are met or exceeded by verifying the information we’ve provided. A long checklist of factors must be satisfied during this stage. Additional documentation may be requested or "conditions" may be placed on the approval. Ultimately, the underwriter is held responsible for the decision made on a loan and must assure that anyone else picking up the file would come to the same conclusion.
Closing/Funding.
After any conditions placed on the approval have been satisfied, your loan is cleared for "docs" or closing. Your closing package will be compiled, a Closing Disclosure form will be provided, and then your closing will be scheduled and completed. On loans for primary residences, a three-day rescission or waiting period must transpire between closing and the funding of the new loan. After the rescission, your old loan will be paid off, and your new loan will start.
Every property and situation is unique. Many small steps may occur within these categories, and even a small issue could temporarily derail the process. Things may have changed since you originally financed your home, and the documentation needed today may be more extensive than it was then.
Please realize lenders must take steps to satisfy guidelines that are designed to protect you and everyone else along the way. Things may not always seem to make sense, yet going with the flow will always be easier in the end.
If you have questions about the refinancing process or you're ready to move forward, please don't hesitate to call. We are here to help!
Refi Prospect Workflow – Closing Your Refinance
Subject: Name, When you refinance, you can expect…
Greeting: Here are a few basics to know before closing on your refinance, Name
Here are answers to several more common questions about refinances. While the closing is similar to a purchase, there are some differences, too.
Your “payoff amount” is always higher than your remaining principal balance.
Your balance is the amount of remaining principal owed. Your payoff amount is the balance plus prorated interest from the last payment received until the loan is actually paid off.
The funding date is usually different from the closing date.
The government mandates a three-day rescission period for refinances of primary residences. Loan payoffs will not occur until the fourth business day post closing. This will affect the payoff amount, the final payment date and the release of any cash.
Do you actually get to skip a payment?
It seems that way because your first regular payment is usually not due until the second month after closing. The reality is that while you do get a break on paying principal for the closing month, between the old and new loans, you are still paying a full month's interest.
Don't count on your existing escrow funds for closing. If you have an escrow account for taxes and/or insurance, these funds will be held there until the current loan is paid off. Accordingly, unless funds for taxes due and/or a new escrow account are covered by the new loan, be prepared to advance this money at closing. It will typically take several weeks before your current escrow account funds are returned to you, so it pays to plan ahead.
When you're ready to move forward, our team will be here to help you with your transaction and to answer your questions. We want you to be comfortable with the process and understand it fully. Please let us know how we can help.
Refi Prospect Workflow – Refi DOs and DON’Ts
Subject: Here are a few more refinancing tips, Name
Greeting: Here are just a few more things you might like to know, Name.
This is the last email in our series about refinancing a home, so I want to leave you with some Do's and Don'ts to remember when the time comes to pursue your refi.
DO
Continue to make your regular payments. However, if you have a payment due just prior to your scheduled closing, consult with me first. It may be best to pay at the closing rather than to risk having the payment and payoff letter cross in the mail.
Prepare your home for the appraisal.
The appraiser will take photos inside and out. While a messy house is not really worth less than a clean one, property appraisal is part art, part science. First impressions can make an impact with an appraiser just as with a prospective purchaser.
Keep your ongoing paystubs and bank statements available. Underwriters may request the latest documentation before loan approval or as a condition of loan commitment. Understand that things have changed. Underwriters require more documentation than in the past. Even if requests seem silly, intrusive or unnecessary, please remember that if they didn't need it, they wouldn't ask.
DON’T
Apply for new credit.
Changes in credit can cause delays, change the terms of your financing or even prevent closing. If you must open a new account, please consult with me first. Change jobs during the process. Probationary periods, career or even status changes (such as from a salaried to a commissioned position, leave of absence or new bonus structure) can be subject to very strict rules. Make undocumented deposits. Primarily large but sometimes even small deposits must be sourced unless they are identified. Make copies of checks and deposit slips. Keep your deposits separate and small. Avoid depositing cash. Start any home improvement projects. Small cosmetic projects like painting are not usually a problem. Anything that can disrupt functionality can be an issue if undertaken before the appraisal. Delay projects that require a building permit, involve a bathroom or kitchen renovation, or create structural changes.
And speaking of don'ts, DON'T ever be afraid to ask questions.
Thank you for allowing me to send you information about refinancing a home. Of course, this does not have to be the end of our conversation. I'll occasionally touch base with you. And when you are ready to make a move, I'll be here to help. Together, we'll get you on your way to saving money and achieving your goals.

Marketing
Implement My Mortgage Monitor
My Mortgage Monitor is a video-based, personalized mortgage assessment that encourages borrowers to check their mortgage against the market and explore options for refinance (accessing cash, shortening term, or dropping PMI) and purchase. It is located under
Marketing, Media Library, Public, Interactives.
When available, deal data is populated in the video/interactive and in the email. These fields are based on Primary Deals. If the data is not in the recipient's contact record, they are prompted to enter the information.
The email displays product merge fields based on conditional formatting.Review Product Fields and Conditional Formatting the for additional information.
Only Admins can adjust certain factors in a configuration panel. Configuration panel options for My Mortgage Monitor are:
Colors
Global disclaimer
Default interest rate (applies an adjustment to the national average)
Closing cost factor
Tax factor
Insurance factor
Sales commission percentage
Other factors that may be included in the cost to purchase a new home
Because interest rates and valuations are updated regularly, My Mortgage Monitor was conceived as a regular communication you can have with borrowers so they can remain up to date on the most important industry item to them – their own mortgage.
Best practice is to create a dynamic group of borrowers who closed on their loans more than six months ago and who are not currently in process for a new loan. Then, set up a recurring deployment to go to that group at regular intervals, whether monthly, quarterly, or annually.
You might also deploy My Mortgage Monitor (MMM) as part of a workflow. Common practices are to deploy MMM every six months after a loan closes as part of a post-close workflow or to deploy it annually on the borrower’s loan anniversary date.
My Mortgage Monitor vs Mortgage Checkup
My Mortgage Monitor and Mortgage Checkup, both found in the Public, Interactives folder, serve similar purposes. Mortgage Checkup simply compares interest rates, while My Mortgage Monitor also estimates equity based both on calculated loan balance and AVM where available. Monitor My Mortgage features explanatory videos (including audio of the borrower’s name for most borrowers). Both interactives base calculations on primary deal fields.
Generally, you do not deploy both interactives to the same contacts, at least not in close succession. If you have already set up recurring deployments or workflows for Mortgage Checkup but want to switch, you can either update the HTML in the collections you’re currently deploying or edit the workflow or recurring deployment to point to My Mortgage Monitor.

Dynamic Configuration Panels
Only Admins can customize certain interactive and dynamic videos to meet your company’s specific needs and compliance regulations. Examples of configuration options include language selector, color selector, and addition of disclaimers. Configurations are not available for all interactive and dynamic videos.
While these configurations are applied to interactives and dynamic videos, you set them at the landing page level. Landing pages that contain a configurable interactive or dynamic video are tagged CONFIGURABLE.
Configure an Interactive or Dynamic Video
From the media library, locate the Landing Page that hosts the interactive or dynamic video you want to configure.
Select more options, next to the applicable title.
Select View if the landing page is in the Public library. Select Edit on the title if you previously cloned the landing page and it’s located in your company’s folder.
Click the Select Content Block list.
Select the content block that contains the Configurable Dynamic Video or Interactive.
Select Dynamic Configuration.
Select Create New Dynamic Configuration.
Enter a name for the edited configuration, only you will see this.
Complete the process to edit or keep the default settings.
You can choose a color theme, set language options, and create a play list of up to three additional in process videos.
Select Save New Config.
Select Attach to this Landing Page.
Preview your landing page with your new settings; return to the Media Library and select Preview in More options.
If you add this same interactive or dynamic video in a new landing page, the configuration you just saved will be available. You will see it on the left side of the configuration panel in the list of Config Names.
If you have cloned a landing page, the Dynamic Configuration option will appear for any relevant content blocks; however, the content block will not be labeled as configurable. You’ll want to select the block that contains the interactive or dynamic video.
Some interactives include a state list selector. Recipients can select their state from a list, and state averages for factors like home price, real estate taxes and homeowners insurance overwrite pre-populated national average values for those factors. The configuration panel will allow you to select specific states to appear in the dropdown. In some cases, the configuration panel also allows you to set default values for the same factors. In those instances, your default values will appear initially, rather than the national averages. Recipients will still be able to select their state and populate state averages.
To make adjustments to default interest rates, locate the Adjust Default Interest Rate in the Configuration Panel. If your company's typical pricing is lower than the default, enter a negative number to subtract from the national average displayed. For example, if the interactive shows the national average as 7.000% and you enter -.5, the average will appear as 6.5000% on your branded interactive. If your pricing is typically higher, enter a positive number, and Surefire will adjust accordingly.
Remove or Delete a Configuration
To remove a configuration:
Select Detach from this landing page.
Select Remove Config.
A configuration must be detached from all landing pages before it can be deleted. Interactives or Dynamic Videos on Landing pages with no company configuration attached will carry Surefire default settings.
Review Set Up a Dynamic Configuration for Relationship Builder Videos for additional information.

Power Calls is a premium feature add on which allows users to call their contacts from Surefire using set scripts and reasons.
Power Calls allow the user to call down an entire list of contacts with their various reasons and scripts, one after another.
It allows the user to leave pre-recorded voicemail while the next call dials in the queue.
Power Calls also allows the User to drop follow up emails and SMS (text messages) with one click.
Pre-made Power Calls are available in Public folder, Power Calls. The Admin and the user can create their own custom scripts for org-wide and/or individual use.
