Purchase and Configure a Company Phone Number
Purchase and Configure a Company Phone Number Surefire users can use either Company-Purchased or System Verified Personal Phone numbers to make voice calls to a Contact simply by clicking on the phone number(s) that appear(s) right inside their Contact record.
Company-purchased phone numbers are managed (including the automated prerecorded message that's played when calls placed to those numbers are not answered) in CRM Settings, Master Settings in the Telephony tab. Your Company Phone Numbers and their attributes are listed in a searchable and sortable table.
Caller ID
When a call made to a Click-to-Call telephony number is forwarded to another number, Telcom Companies Caller ID services display the number of the caller, and not the Click-to-Call Telephony number from which the call has been forwarded.
To add a new Company Phone Number for use with Surefire s integrated telephony feature first, select a phone number and then configure the phone number's attributes (i.e. how it is identified and functions) .

Contains - Search for available numbers by a consecutive series of numbers, a phrase, and/or a combination of letters and numbers contained anywhere in the number, e.g. "WD40" Starts with - Search for available 10-digit numbers based on the numbers and/or letters they start with. Practically, then, in the Criteria field (see next step), if you were to enter only three numbers, then you'd be searching by area code. Ends with - Search for available 10-digit numbers based on the numbers and/or letters they end with In the Criteria field enter a number, letter or bot that are appropriate to the Search Type you selected.
The Contains option provides the option to enter a string of numbers and letters.
If applicable select Toll-Free to limit search results to Toll-Free numbers.
Toll-Free Numbers will not have a US State associated with them in the Company Phone Number table shown on the Telephony tab under Master Settings.

My Text Message Numbers
This section is a summary of Personal Phone Numbers associated with your Surefire user account. Text Message Priority - In addition to determining what order the system will send texts, this is also the Default Order in which the Surefire system presents numbers for use when making outbound click-to-call calls. You can re-order Priority, by dragging the numbers here or you can select Menu, at the end of the row and Edit. Name - The default entry is simply the phone number itself. You can, however, edit this to something more memorable for easy reference.
Incoming Text Options -
Entries in the column indicate whether or not texts sent to this number will be forwarded to the personal number of your choice. If texts are to be forwarded, the destination number is listed here too. Incoming Call Options - Details on how calls made to this number are currently handled. Outgoing Call Options - Details on how calls made from this number are currently handled.
Configuring a Voice Number
To configure how incoming and outgoing voice calls are handled by Surefire for a given phone number associated with your account:

In the Edit Details screen verify or set the following fields: Name - If you plan to have multiple numbers, give each a unique Name Number - The actual telephone number. This field is not editable. Text Message Priority - If you have more than one number, this Priority ranking determines what order the system will send texts in. Incoming Text Options - If Forward to my cell is set to Yes, any direct responses to a text from your Text Message Number is forwarded to the number designated as the Mobile Number on your User Profile. Incoming Call Options - Select from the drop down list: Ring Cell Number on File - the call is routed to the Cell Phone Number that you've entered under the Contact Info section on your Surefire User Profile page.
Ring Private Cell Number on File - the call is routed to the Private Cell Phone Number that you've entered under the Contact Info section on your Surefire User Profile page. This number, when used, will remain "private" and not display for the recipient's phone. Ring Primary Number on File - the call is routed to the Office Phone Number that you've entered under the Contact Info section on your Surefire User Profile page. Disabled - When this option is selected, calls made to this number will not be connected.
When a call made to a Click-to-Call telephony number is forwarded to another number, Telcom Company Caller ID services will show the number of the caller, and not the Click-to-Call Telephony number from which the call has been forwarded. Outbound Call Options - select: Enabled - This number will be available as an option when choosing from which number you want to call a contact directly from Surefire.
Disabled
-This number will not be available as a selection option when choosing from which number you want to call a contact directly from Surefire.
For Outbound calls, your computer must have microphones and speakers turned on, whether directly in the hardware of your computer or a headset. Please also be sure that your microphone is not muted.

The map displayed provides an interactive visual representation of how thoroughly you have each state covered with regard to purchased company phone numbers for use in Surefire 's click-to-call telephony features.

Power Calls and Telephony
Text Messaging in Master Settings
If you have purchased any Text Messaging Numbers for use, you can manage their settings from the Text Messages tab under CRM Settings, Master Settings.
The screen is divided into several sections:
Allow Text Messages to be sent to Text Message Subscriptions
Text Message Opt-Out Frequency Control
Zapier - Assume Text Message Opt-In (trusted source)
Allow Text Messages to Be Sent To As a way to limit the potential ramifications of unsolicited marketing by text, some organizations may want to limit which phone numbers Surefire users are able to send text messages. Surefire provides the following options: All contacts not unsubscribed - This selection will allow Surefire users to send text messages to all contacts except those that have opted out by replying STOP to a text received from Surefire.
Only contacts who have opted in - This selection will allow Surefire users to send text messages only to contacts who have opted in to receive text messages via one of the three possible ways outlined below.
Ways to Opt-In
Form Opt-In
– Surefire has created the option to add the field for Text Message Opt-In to any custom form created by an organization. This field option provides the organization with the ability to capture Contact Opt-In’s with any form submission. This option is the only native way for the Surefire system to capture and monitor contacts that have opted into receiving text messages.
Data Import
– An Organization can create an import map in Data Management that is unique to contact opt-ins.
Standard dedupe protocols should be considered so as not to create duplicates should the list include existing contacts.
Zapier
– An organization can set up a Zap that will assume text message opt-in for all contact mobile phone numbers added or edited in this manner based on specified conditions. Those users and conditions that are set up using this method will be listed in the Zapier – Assume Text Message Opt-in (trusted source) section.
Text Message Opt-Out Frequency Control
This section allows your organization to choose a standard Opt-Out layout/footer to be used for all text messages. In addition, the frequency for how often the Opt-Out layout/footer will appear for text messages can be set. This frequency control is intended to eliminate the Opt-Out language appearing with every single outbound message. This can be especially useful if you text a particular contact frequently.
To set the frequency, select the number of days between appearances of the Opt-Out layout in any text message. The Opt-Out layout will appear in the first message sent and then not appear again until at least the selected number of days has elapsed. For example, if 10 days is selected, the first text message will contain the Opt-Out layout. Then, that layout will not appear again until at least the 11th day from the initial message, no matter the number of messages sent to that contact in the intervening timeframe.
Text Message Subscriptions
This section provides a cumulative total of contacts who have actively opted in or opted out using one of the above-described methods.
Once populated, the quantity number can be clicked on and opened to view a table showing the username, contact name, mobile phone number, and date/time added to the list.

Marketing
Power Calls and Telephony
Do Not Call Registry
The National Do Not Call (DNC) Registry is a list of phone numbers from consumers who have indicated their preference to limit the telemarketing calls they receive. The registry is managed by the Federal Trade Commission (FTC), the nation’s consumer protection agency. It is enforced by the FTC, the Federal Communications Commission (FCC), and state officials.
The DNC provisions of the TSR cover any plan, program or campaign to sell goods or services through interstate phone calls. This includes calls by telemarketers who solicit consumers, often on behalf of third-party sellers. It also includes sellers who provide, offers to provide or arrange to provide goods or services to consumers in return for some type of payment as part of a telemarketing transaction.
The National Do Not Call Registry covers intrastate telemarketing calls under the FCC’s rules. The do not call provisions do not cover calls from political organizations, charities, telephone surveyors, or companies with which a consumer has an existing business relationship.
A company with which a consumer has an established business relationship may call for up to 18 months after the consumer’s last purchase or last delivery, or last payment unless the consumer asks the company not to call again. In that case, the company must honor the request not to call. If the company calls again, it may be subject to a fine of up to $42,530.
If a consumer makes an inquiry or submits an application to a company, the company can call for three months. Once again, if the consumer makes a specific request to that company not to call, the company may not call, even if it has an established business relationship with the consumer.
A consumer whose number is not on the national registry can still prohibit individual telemarketers from calling by asking to be put on the company’s own do not call list.
More information is available at the FTC website.

Marketing
Power Calls and Telephony
Do Not Call Registry
Do Not Call
You can see the total number of contacts whose phone numbers have been made unavailable to be called via Click-to-Call phone calls in Master Settings, Telephony.
You can make a contact phone number unavailable by clicking Block Number next to the appropriate contact record phone number.
Once populated, you can click number in the Do Not Call List (DNC) to view a table showing the blocked phone number, the date it was blocked and who initiated the block. There is also a button to view the specific contact record associated with the blocked phone number. This list can be sorted, filtered and searched.
There are multiple options for unblocking a number. In the contact record, click Unblock Number next to the blocked phone number to unblock it.
You can expand the Do Not Call List, select and choose Unblock.
You can unblock multiple numbers at a time, select the appropriate boxes at the beginning of each row and select the Unblock option that appears. Select the header check box to automatically check all rows/phone numbers to unblock all at once.
Once a number has been unblocked, it will then populate the Do Not Call Removals area of the Do Not Call List box. This list can also be expanded when the quantity number is clicked and will show an identical table as the Do Not Call list when expanded, except that it also provides the ability to block the number once again.
Import Global Do not Call List
You can import your own Do Not Call list using the import feature. In C RM Settings, Telephony select tin the Do Not Call List screen select, Import Global Do Not Call List. This generates a Manual Upload Job pop-up box with instructions.
Imports can be done from .CSV, .xlsx or .json files types.
For Imports, phone numbers in the upload should be in one of the following formats for Surefire:
330-730-2872
(330)730-2872
3307302872
A phone number on the DNC list can receive text messages if the contacts have opted in to receive them. Surefire is not able to manage a DNC (Do Not Call) list. The FTC does not allow this. They require each client to have their own account for the DNC, and of course, pay the fee.
If a Service Provider accesses the registry through a client's account, the client must have its own subscription with the Registry. Therefore, clients must create their own account with the FTC.

Turn on Postcards and Print Mail
Turn on Postcards and Print Mail Surefire offers options for your company to allow One-Time print deployments and Recurring Deployments using rules, workflows, recurring, or admin orders including postcards and printed materials. Print deployments must be turned on by an administrator as printed and mailed postcards are offered at an additional cost.
In your Print Settings, you can:
Turn on or off all print capabilities
Select between company pay and user self-pay for One-Time print deployments
Allow company pay or turn off print capabilities for recurring deployments including postcards and printed materials
Set a monthly spending limit for your company
Allow Print
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select Print.
Select Enable Print, ON.
Select the print settings for One-Time print deployments. You can select either company pay
The company pay print option uses the company and user print limits you set for your company
Any One-Time print deployments deployed by users will be deducted from the company and user print limits. user self-pay models for One-Time print deployments.
The user self-pay model allows users in your company to pay for One-Time print deployments themselves prior to deploying the print deployment.
You must be logged in to make a payment.
Select print settings for Recurring Deployments including postcards.
You may choose to allow the company pay model or turn off the recurring deployment print option for postcards and print materials.
The company pay print model uses the company and user print limits you will set for your company. Any costs associated with postcards for recurring deployments will be deducted from the company and user print limits.
Turn off the recurring deployment feature for postcards and print materials will allow your company to turn off print capabilities for recurring deployments while still allowing users to print using the One-Time print deployment feature.
The user self-pay print option is not available for recurring deployments including postcards.
Set your monthly spending limit.
You can spend as much as $10,000 per month on postcards across your company
The user print limit is deducted from your company print limit.
The company and user print limits set for your company will be applied to all deployed prints, One-Time and recurring, using the company pay print option.
Example:  10 users could send up to 450 postcards each.
The Save Changes button is inactive until the Print Limits are set.
Select Save Changes.
Review Send Postcards for additional information.

Closing Gifts, Postcards and Print Mail
Closing Gifts
Closing Gifts Surefire offers several options for personalized closing gifts for Loan Officers to say “Thank You” to their customers. LOs can subscribe to the closing gift service to have their choice of gift automatically sent to clients. Surefire closing gift enrollment is completed through the Retention Center.
Billing and Delivery
Once a Loan Officer has enrolled through the Retention Center, their credit card will be billed every month for any qualifying closed loan deals. Charges will show as being from Top of Mind Network on their billing statement.
A $1 charge may be displayed on the loan officer’s statement after the initial enrollment as a hold to ensure a valid card. This charge goes away after the initial closing gift charge occurs.
Gifts should arrive to borrowers one to six to eight weeks after their loan closes. There are no added costs for shipping and handling. Invoices are sent as the gifts are processed, and include the name of the primary borrower only (co-borrower not listed) to provide detail on which closings received gifts during the billing cycle.

Borrower and Co-Borrower Personalization
The gifts are personalized with the borrower (and co-borrower, as applicable) name as the name(s) appears within Surefire. The personalized gifts utilize the nickname if available, and default to the first name if no nickname is provided. For Stampers, the borrower first and last name are included, as well as the co-borrower, combining the two if the last names match (i.e. John & Jane Doe or John Smith & Jane Doe). The Bamboo Cutting Board includes only the borrower last name, while the 2 Bamboo Board Set will have the last name of the borrower on both boards.
For more information on closing gifts, reach out to your Customer Success Manager.

You can win more deals by making a fast and personal connection with your leads, clients, agents and more with Surefire CRM’s Power Video.
Without the need for any extra software, you can quickly shoot videos in Surefire or upload your own. Videos can be sent as text messages or emails – deployed immediately, or scheduled for later. Videos are a perfect way to connect with new prospects, give status updates along the way, and even celebrate at closing. If a client wants to upload videos or video clips into Surefire, the best way to do that is to use Power Video.
Power Video always works best when managed by an Admin. Although a user can record and make their own video and deploy it, it is just more efficient and strategic when an Admin does it because admins have been trained to: create a targeted email create the marketing pieces deploy marketing pieces incorporate emails into rules and workflows.
Surefire ’s Power Video, helps you to: text videos with Power Messaging, inline playing inside of their phone natively (if less than 20 second). If longer, it will appear as link on landing page. email videos individually or to a group record videos right from platform or on your computer store videos hosted by Surefire (unlimited storage) upload videos for repeat use

Customer Relationship Management (CRM) Master Settings section is where Administrators can make changes to the various elements of the Surefire system. Here you can set parameters for your business emails, forms, text and telephone messages etc.

CRM Master Settings

The Safe Deployment Time Window is a mandatory setting. All deployments that occur outside of the hours selected are deferred to the next day. Complete the following steps to set deployment windows:
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Scroll to the Safe Deployment Time Window field.
Select the applicable hours the deployments are allowed.

CRM Master Settings
Creating a Closed Deal Policy
Creating a Closed Deal Policy Surefire Administrators can create policies whereby, if that policy's conditions are met, the system will automatically set a deal's status to closed.
This feature is particularly useful, for example, when it is applied to Deals that have been imported into Surefire that have been closed in their native software application, but not in Surefire.
To access Surefire 's Closed Deal Policy feature:
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select Closed Deal Policy tab.
Select the Product you want to define the Closed Deal Definition for.
Two tabs are available
[Product Name] - Closed Deal Policy
[Product Name] - Closed Deals Log.
Create Closed Deal Policies
Go to [Product Name] - Closed Deal policy tab.
Select Sales Process "won" Phases checkbox is selected.
When this option is checked, set to On, for any Deal associated with the Product selected at the top of the screen, if the sales process has achieved a sales phase of type won, the deal will be automatically defined by Surefire as Closed.
Define value conditions for one or more of the available product fields.
Example, this product might have a Closed Date field. You could set the valued condition to be Is Not Empty.
Any deals associated with this product where there's any entry in the Closed Date field, Surefire would know to define the Deal as closed.
Set a maximum of five (5) conditions per product. If any of these conditions are met, then any Deal associated with the Product selected at the top of the screen, will be automatically defined by Surefire as Closed.
Select Save Policy.
Enter I understand.
Select Yes, Save Now.
Once a policy has been saved, the system runs the policy against all existing Deals.
During this process, the Closed Deal Policy Feature cannot be altered.
Select the refresh button to view updates of how the application of the Closed Deal Policy process is progressing.
Select Remove Policy to remove the Closed Deal Policy for this product, than select Save Policy button. This will delete any Product Field Value conditions entered previously. This is optional.
Closed Deal Policy - Closed Deals Log
The system retains a record of every deal it has closed per user-configured Closed Deal Policies.
To view these records, select the Closed Deals Log tab.
A sortable-by-column and search-able log displays and includes:
Which Deals are marked as closed by the system, and when Closed Deal Policy condition that was applied by the system in order to determine that the Deal should be closed
Name of the contact the deal was with Email address of the Surefire user who created the Deal

CRM Master Settings
Manage Data Duplication
Whenever new data records are entered into Surefire, either manually, via Forms, a Zapier-Integrated app or indeed via a Data File Upload Job, the system's Duplication Check engine is engaged, running a check to ensure that it is not creating duplicate or conflicting Contact, User or Deal records.
Duplication check policies (aka Detection Logic) are managed under Settings, Master Settings, Data Settings and are organized into four categories, or Channels, each of which has its own customizable contact, deal and, in the case of Data File Upload Jobs, user record check logic: Manual Entry - Contact and Deal records that are manually created Forms
-Contact and Deal records created via Form submissions
Zapier
-Contact and Deal records created via Zapier-integrated apps API - Contact, Deal, and User records created via data uploader and/or API calls.
Data Duplication Rules that are Applied to All Channels
By default, the system always applies the following rules to all four input channels: A contact duplicate check of last name + birthday.
Checks are done in order-based on priority. You can drag and drop each step of a duplication check to re-sequence (see below for details) Policy Fields is a combination of record fields (e.g. Contact First Name + Birthday, or Deal Closing Date + File Number) that determine if a record is a duplicate (see below for details)
Contact Deal Duplication Check policies also apply to Deal Team Members
To ensure performance, the system enforces a limit of five (5) check policies per channel per contact / deal.
Duplication Policy Sets
The input Channels of Surefire 's Data Duplication function, which are automatically activated and applied to all user-initiated Contact and Deal entries, are divided into two Duplication Policy Sets: Contact and Deal.
The exception is API channel, which is covered in detail in Data Import Duplication Checks
Contact Duplication Policies
Reviews the contents of Contact-specific data fields for manually entry Contact & Deal Member records against the contents of those same fields for all existing Contact & Deal Member records in Surefire.
Example Field Types are: Contact Name, Contact Email Address or Contact Source.
Deal Duplication Policies
Reviews the contents of Deal-specific data fields for manually created records against the contents of those same fields for all Deals currently setup in Surefire.
Field Types will be Product-specific, but some examples (for a mortgage product) might be: File Number, Closing Date, or Credit score.
Data Duplication Process
For each Duplication Policy Set (Contact, Deal, and in the case of the API channel, also User), the system does up to 5 checks, in a prioritized order.
For each of those checks, the system compares a Policy Set (i.e. the contents of one or more incoming data fields that have been selected for that check when the Policy was setup) against the contents of those same fields in all of Surefire.
The system must pass all of these checks (i.e. confirm that there is no matching data already in the system) before the new data record can be created in the system.
Configuring a Manual Contact Entry Duplication Check
Let's say you wanted to make sure that any Surefire users that are manually adding Contact Records to the system don't accidentally enter duplicates. You can follow the below steps:
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select Data Settings tab.
Select Data Duplication Policies
Select the Manual Entry channel from the list.
Select the Contact Duplication Policy tab.
Notice the Last Name + Birthday is already listed as a default Duplication Check Policy.
It's possible that a user might want to create a Contact Record in Surefire for a person with a common last name (e.g. Smith) whose birthday is the same as someone else already in Surefire with the same name (i.e. there is already a Contact in Surefire with the last name Smith who also has March 13th, 1975), you might want to add an additional Duplication Check policy by clicking the Create New Contact Duplication Policy button. That way you can ensure the system would not disallow the entry of two March 13th, 1975 Smiths even though they're different people.
Select Policy Fields for a list of Contact Record Fields available for selection.
Select the Contact Field(s) you want the system to check against the incoming record, e.g. Contact Email.
Click Save.
When a new Contact is manually entered into Surefire, the system would first look at the data record it's being asked to add and confirm that there are no Contact Records already in Surefire that have both the same contact last name and the same contact birthday (as the incoming record).
Assuming that this check is passed (i.e. that there are no matches), then the system would move on to the second check and confirm that no contacts in Surefire use the email address that is included in the Contact record that is being manually entered.
Should the system fail any check, then the record will not be created.
You can change the priority of the Duplication Checks (i.e. the order in which they are run) by using the grab bars on the far left of each row to drag and drop each check to higher or lower in the list.

CRM Master Settings
Turn on or off Deployment Queue
There are times administrators may want to pause all deployments and have them held in a queue so that deployments will have to be triggered manually or, if so desired, canceled by an administrator.
This functionality might be useful, for example, if a change has been made to the system that is ready for live testing (e.g. automated Rules). However, in case this change is not successful, you wouldn't want it affecting anything but the controlled test deployments.
Turn On Deployment Queue
To queue all deployments so that only those that are triggered manually are deployed:
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select General tab.
Switch the Deployment Queue toggle to Enabled.
Enter I Understand on the Confirmation screen.
This confirms that you want the functionality is on and that you are aware all deployments will need to be Manually Deployed under Marketing, Deployment Center, Queued.
Select Enable Setting.
Once the Deployment Queue function is on, a new tab is added in Deployment Center titled Queued. Select this to manage Queued Deployments.
Manage Queued Deployments
Go to Marketing, Deployment Center.
Select Queued tab to view your queued deployments.
Future items will not be populated in the queued tab.
Select the deployments you wish to manage by clicking the checkbox.
After selecting your deployments, you can: Deploy - The deployment will be sent after confirmation. Cancel - This will remove the deployment from the queue and add it to the Canceled queue. Canceled items will not be sent and cannot be recovered. Clear Selected - This will un-check all selected deployments.
Enter Confirm.
Select Yes, Deploy Now to send.
Physical deployments, such as postcards, are subject to processing and shipping time.
Turn Off Deployment Queue
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select General tab.
Switch the Deployment Queue toggle to turn off.
Confirming this action causes the system to immediately deploy all content in the Deployment Queue.
Enter I Understand.
Select Disable Setting.

CRM Master Settings
Approval Manager Administration
Approval Manager Administration Surefire can be set up so that Users are required to submit for approval any additions or changes made to Content Collections (including landing pages), Workflows, Rules, User Profiles, Team Member Assignments, and/or Single Property Sites to administrators before those additions or changes can be committed to the system.
Administrators review these submissions by accessing the Approval Manager function found in the Marketing section of Surefire.
Users are in turn notified by email about which of their submissions has been approved or rejected.
A typical example of where the Approval Manager might be used is when a Corporate Marketing and Compliance department wants to control and/or limit what types of marketing materials their loan officers are able to send out.
Approval Manager setup is administered:
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select Approval Manager.
Turn on and off this feature by toggling the master switch.
Next select one of the two options are displayed on the screen: Require Approval - This section is where you set which types of elements in Surefire that will or will not require approval whenever changes or additions are made to them by Users. Notifications - This section is where you choose how and whether Users receive notifications about the status (i.e. Approved or Rejected) of their Content Approval Request Submissions.
Require Approval
Use the toggle buttons to select which Object Types will require administrator approval before changes or additions made by Sales Uses can be committed to the system. Content Collections - Includes adding, changing, or deleting collections and landing pages, including adding email and Text Messaging assets to them Workflows - Includes creating, updating, deleting, pausing, and un-pausing workflow Rules - Includes creating, updating, deleting, pausing, and un-pausing rules User Profile Changes - Includes user profile changes Team Member Assignments - Includes creating, updating, and deleting
Single Property Sites
-Includes creating, updating, and deleting sites
Notifications
Use the controls in this section to manage how content approval and rejection notifications are sent, including which users and/or user groups will be excluded from and/or explicitly included in receiving such notifications. Email - A system-generated email is sent to the email address listed in the Sales User's Surefire User Profile
Receive Notifications for Child Companies
When allowed, Content Approval Request Submissions made by a Sales Users are received not only by administrators of that Sales User's organizational unit in Surefire but also by any administrators in any organizational units that are superior to that one in the Surefire hierarchy.
This function might be turned on for an enterprise where the Child Companies in Surefire do not include any administrator user accounts and thus any Content Approval Request Submissions would need to be rolled up to the Administrators whose user accounts in Surefire are located in the top-level Company (e.g. "Corporate").
Exclude Users from Notifications
You can select users from the currently selected company to exclude from receiving notifications about content approval and rejection.
Enter all or part of the Surefire username for the person(s) you want to exclude. The system displays all matching results in a drop-down list.
Select a name for addition to the list of excluded users.

CRM Master Settings
Web Page Settings for Landing Pages
In order to use Landing Pages in Surefire, you will need to create domains for the system to host them on.
To manage domains, go to CRM Settings, Master Settings, Web Pages.
Set Up Default Domain Surefire currently offers the sf3.tomnx.com domain to host your landing page. To create a subdomain with this domain, perform the following steps:
Select New Domain. button
Choose the domain from the list.
Type in a Subdomain Name.
The subdomain is what precedes the main domain. e.g. when you choose sf3.tomnx.com as your domain and create a subdomain of Welcome, the landing page is hosted on Welcome.sf3.tomnx.com
Select Create.
If the domain already exists, you will receive an error and will need to use another subdomain.
Once you have created the subdomain, when you insert a Dynamic Landing Page link using the Insert a Landing Page Link in an email template, this domain will now be available as an option for you to use.
This only applies to Dynamic Landing Pages. Permalink Landing Pages have a pre-set permalink Domain.
Create Custom Domains
For marketing purposes, you will likely want to use your own custom domains with your Landing Pages in order to maintain consistent branding and provide for a more seamless user experience.
To create a custom domain, you use the same process as for a default domain; however, you will need to select the checkbox for Custom Domain.
Before using this option, you will need to configure settings on your website's control panel and point the CNAME DNS records to: cloudrouter.tomnx.com
This will ensure that your custom domain (e.g. ABC Mortgage Inc. creates a custom domain for loans.abcmortgagesinc.com) that is set up on your web host (e.g. Bluehost, HostGator, GoDaddy, or similar provider) will point to your new custom domain in Surefire and properly resolve any Landing Pages.
For security, you will need to Log In and create a Support Ticket and include:
Fully Qualified Domain Name (FQDN) of the CNAME
Country (C), State (S), City (L), Legal Company Name (O), and Common Name (CN)
Example: C= US, S= Georgia, L= Atlanta O= ABC Mortgage INC. , CN= sitename.domain.com (we are unable to process wildcard certificates)
Contact information for your organization's IT department managing your website/domain, including name, phone and email address.
The Surefire Team will generate a Certificate Signing Request (CSR), and will provide that information back to you securely via the support ticket you created once we receive the information above. From there, your IT department will obtain the Signed Certificate (CRT) per your company's protocol.
Once you obtain the CRT from your IT Department or domain provider, please attach in your Support Ticket so that it is sent securely for The Surefire Team to complete the process.
The Surefire Team will install the certificate and confirm successful completion of your customer domain for use.
There is a required 3 business day period after we receive the Signed Certificate (CRT) before install.
CRTs expire annually, so be on the lookout for a reminder from your certificate provider next year to renew your secure, custom domain. We do recommend setting a calendar reminder a few weeks before your next expiration as well.

CRM Master Settings
Set Incoming Form Approval Master Rule
When Form data is submitted to Surefire, the system refers to the Incoming Form Approval Master Rule to determine whether that data is automatically added to the CRM or if it will need to be reviewed and approved first.
Each individual Form has its own Submission Approval setting that, if configured, supersedes the Incoming Form Approval Master Rule described here.
All Form Submissions and related Reviews are done from Marketing, Forms Reporting.
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select Forms tab.
In the Incoming Form Approval list and select one of the following:
All form submissions must be approved before being added as contacts
Addition of any data submitted from Forms to Surefire will be pending until it is reviewed and marked approved from the Forms Reporting Pending tab.
Only public form submissions must be approved before being added as contacts
Currently all Responses are Public. This functionality will be applicable once Surefire includes a Secure Forms feature: Data submitted from "Secure" iterations of this Form will be entered into Surefire automatically.
All form submissions are added to the contact database immediately
Any data submitted from this Form will be entered into Surefire automatically, with no review or approval required.

Whenever you Schedule a Deployment, the time selected will always be in the Company Time Zone. This is why if you have Companies in different time zones it is good to set the Company Time Zone to the local time to avoid any confusion regarding Deployment Times.

CRM Master Settings
Create an Opt Out List
To Create an Opt Out List, follow these steps:
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select Email.
Select Add New List.
Enter an Opt Out List Name.
Select Create.
The Opt Out List is now available to use for any member of your entire Company.
Review Master Email Settings for additional information.
Using Opt Out Lists
When you Create an Email Deployment, you must always associate it with an Opt Out List. When someone who receives your email then clicks on the Unsubscribe link, they are added to the Opt Out List.
Review Create a Deployment for additional information.
That means that whenever you send another Email that uses the same Opt Out List, this recipient will not be sent the email.
For example, let's say your Company has two Opt Out Lists:
Transactional
Marketing
When you Deploy an Email inviting Prospects to a seminar, you would use the Marketing Opt Out List. But when you are sending out emails regarding loan status updates, you would use the Transactional Opt Out List.
This way, even if a Prospect opts out of your Marketing Emails but a year later applies for a loan with you, they will still receive the necessary Transactional Emails since those emails will use an alternate Opt Out list. (That is of course assuming they do not Opt Out of your Transactional emails!)
You cannot Build an Email Audience for a Deployment without specifying an Opt Out List. You also must include an Unsubscribe link on every Email Layout.
Review Build an Audience for a Deployment and Create an Email Layout for additional information.

Microsoft Authentication Configuration
If your organization utilizes Microsoft Office 365 computing services, you must set your Microsoft Exchange integration configuration for Modern Authentication to have your user’s Surefire calendars connect to their Microsoft Exchange/Office 365 calendars. Microsoft no longer supports Basic authentication in Exchange Online.
This configuration is an Admin only function.
If you are set up as an Azure SSO, or intend to utilize this functionality, then your exchange integration configuration can be set up easily by using the same information for both. Azure SSO is not a requirement for Modern Authentication, but if your organization is planning to add Azure SSO, set this up prior to setting up your Microsoft Exchange integration. In addition, be certain your organization’s Single Sign-On (SSO) is fully integrated with Surefire and working appropriately prior to setting up your Microsoft Exchange modern authentication configuration.
Admins are required to set up the Modern Integration configuration for their entire organization prior to users integrating with their own profiles. Once configured, the user’s integration is completed as normal (see, Connecting MS Exchange Calendar.)
Azure SSO Admins
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select Exchange Integration
The Microsoft Exchange default method is set as Basic and if your organization does not use Microsoft Office 365, then there is nothing further that needs to be done from an organizational level. If you are an Azure integrated organization, then you will need to switch your organizations exchange authentication method from Basic to Modern.
Once you have chosen Modern, you will be presented with an expanded screen to enter your exchange configuration information.
If you are SSO integrated, you will be presented with a toggle option to utilize the same Azure configuration information. If toggled to Yes the necessary information will automatically populate.
Additional Calendar.ReadWrite permissions also need to be turned on. Add the MS Graph API permissions to your existing integration app for Surefire in Azure. These additional permissions are listed in the Setup Help section below the Authentication screen.
As an SSO organization, if you have existing users provisioned, an Admin can auto-provision these users for Microsoft Exchange by initiating the auto-provision Modern Authentication button. Auto-provisioning only works for users successfully logged in through SSO. Future users will have to manually provision or an Admin will need to click the auto-provision button again to capture them.
Non-SSO Integrated Admins
If you are NOT SSO integrated and are not copying over your setup information, there are some help guides below the Exchange Authentication box to assist in setting up your Modern authentication.
Admins will also need to access their Microsoft 365 Admin Center, Azure Active Directory to set up and register a New Application.
Microsoft/Office 365 integration will only work for Business/Enterprise level subscriptions.

Opt Out Lists
When you Create an Email Deployment, you must always associate it with an Opt Out List. When someone who receives your email clicks on the Unsubscribe link, they are added to this Opt Out List.
That means that whenever you send another Email that uses the same Opt Out List, this recipient will not be sent the email.
For example, let's say your Company has two Opt Out Lists:
Transactional
Marketing
When you Deploy an Email inviting Prospects to a seminar, you would use the Marketing Opt Out List. But when you are sending out emails regarding loan status updates, you would use the Transactional Opt Out List.
This way, even if a Prospect opts out of your Marketing Emails but a year later applies for a loan with you, they still receive the necessary Transactional Emails since those emails use an alternate Opt Out list, assuming they do not Opt Out of your Transactional emails.
You cannot Build an Email Audience for a Deployment without specifying an Opt Out List. You also must include an Unsubscribe link on every Email Layout.
Summary
This table displays all of the Opt Out Lists that your Company has created. Quantity - Column displays number of Opt Outs by Mine/Company Edit/Delete - Use the menu icon to edit the name of the list or delete the list
Never delete an Opt Out List that contains valid opt-out email addresses. This could put you in a position to be violating CAN-SPAM regulations.

If more than one Contact shares this Email, all Contacts will be on the Opt Out list. The Opt Out applies to the Email, NOT to the Contact. Content Collection - Collection that contained the Email Media that the Opt Out click happened from Unsubscribed Date/Time - When the Opt Out took place

CRM Master Settings
Create Custom Fields
A Field is where you store an independent piece of data. An easy way to visualize a data Field is to think of it as an individual cell in a spreadsheet.
Certain types of objects in Surefire are made up of the contents several different data Fields. For example, a Contact or User record is an object that's comprised of several distinct pieces of information such as First Name and a Last Name along with other details, such as a Mobile Phone number or a Birthday. Another example, a Company record in Surefire is defined by its Company Name along with several other attributes, such as its Website.
Breaking objects like Contact, User and Company records into Fields means that these objects can be easily queried and accessed from, and for integration with other features in Surefire, such as Advanced Search, Forms, or any other CRM section that would need access to or employ this data.
Data in Fields is entered in multiple t formats. In our examples, First Name, Last Name and Company Name are all be entered as text, while Mobile Phone Number is a 9-digit number, Birthday is in the form a of a date (mm/dd/yyyy) and Company Website is in the form or a URL (www.companyname.domain).
Custom Fields
Depending on how you use Surefire, for Contact, User and Company records, you may want to create identifying data fields in addition to those that are available by default (First Name, Last Name, Website, etc).
For example, if the majority of your Surefire contacts are customers seeking Mortgage Loans, you might want to further identify them, in addition to details like their name and how to get in contact with them, by the type of loan they are eligible for (e.g. Fair Housing Authority or Veterans Administration).
To do this, you would want to add a custom field that captures Loan Eligibility to that object type (Contacts) in Surefire. Now, when a new Contact is entered into the system, there's a place for the loan type to be entered. This data, in turn, can then be employed for use with other features of Surefire.
Adding Product Fields is a separate topic.
Add a Custom Field
Go to CRM Settings, Custom Fields.
Select the tab corresponding to the Object type for which you want to add a Custom Field:
Contacts
Company
Users
Drag the icon for a desired data format (Text, Date, Website, etc) from the Elements area on the right side of the screen and drop it into the drop area.
Configuring Custom Fields
After you add a Custom Field by dropping it into the drop area, you are presented with the Field's Details pop up screen. This is where you define how the Field appears, what content it presents and what content it requests.
All Custom Field Details pop up screens will present you with an area where you must type in a Label for the Field. This is the text that appears next to the Field when it appears in the New or Edit screen for the selected Object in Surefire. The Label's purpose is to indicate to the Surefire user what type of response data the Form Field is supposed to capture.
Field Types
Defined below are the Custom Field types that can be added to Surefire Contact, User or Company records: Short Text - Text field that appears as a single line; cannot be re-sized (in Field Details pop up) to show more lines of text - 100 character max.
Long text
-Text field that can be re-sized (in Field Details pop up) to show more lines of text. Number - Only positive and negative numbers, including decimals, can be entered into this Field. Decimal - Only positive and negative numbers, including decimals, can be entered into this Field. Currency - This Field appears with a dollar sign displayed at its far left. Only positive and negative numbers, including decimals, can be entered into this Field.
Percent
-This Field appears with a percentage sign displayed at its far right. Only positive and negative numbers can be entered into this Field. Checkbox - Use Checkboxes when you want editors of your record objects to be able to enter one or more selections from a set of pre-set options. Options are added in the Field Details Pop Up screen. Example, Contact's Preferred Ice Cream Flavors:
Vanilla
Chocolate
Strawberry
Coconut
Pistachio
Rocky Road Radio - Use Radio Buttons when you want editors of your record objects to be able to enter a single preference selection from a series of options. Options are added in the Field Details Pop Up screen. Example, Contact's Single Favorite Ice Cream Flavor:
Vanilla
Chocolate
Strawberry Dropdown - Displays a List Menu of selection options directly underneath the Field itself. This list menu remains visible until a single selection is made or it is dismissed by the user clicking elsewhere on the Form screen. Options are added in the Field Details Pop Up screen.
This is similar to Radio but better used when you have so many options to choose from that you wouldn't have the room to have them all visible by default. Example, Contact's Single Favorite Ice Cream Flavor:
Vanilla
Chocolate
Strawberry
Coconut
Pistachio
Rocky Road
Cherry Garcia Date - Contents of this Field are formatted as mm/dd/yyyy. When an editor of your record object clicks on the Field, an interactive calendar pop up is displayed. Date/Time - Contents of this Field are formatted as mm/dd/yyyy 03:48 PM. When an editor of your record object clicks on the Field, an interactive calendar pop up is displayed.
Email
-Text entered into this Field must conform to standard email address format, i.e. name@domain.name Website - Text entered into this Field must conform to standard URL address format, i.e. www.domain.name. The system will accept forward slashes plus further address specifications appended to the URL. States - A dropdown, the options are pre-populated with all 50 states plus all American Territories.
Rating
-This is a star rating for a Contact. An editor of your record object should enter a number between 0 and 5 into this field.

This process allows you set up an automatic round robin distribution for leads.
Establish Round Robin
Go to CRM Settings, Roles / Permissions.
Verify or select the Org User Profiles are set to Waterfall for your admin role.
Go to My Company, Company Info.
Select Round Robin tab.
Select Create a Round Robin.
Name your Round Robin.
Select Add User(s) to add the users to the Round Robin group. select Include Child Company Users to locate users when applicable select Honor State Licensing to account for state licensing when distributing the Round Robin. select Apply Location Intelligence to further refine the distribution and ensure that a lead is assisted by the closest available user.
By allowing this option, the system will check the available 5-digit zip code and attempt to match to a user's zip code within the Round Robin distribution configuration. If there is no 5-digit match, the system will attempt to match the first 3 digits of the zip code. Again, if no match exists, the system will default to Honor State Licensing (if turned on).
Select the distribution rate.
Round Robins do not assign leads in the order the users are listed. i.e. 3 to Amy, 1 to Linda, and 1 to Susie. Instead, the leads are assigned in "rounds". A "round" is the total number of weights. In this example a round is 5, so for every 5 leads 3 should be assigned to Amy, 1 to Linda, and 1 to Susie (overall, not necessarily in that order).
Select Save.

Single Sign On SSO User Deactivation
SSO User Deactivation
If you've setup up Single Sign-On (SSO) integration so that users are automatically granted access to Surefire via the credentials they use to sign on to your corporate network (e.g. Microsoft Azure), you may want to ensure those users' access to Surefire is automatically suspended as soon as their corporate network accounts are removed or turned off.

Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select Single Sign-On.
Scroll to the bottom and select Open SSO Advanced Configuration.
Select User Deactivation tab.
Users that have had their access to Surefire (via SSO) deactivated are listed in a table that you can search, sort, and filter table.
Use the slider to turn on or off the automatic access to Surefire.
When turned on this applies to any user who access Surefire via SSO but has had their corporate network accounts removed or turned off. Surefire updates the list of deactivated users every day at 3:30 am EST.

Field Mapping is a way to automate entering details from a user's network account into analogous data fields for that user's record in Surefire. These details can be set up to be updated in Surefire only when a user's network account is initially created, or when that account is updated, or both.
This process is recommended after you have set up SSO integration.

These data fields are updated in Surefire when a user's network account is initially created, or when that account is updated, or both.

The number of roles and branches may vary widely depending on the company

CRM Master Settings
Roles and Permissions
Roles and Permissions Surefire offers a repository of articles that help users understand and navigate the platform. If users can’t find the information they need, have additional questions, or want to speak directly with customer support, they can submit a support ticket.

CRM Master Settings
Roles and Permissions
Configure a Role
Various rights and permissions are added when you create a custom role. You must choose which functions and components the Role will be able to access, create or change, delete, and/or have the ability to execute.
Permission Categories
These functions and components, displayed as rows in the Permissions Table, are divided into Permission Categories, such as Calendar, Marketing, or CRM Admin Settings.
In each of these category groups are the actual functions and components you will be granting permissions for. For example, under the permission category Marketing, you'll find Permission Categories like User Library Content, User Workflows, and User Deployments.
Permission Types
For each Surefire Permission, you will have the ability to assign various Permission Types to your Custom Role. The Type is the actual rights assigned to that Permission (e.g. View, Create, etc.).
For most functions and components, you can assign the following permissions:
View
-The Custom Role will be able to view, but not change, entries in Surefire for this function or component type. Create - The Custom Role will be able to add a new entry into Surefire for this function or component type. Edit - The Custom Role will be able to make changes to entries in Surefire for this function or component type. Delete - The Custom Role will be able to delete entries in Surefire for this function or component type. Grant - Certain Permissions in Surefire do not lend themselves to the above View/Create/Edit/Delete format. Instead, these Permissions are governed by the Grant Permission Type, which is simple Yes/No Boolean right that is assigned to a Permission
For example, the Company Settings Permission has Grant Rights. This is because this Permission grants the Role the ability to access the Company Settings component of Surefire. A user cannot Create or Delete the Approval Manager.
Therefore, if an administrator wants a Role to have the ability to access and edit Company Settings, they will check Grant. Conversely, when a Role (such as Sales User) should not be able to change Company Settings, this Permission would be off.
Assigning Permissions
You can assign Permissions in the following ways: Case by Case - For any given function or component (displayed as a row in the Permissions Table), you can click the checkbox in the column corresponding to the specific permission you want to assign. By Column - You can click on the Permission Type buttons at the top of each column to assign that permission to all eligible functions or components (i.e. rows in the table).
All -Click on the All button, located at the far right of the header row of the Permissions Table, to assign all available permissions to all functions and/or components.
Waterfall
If a Permission has Waterfall assigned to it, then that Custom Role will be able to access that function or component for both the company the User Account is created in, as well as for all of that company's subordinate companies.
Without the Waterfall permission assigned, a User Account assigned that Custom Role can access that function or component for only the company the User is created in (and not any of its subordinate companies).
Permissions that have Waterfall assigned to them are marked with a shield icon in the left-most column of the Permissions Table.
Save & Reset Save to apply your Permission assignments to the Custom Role. Reset to revert to Permission assignments for this Custom Role as they were the last time they were saved.

CRM Master Settings
Roles and Permissions
Permission Categories
Whenever you Create a Custom Role, you will need to assign rights and permissions to the various functions and components the Role will be able to access, create or change, delete, and/or have the ability to execute in Surefire.
These functions and components, displayed as individual rows in the Role Permissions Table, are grouped into 9 Permission Categories. Descriptions for each are provided below.
Permission Definitions
My and Org
Throughout the Role Permissions Table, certain functions and component names are preceded by the terms My and Org. In this context, these terms are differentiated as follows: My - When assigning a role its permissions to a function or component preceded by the term "My," then any Surefire users assigned that role will only be able to access, create or change, delete, and/or have the ability to execute their own instance of that function or component.
For example, giving a role access permissions to My
Calendar would mean that any users assigned that role would be able to access their own calendar, but no one else's Calendar within their Surefire Company. Org - When assigning a role its permissions to a function or component preceded by the term Org, then any Surefire users assigned that role will be able to access, create or change, delete, and/or have the ability to execute instances of that function or component for all users within their Surefire Company.
For example, you might want to give a Management Role access permissions to Org
Calendar so that users assigned that role would be able to access Calendars for all the users in their company.
View, Create, Edit and Delete
For most functions and components, you can assign the following permissions:
View
-The Custom Role will be able to view, but not change, entries in Surefire for this function or component type. Create - The Custom Role will be able to add a new entry into Surefire for this function or component type. Edit - The Custom Role will be able to make changes to entries in Surefire for this function or component type. Delete - The Custom Role will be able to delete entries in Surefire for this function or component type. Grant - Certain Permissions in Surefire do not lend themselves to the above View/Create/Edit/Delete format. Instead, these Permissions are governed by the Grant Permission Type, which is simple Yes/No Boolean right that is assigned to a Permission
Functions and/or Components to which you assign the Grant permission, by nature of being actions, are not eligible to have View, Create, Edit or Delete permissions assigned to them. Waterfall Permissions - Functions and/or components that can have the Waterfall permission assigned to them (marked with a shield icon in the left-most column of the Permissions Table in Surefire ) are marked with an asterisk (*).

CRM Master Settings
Roles and Permissions
Waterfall Permissions
If a Custom Role Permission has the Waterfall right assigned to it, then any User Account assigned that Custom Role will be able to access that function or component for both the company the User Account is created in, as well as for all of that company's subordinate companies.
Without the Waterfall permission assigned, a User Account assigned that Custom Role will be able to access that function or component for only the company the User is created in (and not any of its subordinate companies).
Functions and/or components that can have the Waterfall permission assigned to them are identified with in the left-most column of the Role Permissions Table.
Example
You have Custom Roles for Division Manager and Assistant Division Manager.
You want the Division Manager to be able to have full rights (e.g. View, Create, Delete, etc.) for Org Contacts that both reside at that Division Manager's own Company Level (East Region in the example pictured below) as well as all those Contacts that reside in all of the underlying Companies, i.e. the Division Branches (Boston, Charlotte and NYC).
Conversely, even though they are located higher in the company structure, you do not want to allow the Assistant Division Manager role to view or access any Org Contacts except for those that reside within the Assistant Division Manager's own Company Level (i.e. East Region).
In this scenario, pictured below, you would assign the Division Manager Role full Permissions for Org Contacts and then additionally check Waterfall Permissions:
However, for the Assistant Division Manager, should not have Waterfall Permissions. You can deselect the option.

CRM Master Settings
Roles and Permissions
Create a Custom Role
Go to CRM Settings, Roles/Permissions to view the Custom tab.
System administrators can wholesale assign permissions to a group of Users by using Custom Roles such as:
Administrators,
Standard Users
Power Users.
Each of these Roles has its own different set of Permissions, i.e. actions they can perform, CRM areas they can access, etc.
For Example, you might create a Custom Role, called Admin Assistants, which has only limited permissions within Surefire, such as:
View permissions for Contacts
View and Create permissions for Calendar Events.
Then, when a user account in Surefire is setup for an Admin Assistant who has just joined the company, that user account can be assigned the Admin Assistant Role, and those pre-configured permission limitations are applied to the new user.
The Roles/Permissions screen is divided into two sections:
A list of Custom Roles
Interactive Role Permissions Table
The Permissions Table for the selected Custom Role is where you edit and adjust Permission Settings.
Custom Roles List
The Custom Roles List, which is displayed as a table, shows all of the Custom Roles defined in Surefire along with the number of users that is assigned to each. This is where you can Manage Custom Roles.
By default, there are two Custom Role types included in the list. Administrator - All possible permissions granted Standard User - A subset of default permissions with lesser controls than Administrator
Create New Custom Role
The Custom Roles List is also where you can Create a new Custom Role:
Select New tab.
In the New Custom Role field enter a Custom Role name such as Power Users.
Select Add New Custom Role.
A new Custom Role, with no permissions assigned to it, is added to the Custom Roles list.
Role Permissions Table
The Permissions Table, located on the right-hand side of the Roles/Permissions screen, is where you Configure a Role by granting types of access and management permissions to Surefire functions and components (grouped in the table into Permission Categories).
You can limit which functions and components (i.e. rows) are displayed in the table by typing all or part of the names of the function or component you want to see into the Filter Permissions field.

CRM Master Settings
Roles and Permissions
Manage Roles
You can clone, delete, rename, tag and manage access to Custom Roles on the Roles/ Permissions screen.
Clone & Delete
The Custom Roles List, which appears as a table, displays all the Custom Roles defined in Surefire along with the number of users assigned to each. Clone Custom Role - Create an editable copy of this Custom Role. Useful for when you want to base a new Custom Role on an existing one with minimal changes. Delete Custom Role - You can only delete Custom Roles that have zero users assigned to them. Custom Roles eligible for deletion display in red.
Rename a Custom Role
In the Custom Roles list, click on the custom role name.
Select Rename Role.
In the Edit Role Name field, enter a new name for the selected Custom Role.
Select Rename.
Tags
Tags are unique identifiers that can be added, like labels, in order to further categorize or note a small reminder about a Custom Role.
To apply a Tag, in the Tags field (located in the upper-left of the Custom Role Permissions Table), type in the name of a new or existing tag. Select Enter.
Edit Use Tags
Apply Use Tags to manage which Surefire contacts or organizational units will have permission to use (i.e. apply) this Custom Role.
Click on the Edit Use Tags. You can access two functionality components: Exclude Tags and Except For Tags.

Tags are unique identifiers that can be added, like labels, in order to further categorize assets, resources and entries in Surefire.
Specifically, Tags can be applied to:
Contacts
Contact Dislikes
Content Collections
Rules
Workflows
Forms
Images
Landing Pages
Dynamic Videos
Tags can be used as a way to categorize and organize any of the above items. Once a Tag has been created, it is available to be applied to any items. You can apply an unlimited number of Tags to an eligible item in Surefire.
Additionally, permissions governing who can have access to apply individual Tags can be set.

CRM Master Settings
Tags
Create a Tag
Go to CRM Settings, Manage Tags.
Select + Add Tag.
Enter a Tag Name.
This is the text that appears on the tag when it is applied to an item in Surefire.
Enter a Tag Category.
Tag Categories are ways to organize and group Tags. You can think of a Tag Category as a way of making folders where groups of Tags can be found.
It will only add and display Categories already active in Surefire.
Select Save.
Like vs. Dislike Tags
Tags can be classified as either liked (displayed in green) or disliked (displayed in red).
You can use this classification to help you visualize and remember which tags have positive and negative connotations.

CRM Master Settings
Tags
Categorize a Tag
For the purposes of classification and organization, Tags in Surefire are grouped together into Categories.
Tag Categories provides an option to group similar items together. You create Category labels which in turn, apply to Tags.
Before a Category can be applied to a Tag, it must be created in the Surefire system.
Go to CRM Settings, Manage Tags.
Select + Add Category on either the Tags, Categories or Tag Cloud tab.
In the Category Name enter a name for the new category.
Select Save.
The category can now be applied to a tag by either Edit a Tag or Verify a Tag.
Apply a Category - Edit Tag Pop-Up
In Manage Tags, select Tags tab.
Select the Tag link. Alternatively, under Actions column, select In the Tag Category field, enter a category name.
Select Save.
Enter the name of a Category that has already been created in Surefire.
The system uses predictive text to list any available Categories already in the system that match with whatever partial Category name you type.
Apply a Category - Verify a Tag
Tags that have been added, but have not had a category assigned to them will appear in the table with Needs Verification displayed as a link in the Category column.
Select the Needs Verification link.
In the Tag Category field enter a tag.
Select Save.

CRM Master Settings
Tags
Manage Use Tags
Employ Use Tags to manage which Surefire Users or groups of Users (e.g. Organizational Units) will have permission to view and/or use various components in the CRM such as Tags, Assets, Layouts, or Roles.
Review Create a Tag Media Assets, Media Layouts, and Create a Custom Role for additional information.
You can configure a Use Tag by clicking on the Edit Use Tags button that appears on any Surefire components where Use Tags are employed to manage access to that component.
Edit Use Tags buttons include a dynamic display component: The numbers of Exclude and Except For Users and/or User Groups that have been directed to not have or, as an exception to that direction, have access to the component are displayed as numbers inside an orange box and green circle respectively. These concepts of Exclude and Except For are described in more detail below.
Configure Use Tags
Select Edit Use Tags.
Two functionality components exists: Exclude Tags and Except For Tags.
Exclude Tags Surefire Users or User Groups that are added as an Exclude Tag for a given component of the CRM will not see that component listed as an available option when using the CRM. For example, if a Surefire User has been added as an Exclude Tag for an image asset, then that user will not see that image listed when viewing images in the Surefire Media Library.
To Add a User or User Group to the list of Exclude Tags type all or part of their name into the Exclude Tags field. The system uses predictive text to list any available Users or User Groups in the system that match with whatever partial name you type.
Once the User or User Group you wish to add to the list is displayed below the field, click on it to select it.
Users or User Groups that have been added to the list of Exclude Tags for this CRM component are displayed as individual icons above the Exclude Tags field.
To Remove a User or User Group from a list of Exclude Tags for this CRM component by clicking on the X on the right-hand side of the corresponding icon that's displayed above the Exclude Tags field. Thus, in the example pictured above, to remove the User Group Surefire Events as and Exclude Tag, you would simply click on the X on the right-hand side of the orange icon.
Except For Tags Surefire Users or User Groups that are added to the list of "Except for Tags" for a given CRM component will be explicitly excluded from the "Exclude Tags" list for this Tag. That is, they will see that component listed as an available option when using the CRM even if they are part of a User Group that has been added as an Exclude Tag. Except For Tag list entries are added, deleted, and displayed in exactly the same way that Exclude Tag list entries are as described above.
Manage Tags
Tags can be applied to multiple assets, resources, and entries across Surefire, it's important to have a centralized place within the CRM where you can manage them all.
To Manage Tags, go to CRM Settings, Manage Tags. Here you can create, edit, and categorize your tags for easy access and search ability.

CRM Master Settings
Tags
Manage Tags
Since Tags can be applied to so many assets, resources and entries across Surefire, it's important to have a centralized place within the CRM where you can manage them all.
In the CRM Settings, Manage Tags screen is divided into 3 tabs, Tags, Categories, Tag Cloud each with several subordinate sections and functions.
Tags Tab
On this tab, Tags that have been entered into Surefire are displayed in a sortable, interactive table.
You can filter which Categories of Tags are displayed in the table by selecting the Filter Tags Types and then, in the ensuing pop-up, using the checkboxes to select or de-select Tag categories.
You can add new Tags and Tag Categories using the corresponding buttons.
Tags that have been added, but have not had a category assigned to them will appear in the table with Needs Verification displayed as a link in the Categories column. Click the link to launch a pop-up window in which you can categorize the Tag.
You can search for a Tag by name using the Search field, also located above the table.
You can edit and delete existing Tags using the buttons in the Actions column.
Edit Tags
When, for any Tag listed in the table, you click on the Edit Tag button in the Actions column, an Edit Tag pop-up appears.
Two types of Tag attributes that are managed here
Enter a Tag Name
(required) and Enter a Category Name
(optional).
The system uses predictive text to list any available Categories already in the system that match with whatever partial Category name you type.
Use Tags Editor
Select Edit Use Tags button on the Edit Tag screen to access the Use Tags Editor.
This is where you can manage what Surefire contacts or organizational units will have access to apply and use this Tag.
Merge Duplicate Tags
Once your organization begins using Tags, it is likely you'll have Duplicate Tags. You can manage these by choosing multiple tags and merging them into one tag. Start by searching for and clicking the checkboxes next to the Tags you want to merge together. Once you have all the Tags selected Hit the Merge Tags button and the Manage Tags pop-up will display.
Here you will select which Tag you want to replace all the other Tags you selected.
After selecting the Primary Tag, the Target Tags will auto-populate with the remaining Tags that will be merged.
Categories Tab
On this tab, Tag Categories that have been entered into Surefire are displayed in a sortable, interactive table.
You can add new Tags and Categories using the corresponding buttons, and you can search for a Category by name using the Search field, also located above the table.
You can edit a Category's name or delete a Category using the buttons in the Actions column.
Tag Cloud Tab
On this tab, you can see a table listing Tags ranked by Most Used within Surefire (with the number of uses listed in the Count column).
You will also see a "Word Cloud" which is a visual representation of Tag usage frequency, where the names of Tags that have been more frequently applied appear larger.
Objects [Tag Name] is Assigned to For any given Tag in the Word Cloud, click on either the number in the "Count" column or on the Tag name as displayed in the 'Word Cloud' to see the Objects [Tag Name] is Assigned to pop-up shows where the Tag is being used.
