CRM Master Settings
Tags
Allow Users to Add Contact Tags
This feature eliminates the regular need to manage and merge Tags by an Admin.
Standard Users and any Non-Admin roles should have the following permissions set up in CRM Settings > Roles/Permissions in order to add Existing Tags to a contact record (must be set by an Admin):
The User can select an available Tag from the dropdown as the search is entered and click Like or Dislike to add the Tag to the contact record if an appropriate one already exists. Start by navigating to Contacts, View All Contacts and open a contact. In the Overview screen click the Add Tag hyperlink.
If the User types out the entire Tag name/description and is able to click Like or Dislike then that Tag either already exists in the dropdown (within the company) and the pre-existing Tag will be honored - no duplicate Tag will be created - or the User has been given the permission to create a Tag.
If no appropriate matching Tag exists in the dropdown (within the company), the "Like" and "Dislike" buttons will not be activated, and the User will not be able to add the typed Tag. For a User to add a Tag not pre-existing within the dropdown, the user would need to have the Create-Tag permission (shown below).
From the Edit Permissions screen for the Role you want, scroll to find CRM Admin Settings then locate Tags and toggle to under Create.
If the User has the Create Tag permission, then when the full Tag name is entered and no pre-existing Tags of the same name exist, the Like or Dislike will be available to select, and a new Tag will be created within the company and will be available for others to use.
To Remove a Tag from a contact record, simply click the red or green X.

Administrators can create and use Rules to automate nearly any action within the CRM. This can range from assigning Leads and sending auto responder emails to both the User and Lead to assigning Tasks and Updating Fields when a Deal moves to a new pipeline stage in a Sales Process.
Essentially, any action taken or change made within Surefire can potentially be used as a trigger to perform a host of further actions. Put simply, a rule is composed of the following elements:
Evaluation Criteria
Conditions
Actions

CRM Master Settings
Rules
Create a Rule
Create a Rule Surefire Administrators can create and use Rules to automate nearly any action within the CRM. This can range from assigning Leads and sending autoresponder emails to both the User and Lead to assigning Tasks and Updating Fields when a Deal moves to a new pipeline stage in a Sales Process.
Essentially, any action taken or change made within Surefire can potentially be used as a trigger to perform a host of further actions. Put simply, a rule is composed of the following elements:
Evaluation Criteria
Conditions
Actions
Settings
To Create a Rule, go to CRM Settings, Custom Rules and click the Create Rule button. The first step is to Name and Save the Rule to a directory location.
Rule Library Location
Library Locations can range from parent company all the way down to a specific user. A waterfall effect is essentially in place with Rule Libraries. So if a rule is created in the parent company profile, then it is subject to being activated for all users. On the same note, if a rule is created in a child company, then that rule is only subject to users within that child company and any child companies within.
Products & Sales Process
If you want a Rule to involve a Product and/or Sales Process, you will adjust that setting here by selecting the Product and/or Sales Process from the dropdown.
Criteria
In the act of building a Rule, the first step is to define the object and event occurrence that determine if the rule should be evaluated.
For example, this could be When a Contact is Created or When a Deal is Created or Edited. A Rule cannot begin to function without this step.
Condition Groups
If the above base Evaluation Criteria are satisfied (e.g. New Contact is Created), then the system will next determine if the subsequent trigger Conditions are met to determine whether or not to Run the Rule.
Conditions can range from the simple (e.g. State equals California) to the complex (e.g. State equals California AND Loan Purpose is equal to Purchase AND Lead Source is to REA Partner OR Trulia).
Actions
Once the Criteria and Conditions are defined, you next choose what Actions you want Surefire to take when this Rule is triggered. There is a wide range of Actions ranging from Deploying Content to Adding Tasks.
Actions can be set to occur Immediately or time-delayed to run at a later Date/Time.

CRM Master Settings
Rules
Add Rule Conditions and Groups
After Setting Rule Evaluation Criteria, the object and event triggers and the conditional style, the next major element of Creating a Rule is Adding Rule Conditions. Once the Evaluation Criteria are met, the system will check to see if the Rule Conditions satisfy the requirements to run the rule.
Keep in mind that the evaluation criteria settings establish what condition fields should be used in conjunction with the overall objective of the rule in order to function properly.
If your criteria setting is When a CONTACT is added/edited... then your conditions should be limited to CONTACT fields. You should not use PRODUCT fields or PHASES as conditions.
If your criteria setting is When a DEAL is added/edited... then your conditions can use CONTACT and PRODUCT fields, but should not use PHASES.
If your criteria setting is When a SALES PHASE is added/edited... then ALL field types can be used as conditions.
If your criteria setting is When a TEXT MESSAGE is received... then your condition is limited to only the Text Message.
If your criteria setting is When a RATE ALERT is received... Then ALL conditions are available.
To Add a Condition, click the Add a Condition button.
If you try to Save a Rule without creating at least one condition, you will receive a warning. This is because a rule without a Condition will run every time that its Rule Evaluation Criteria (e.g. Contact is Edited) occurs. This will likely be more often than needed
Add Rule Condition
A Rule Condition is a statement that must evaluate as "true" in order for the condition to be met. Some examples of a Rule Condition are:
State equals Ohio
Loan Amount is greater than or equal to $600,000
Credit Score is not empty
Text Message is equal to STOP
The following elements comprise a Rule Condition statement:
Conditional Style
Fields
Evaluation Criteria
Value Criteria
Conditional Style
Similarly to Conditional Style when you Set Rule Evaluation Criteria, you must set a Conditional Style for each Condition Group. By default, Condition Groups will start off set to All.
All This is an And option. If you create more than one condition, all of them must evaluate as "true" in order for the Rule Actions to run. Below is a simple example. A Contact must meet both of these requirements (State equal to California and Loan Type equal to VA) to trigger the rule.
Any This is an Or option. With this option, if any of the multiple conditions evaluate as True the Rule triggers and the Rule Actions run. Here is a simple example showing an Any Condition based upon Lead Source as well as another based on Title and Mobile fields.
Fields
The next step for setting the Rule Condition is to define the Field(s
) that are part of the Condition. Simply pull the dropdown to find the Field or alternately search in the field box to pull it up.
By default, all Contact fields, including Custom Fields, are available. If you select a Product and Sales Process, you will also have access to their respective Product Fields and Sales Process Phases.
Evaluation Parameters
Select the Evaluation Parameters of the Field Value . Depending on the Field Type (e.g. Number, Date, Text, etc.) you will have different evaluation options.
Examples include but are not limited to:
Field Type
Evaluation Options Text equal to not equal to contains does not contain starts with ends with is empty is not empty Number equal to not equal to greater than less than greater than or equal to less than or equal to is empty is not empty Date equal to is empty is not empty is newest between exact dates between month and days between relative days before date after date between relative month/day before relative date after relative date
While most of these Evaluation Options are self-evident, there are a few worth taking note of: Not Equal To - when you use this option, you will return the entire universe of Contacts excluding those that match. This might be more than you need.
For example, if you enter State does not equal Idaho, this will return every Contact without this value. Even Contacts with an empty State field will match. Between Month and Days - This option allows you to choose a date range of Month (e.g. January and April) and Day (e.g. 4th and 10th) independent of the actual year.
In the previous example would be triggered on all values between January 4 and April 10 for that field. This could be useful for Date fields like Loan Anniversary or Birthdate. Between Relative Days - This option allows you to look backward and forwards across a range of a fixed number of days. For example, if you want to trigger an email based off of any New Contacts with a Desired Closing Date within 30 days.
Select the Desired Closing Date field and use the Relative Date field to set the Evaluation Parameters to read 0 Days Ago ("0" corresponds to Today) and 30 Days From Now.
Value Criteria
After you have selected the Field and Evaluation Criteria you enter the Value Criteria. This is the actual value for the field that will trigger the rule. Different Field Types have different Value Criteria options.
Field Type
Value Criteria Input
Text/Number
Manual input
Dropdown/Radio/Checkbox
Choose from the option list
Date
Calendar picker
For the system State field, you can select multiple states without having to add new Conditions.
Add a Condition Group
Your entire Rule is made up of one or more Condition Groups. When you begin entering in the first Condition, this is included in your first Condition Group. You don't necessarily need to add additional Groups.
If you select an All Conditional Style, then all you really need to do is add as many Conditions as you want to the first Group since they all need to be fulfilled. There is no further nuance to your Rule.
But if you wish to add an, either between two Conditional Groups or within a Conditional Group, you will need to add a new Condition Group. To do this, click the Add a Condition Group button which will create a new Condition Group Section.
An example of a moderately complex rule that would require more than one Condition Group would be:
State equals Pennsylvania, Alaska, Texas or South Carolina; AND Loan Purpose equals Purchase; AND Lead Source equals REA Partner; OR Lead Source equals Zillow
In a Rule the Condition Groups would look like this:
Remove Conditions and Groups
If in the course of editing your Rule you wish to remove a single Condition or an entire Condition Group, click and confirm your choice.
To remove a Condition, you need to hover your mouse over anywhere in the Condition and appears on the left. For the Condition Group, is permanently displayed in the top right.
To instantly remove conditions moving forward, on the pop-up confirmation window you can click the checkbox to bypass the delete confirmation process.

CRM Master Settings
Rules
Add Rule Actions
After creating the Evaluation Criteria and Rule Conditions, your final step in Creating a Rule is to define what Actions you want Surefire to take when the conditions are met.
Possible Actions that you can automate from Rules is:
Add a tag
Add a task
Add/Remove Workflow
Assign contact to user
Deploy content
Deploy print content
Remove tag
Rule Action Button (Webhook)
Update contact data
Update contact type / life cycle status
Update lead score
Text Message triggered Actions are limited to:
Add a tag
Remove a tag
Remove from Workflow
To add an Action to a Rule, click the Add an Action button. There are no limits to the number of actions you can add and all actions can be set to occur immediately or can be set for varied times into the future.
Action Timing
Each Rule Action has the same Timing Setting Options. This tells Surefire when you want the Action to occur.
By default, the system will run the Action automatically with the Timing Type set to Delay for 0 Minutes. If you want to delay the Action, you can assign a whole number (e.g. 1, 3, 10, etc.) and choose a time increment type from:
Minutes
Hours
Days
If you have added any Actions with delayed timing, the Action Summary section will show all Actions with their respective timing:
Add a Tag
When adding a Tag, type the name of the tag in the Tags box. When you see what you are looking for, select it from the dropdown.
After you click Apply, the Rule will now add the Tag to whatever Contact or Deal that triggers this Rule.
You cannot Create a Tag from this section. If you want to apply a new Tag with this Rule, you will first need to Create a New Tag.
Add a Task
You can use a Rule to assign a Task to yourself or another User in Surefire. This will then appear in the My Tasks section of the Calendar for the assigned User.
After entering a Name and Details, you can complete the following other Action fields: Priority - select between High, Medium and Low Priority for your Task.
Days Until Due (required) -
This is the number of days from when it is created that the Task is marked due. 0 indicates it is due the day the Task is created, 1 is the day after it was created and so on.
This date is not the date the Rule is triggered but the date the Task is created. Let's look at a simple chronological example:
Rule triggers (9/1)
Action is set for a Task to be created 3 days after Rule Trigger (9/4)
The Task Days Until Due is set to 2 (9/6)
So in the above we see that the Task Due date is set to 9/6 as that is two days after the Task Creation (9/4) and not the Rule Trigger date (9/1). Activity - select between the Activity Type options of To Do, Phone and Other.
Assignee
(required) -The most critical element is assigning the Task to the appropriate User. You can select from these options: Contact Owner - This assigns the Task to whatever User owns the Contact at the time the Task is created. Specific User - select a User from a list of all Company Users from Companies you have access to. Team Member - if you have Team Member Slots created in your Company you can select from among them here.
The Team Member Slot will always be the one associated with the Owner of the Contact/Deal that triggers the Rule.
If a triggering User has an empty Team Member Slot, the Task is skipped.
Add a Sales Process
To Add a Sales Process, select the Sales Process of Choice from the list and select Apply.
Add/Remove Workflow
To Add a Workflow, select the Workflow in the Workflow to add list, select to whom you want it applied (Contact and/or Spouse), and select Apply.
To Remove a Workflow, select the Workflow in the Remove other workflows list, choose to whom you want it applied (Contact, Spouse and/or Co-Owner(s)), toggle the switch to Force remove from the workflow, and hit Apply.
You can Add and Remove workflows in the same action.
Assign Contact to User
Assigning a Contact to a User is the Action to use if you want to assign incoming Leads to sales. To Assign a User, select the desired one from the dropdown and select Apply.
Deploy Content Deploying Content as a Rule Action is very similar to Creating a Deployment in the Deployment Center only without the Audience Builder element.
You are presented with a version of the Media Library from which you can follow these steps to Deploy Content Collection.
Navigate or search to find the Content Collection you want
Under the Media Type column, click the Media icon to Preview, this is optional.
Complete the Preview steps.
Select Content Collection to use.
Under the Available Media Types section, select Use under the Media Type you want to Deploy.
You cannot Deploy Social as an Action.
For Content Collections with multiple Media Types, you can only Deploy a single type per Action. If you want to Deploy more than one Media Type from the same Collection you need to create a separate Action.
Email
Recipient Type

(e.g. Spouse, Co-Brand)

This may allow other Users running this Rule to send Deployments to your selected contact.

Text Message Options

Using this option, if you exceed your daily number of Text Message sends, the overflow will not be sent.

To remove a Tag, type the name of the tag in the Remove Tags box. When you see what you are looking for, select it from the list. You can also remove a tag(s) through category. Simply click on the box Remove By Tag Category and choose the desired tag category. Then click Apply.
The Rule is now set to remove the designated tag from the Contact once the conditions that trigger the Rule are met.

Webhook must be turned on and properly configured by your account administrator in order for this action to successfully process. If turned off, webhook actions are skipped.
Update Contact Data
This Action will allow you to update any Contact Field with a new value. After you select the Field to Update, you will have two options for the Value Type of the Field:
Field Value
Choose another Contact Field from the Value From Existing Field dropdown. This will update the previously selected field with the current value of your newly selected Existing Field.
Manual Value
Enter in a value to update for any Text or Number fields. For Dropdown and other fields with preset values, choose from the existing options.
Drop-down, Checkbox, and Radio field types are only able to take Manual Values.
You can also add more than one Field to Update from within the same action by clicking the Add More button. You can delete any additional updates by selecting and confirming.

You can change the Contact Type and/or Lifecycle Status using this option. You have two settings on this Action: Contact Type (required) - Choose from the dropdown the Contact Type to change to. Lifecycle Status - Depending on the Contact Type selected, you will have available all of the Lifecycle Statuses associated with that Type. Choose the one to update to.
If you just want to change the Lifecycle Status, select the Contact Type that the Contact should already be in and then set the Lifecycle Status.
Update Lead Score
You can use a Rule to automatically update a Lead Score on a Lead. Simply use the slider to indicate the amount that you wish to increase/decrease the Lead Score by.
This is the number of points you are changing the score by, not the actual Lead Score. For example:
A Lead has a Lead Score of 25
A Rule is Triggered with a setting of Update Lead Score by 10
The New Lead Score is 35 (25 + 10); not 1

Create a Birthday Rule
A Birthday Rule monitors all contacts that have birthdays and then deploys chosen content to them on their special day.
You can configure a Birthday Rule's subscription settings to automatically subscribe users in your company to it. Alternatively, you can allow users to subscribe to your Birthday Rule via the Deployment Center.
You may want to periodically change what content is deployed by your Birthday Rule so that the same birthday email is not going out year after year.
Go to CRM Settings, Custom Rules.
Select Create Rule.
In the Name field, enter a name for your Birthday Rule.
In the Library field, choose which Company's folder you want to save this Rule to (and therefore which Company's users you want to have access to the rule).
Select the following from the list:
When - a contact is - monitored and after - all of the following conditions are met...
Select Add a Condition Group and add the following condition:
Contact Birthday between relative month/day "0" x Days Ago and "0" x Days From Now Note that between relative month/day 0 x Days Ago and 0 x Days From Now effectively means the current day's date to the system.
Select Add an Action.
Select Deploy Content.
In the Add an Action, select the timing of when your Birthday Rule will be run.
Select Open Media Library button.
In the Media Library, Collections list, navigate to display the content you want to be deployed to Contacts on their birthday.
As an example, you may want to expand the Public folder then expand the Digital Greetings folder, where you can then click on the Birthday Greetings to view previously authored birthday-related content.
Click Select button next to the Birthday Greeting you want to use.
Select Use to see Available Media Types.
In Recipient Type select Contact from the list.
Select CC on the deployment field is optional. An example might be Contact-Owner (Myself).
Select an Opt Out List.
Click Apply.
Configure your Birthday Rule's subscription settings.
There are three types of Rule Subscription Scenarios that can be applied to any given rule:
Users are Subscribed by default to the Rule and cannot Unsubscribe from it - In this "set-it and forget-it" scenario, all new contacts added that have birth dates will be added to this rule.
Users are Subscribed by default to the Rule and can Unsubscribe from it
Users are not Subscribed by default to the Rule and can Subscribe and/or Unsubscribe from it - In this "set-it and forget-it" scenario, users will have to subscribe to the rule via the deployment center.
Select Create Rule.

CRM Master Settings
Rules
Set Rule Evaluation Criteria
In the act of Creating a Rule, the first step is to define the Object and Event combination that will trigger rule evaluation. Building these evaluation criteria tells Surefire that when this change happens in the CRM, you want it to check to see if any additional rule criteria are met.
For example, this could be When a Contact is Added or When a Deal is Added or Edited. A Rule cannot begin to function without this step.
There are three components to this evaluation:
Object Trigger -
When Event Trigger - is Conditional Style - and after
Choose Object
This is the Object in the CRM that the Rule checks for changes against. You can select:
A Contact
A Deal
A Sales Phase
A Text Message
A Text Message Object Trigger will most often be used in conjunction with a Nudge Workflow.
Review Nudge Workflow for additional information.
A Rate Alert
If you want to use a Deal, Sales Phase, or Rate Ale rt as the Object Trigger, you need to Add a Product or Sales Process under the Rule Settings.
Event Trigger
The Event Trigger indicates what needs to happen in the CRM to set off the evaluation criteria. The types of events are:
Added/Edited
Added
Edited
Monitored
Date Fields (such as Contact Birthday) is a required condition to be used for this type of Event Trigger
When monitoring, a record does not have to change to trigger the rule, i.e. an event outside the contact record, such as today equaling a loan anniversary, can trigger the rule
To further customize and/or narrow a monitored rule event trigger conditions, Contact Types and Product Fields (if a product is included in the rule settings) are available and can be added once a Date Field has been input
The use of Sales Phases is prohibited with monitored rules, and the Surefire system will not allow it.
Received
Rules set to trigger via Text Message or Rate Alert, trigger only as a result of Received (or inbound) Text Messages or Alerts
The Event Trigger is the what and the Object Trigger as the where. For example, you select:
Contact as the Object Trigger
Added as the Event Trigger
Every time a Contact is Added, the rule will be evaluated and checked to see if the Rule Conditions apply. However, if a Contact is Edited, it will not be evaluated.
Conversely, if you select:
Contact as the Object Trigger
Edited as the Event Trigger
The rule will be evaluated when you
Edit the Contact
(e.g. change the State to California and Save the Contact.) But if a New Contact enters the system, either through manual input or via a Lead Form, the rule will not be evaluated under this scenario.
However, if you were to select Added/Edited as the event trigger, then both of the above rule scenarios would be evaluated.
Generally speaking, you will usually want to use Added/Edited unless there is a very specific scenario you are trying to accommodate. This most often involves rules that you want to run only upon Contact Creation where Added would be the most applicable setting.
Conditional Style
The final component you must set is a Conditional Style. Here you are telling Surefire for the Rule Conditions I am about to set any (or all) must be met to run the rule.
Any This is an Or option. With this option, if any of the multiple conditions evaluate as True the Rule triggers and the Rule Actions run.
All This is an And option. If you create more than one condition, all of them must evaluate as True in order for the Rule Actions to run.

CRM Master Settings
Rules
Set Condition Groups For Building a Rule
In this video, along with creating a rule, you will need to know how to set your condition group for that specific rule. A Rule Condition is a statement that must evaluate as True in order for the condition to be met.

Rules
Add Products and Sales Processes to Rules
If you would like your Rule to access the Fields on Products and Phases in Sales Process, you must add a Product and/or Sales Process on the Settings section of your Rule.
When you add a Product, you'll automatically have access to all of its associated Product Fields from the Field dropdown. You can build conditions with these fields the same as you would with Contact Fields.
For Sales Processes, you will have access to all of the associated Sales Phases.
Using Sales Phases as Conditions
Building Conditions with Sales Phases is slightly different than with Products. The value of a Phase is considered to be a Date Field as it really representing its Phase Achieved Date. As such, the Condition Evaluation Criteria is as follows:
For most Rule Conditions, you will want to use Phase as a trigger when it is completed. For example, you want a Rule for new applications to start when the Phase equals Application.
To accomplish this, you must build a condition that indicates the Phase Achievement Date is Today. This is done using the Between Relative Dates criteria and should be constructed as :
As 0 represents Today in the Between Relative Days operator, building a statement as such tells the Rule to trigger when the Phase - Application Achievement Date is between Today and Today.
If you wish to extend back to the previous day (to hedge against a scenario where someone is updating a Phase a day late) you could add 1 or 2 to the X Days Ago section.

You can view and manage all of your Company's current active and paused rules:
Go to CRM Settings, Custom Rules. Rules are presented in a summary table.
Besides the standard system columns, there are:
Status
Published - Live rule
Paused - Live rule that has been Paused so that it is not currently running
Draft - Rule that has not yet been Published
Invalid - Something has gone wrong with the Rule Conditions and requires editing. For instance, a Custom Field or Product that are part of the Rule have been deleted.
Library - Indicates where in the Company folder structure the Rule is saved Product and Sales Process - If either have been associated in Rule Settings they will show here
Search Filters and Tags
You can search for any Rules by Name or Tag. You can also Filter by Status.

By default, you will view all of the Rules that reside within the top Company you belong to. To drill down to see Rules saved on the Company level, click the Toggle Folder View to see a Company Library View.
Edit, Clone, Pause/Resume, Save Draft/Publish
From the main Rules page, you can select at the end of the row to manage the Rules.
The following menu options are available:
Edit
Clone
Pause
Delete
Pause and Resume
If you have a live rule that you want to stop working for whatever reason, you can use the Pause option in the menu. You can also go to the Rules Detail for a Rule and click the Pause button.
Conversely, if the Rule Status is currently Paused, this option will be Resume and you can select it to have the Rule resume running under its current conditions.
While a Rule is Paused, not only will it not trigger and run, but also it will not go back and search for any Contacts/Deals that met its criteria while Paused. Only Contacts/Deals that meet its conditions moving forward will trigger and run.
Save and Publish
While you are building a Rule, once you click Create Rule you will Publish the Rule and it is live. If you still have more work to do on your Rule, you can immediately Pause the Rule and then Edit to continue making changes.
When the Rule is ready, select Resume.

Rules
Subscribe to a Rule
A Rule's subscription settings determine whether or not Surefire Users will have that rule applied to their Surefire account and its contents, including Deployment Center Campaigns.
Furthermore, the subscription settings can determine whether or not users can choose to unsubscribe their account from that rule.
Types of Rule Subscription Scenarios
There are three types of Rule Subscription Scenarios that can be applied to users included in and below the library folder designated for a given rule:
Users are Subscribed by default to the Rule and cannot Unsubscribe from it
Users are Subscribed by default to the Rule and can Unsubscribe from it
Users are not Subscribed by default to the Rule and can Subscribe and/or Unsubscribe from it
Modify a Rule's Subscription Settings
Go to CRM Settings, Custom Rules.
Select for the Rule you want to modify Subscription settings.
Select Edit.
Use the Allow Unsubscribe and/or Default Subscribe lists to determine the subscription scenario for this rule.
Select options:
If Allow Unsubscribe is set to No then Default Subscribe is set to All Subscribed by default.
If Allow Unsubscribe was previously set to Yes and is changed to No, then all existing manual subscriptions will be removed and users included in, and below, the library folder designated for this rule are automatically subscribed.
If Allow Unsubscribe is set to Yes then in the Default Subscribe select All Subscribed
Users are Subscribed to the Rule and can Unsubscribe from it
If Allow Unsubscribe is set to Yes then in the Default Subscribe select All Unsubscribed
Users are not Subscribed by default to the Rule and can Subscribe and/or Unsubscribe from it
If Allow Unsubscribe was previously set to No and is changed to Yes, then all existing manual subscriptions will be removed and users included in, and below, the library folder designated for this rule are able to subscribe to the rule, if they choose to.

Equity Alerts
Equity Alerts are notifications that are generated when a borrower’s home equity reaches a certain value threshold or changes significantly. These alerts signify potential refinancing, home equity loan, or HELOC opportunities.
You can set equity alerts for a client’s loan in Master Settings.
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select more options.
Choose Opportunity Alerts.
Select the Principle and Equity - Settings tab.
Set thresholds, as applicable, to activate an alert:
Estimated Annual Appreciation section set a percentage of home value appreciation, above which will trigger an alert to the borrower indicating a significant increase in their home equity.
Equity Alert Settings section set: Alert Threshold field between 1-100 which, when reached, will trigger the system to send an alert the borrower. Alert Active Duration field sets the number of days that the alert will remain on a hot list between 1-365. Time Interval Period field establishes the number of days (1-1000) between achieving the threshold and the time a new alert will be sent out.
Select Save Appreciation Rates and/or Save Alert Settings.

CRM Master Settings
Upload Data via API Upload Data via API Surefire Uploader API turns on the automated upload of Loan Files & Loan Data. When a third-party sync agent for an LOS system, for example, calls the Surefire uploader API, the system creates and queues a job in the Surefire Data Management system.
In order to create a job, two keys are required. An APIKey and a ClientKey.
APIKey
A representative at Surefire must create an APIKey. Only admins can retrieve this key.
Go to My Company, Company Info.
Select API.
Locate Key.
The Key that an admin needs, is the Data Integration Policy Key. Some admins may see a Public API Policy Key, that is not needed for utilizing the uploader to process data.
If an APIKey is not present submit a support ticket or email Surefire support@ice.com.
ClientKey
A ClientKey can be found by going to any user profile and selecting the Integrations item in the Horizontal menu.
The ClientKey is the Zapier Key
If an integration is set at a company level, then an admin's ClientKey must be used for routing data to various users. A lower tiered user's ClientKey would not be able to load data to another user that is not below that user in the role/company hierarchy.
If an integration with a 3rd party is required, then it is suggested that a user profile for that 3rd party be created, most likely admin level for ClientKey use. The name of that user profile is what is important as when that 3rd party delivers data to add/update a contact, both the upload job and the contact history will then denote that the 3rd party was responsible for the add/update.
A data upload job will include details such as:
Who created the job
Who the job is assigned to The job name
Whether the job is initiated manually or via API Whether the upload is for User or Contact Records
A Mapping Tag, the unique identifier for the data field map that's to be used and applied during this upload a .json file containing the data objects that are to be imported
Data upload jobs can also be manually initiated from within Surefire.
Data uploads are viewed, managed, and in the cases of non-third-party initiated jobs, created under CRM Settings, Data Upload.
Third-Party Sync Agent Initiated Data Uploads
Through connecting to Surefire 's uploader API, a third-party sync agent can create a data upload job, specify the data type being uploaded (User or Contact), specify which data field map to use and finally, upload the json data file containing the data objects that are to be processed.
Destination URL for the Surefire Data Uploader API Type: HTTP POST
Production environment
Sandbox environment
Authentication
Key Value pairs included in the Body (see next section) must contain the following tokens:
Body
The following key value pairs should be passed over (a summary is provided in the table below). A Mapping Tag - This key determines which data field map is supposed to be used to map the field columns included in the attached JSON file.
This key value is not required. When not present, the data file for this job will not be auto-processed, and the job will be queued in the Surefire data upload system as a draft.
A Type identifier -
This key determines whether the job is intended to create new users or new contacts.
0 = Users
1 = Contacts
This key value is not required. When Type is left blank, the system defaults to a value of 1, i.e. Contacts.
JSON Filename
-The file which contains a json formatted list of fields to be uploaded. Files must have a column that provides a unique indicator so that users for contacts may be identified. The map selected must also have a column chosen that determines where the unique userid exists.
Request Parameters
Required or Optional
Value Details type
Opt
0 (user), 1 (contacts). defaults to 1 if not provided
Determines whether the job is intended to create new users or create new contacts. mappingtag Opt any string including the following (^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$)
Determines which map within SF3 is supposed to be used to map the field columns in the attached file. file
Req
<JSON file attached>
The file which contains a json formatted list of fields to be uploaded.  Files must have a column that provides a unique indicator so that users for contacts may be identified.  The map selected must also have a column chosen that determines where the unique userid exists.
Sample API Request for Data Upload Job Creation curl --location --request POST 'https://apigateway.tomnx.com/sf3api/ip/uploader/jobs' \
--header 'apikey: INSERT APIKEY HERE' \
--header 'clientkey: INSERT CLIENTKEY HERE' \
--header 'Content-Type: application/json' \
--form 'file=@INSERT FILE NAME HERE' \
--form 'mappingtag=INSERT MAPPING TAG NAME HERE'
Data Uploader Responses
There are a few common responses the Uploader API may return.
Success with Mapping
{"data":{"id":1811,"hasMapping":true,"message":"Job as been successfully queued for processing."}}
Success with no Mapping (Job is created, but not auto-processed, and therefore queued as a draft)
{"data":{"id":1813,"hasMapping":false,"message":"No mapping template found for the mapping tag provided. Job created in Draft status. Please login to SF system to assign mapping and process the job. "}}
Failure, No File Attached
{"error":"file is a required parameter for this action"}
Failures, Authorization
Numerous possible errors, including "error": "Authorization field missing" or “Key not authorized” or “Key expired”

Rate Sheet API allows mortgage lenders and financial institutions to manage and distribute rate sheet data such as interest rates, loan programs, and pricing adjustments across LOS Systems or consumer facing portals.
API design benefits are:
Automation - turns on real-time updates to pricing engines and borrower portals.
Accuracy- reduces manual errors in rate distribution.
Efficiency - supports dynamic pricing strategies and compliance.
The Rate Sheet API supports the four main HTTP operations POST, GET, PUT, and DELETE. You can use: POST to Create New Rate Sheet Entries and add new rate sheet data such as a new loan program or pricing tier.
Example: A lender introduces a new 30-year fixed-rate product. GET to Retrieve Rate Sheet Data and fetch rate sheet information for display or processing.
Example: A loan officer queries current rates for FHA loans. PUT to Update Existing Rate Sheet Entries and modify an existing rate sheet entry.
Example: Update the rate for a specific product due to market changes. DELETE to Remove Rate Sheet Entries and Delete outdated or incorrect rate sheet entries.
Example: Remove a discontinued loan product.

CRM Master Settings
Rate Sheet API Rate Sheet API Details
Rate Sheet API Details
Using the API with SPS you can:
Create a Public API endpoint that accepts program and state adjustment data on behalf of an organization
Validate each program field as the correct type and format before accepting data
Support 50 US States
Accepted Operations: POST for new Programs and State Adjustments. GET for list of Programs. PUT for updating existing Programs or State Adjustments. DELETE for deleting Programs.
The following values are calculated in SPS: Total Loan Amount, First Loan Payment, Cost of APR, and APR and calculated as follows:
Total Loan Amount is calculated based on loan to value, sales price, and the vaff rate.
First Loan Payment is calculated using the fields for program rate, term in months, and the Total Loan Amount.
Cost of APR is calculated based on the first loan average, other rate, point rate, lender credit rate, Total Loan Amount, MI/PMI, continuance in months, program rate, loan to value, sales price, and pre-paid interest days.
APR is calculated using the standard rate function and passing in: terms in months, First Loan payment, and (Total Loan Amount minus Cost of APR)
Review APR Calculations in SPS for additional information on APR.

Value used for the Lender Credit Rate field. Calculations will be based on the associated type field. Percent will use a value calculated based on the Total Loan Amount. Dollar will use the value directly in calculations. lender_credit_rate_type string false false
Type field for the associated Lender Credit Rate field. This field is used to determine how the lender credit rate amount is calculated. months_of_taxes integer false false
The number of months of taxes to be used in calculations. months_of_ins integer false false
The number of months of insurance to be used in calculations. months_of_pmi integer false false
The number of months of PMI to be used in calculations. continuance_mi_years1 integer false false
The number of months or years of continuance of MI. The associated type field determines how this value is used in calculations. continuance_type string false false
The associated type field for the Continuance MI Years field. This field is used to determine how the continuance value is used in calculations. prepaid_interest_days integer false false
The number of prepaid interest days to be used in calculations. months_of_hoa_condo_fee integer false false
The number of months of HOA or Condo Fee to be used in calculations. income_quality Integer false false
Income Quality field used in calculations in Single Property Sites. loan_type string true false
Loan Type field. Options are Conforming, NonConforming, FHA, VA, USDARuralHousing. aus string false false
Automated Underwriting Systems. Options are DU, LP, ManualTraditional, or NotSpecified. amortization string true false
The amortization type for the program. Options are fixed or adjustable. arm_fixed_terms string false false
The fixed terms of an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Options are OneYear, TwoYear, ThreeYear, FiveYear, SevenYear, TenYear, and FifteenYear. arm_adjustable_terms integer false false
The adjustable terms of an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. arm_adjustable_interval string false false
The interval for the adjustable terms of an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Options are months or years. arm_first_adjument_cap number false false
The first adjustment cap for an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Must be between 0 and 100. arm_periodic_cap number false false
The periodic cap for an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Must be between 0 and 100. arm_life_cap number false false
The life cap for an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Must be between 0 and 100. arm_margin number false false
Margin for an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Must be between 0 and 100. arm_index_rate number false false
The index rate for an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Must be between 0 and 100. arm_index string false false
The adjustable rate mortgage index. This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Options are 30 Day Average SOFR, 1 Year CMT, COFI, T-BILL, MTA, and UST. arm_floor number false false
The floor rate for an adjustable rate mortgage (ARM). This is a required field when amortization is set to adjustable. Must be between 0 and 100. use_internal_rates boolean false false
Use Internal Rates field. Setting to true will use the program rate provided in the program details. program_category string true false
The name of the program category. This is used to categorize the program in Single Property Sites. This field is accepted in the GET route as a filter when retrieving all programs. state_adjustments array false false
State Adjustments for the Program. This is an array of objects containing a state and an adjustment value. The adjustment value is a decimal representing the rate adjustment for that state defined by the abbreviated state.

allows you to easily import User, Contact or Deal records that are stored in external datafiles (e.g. Excel or .csv files) through the creation and management of Data Upload jobs.
Manual Data Upload jobs are created and managed in CRM Settings, Data Management.
Upload Data Manually
Through creating and then running Data File Upload Jobs, you can manually upload records from outside databases. You can manually upload:
User Accounts
Contact Records
Deals
Upload Data via API In addition to manual upload jobs, you can import data from third-party applications via API.
Review Upload Data via API for additional information.
Tag Data Uploads
When uploading multiple, like-categorized contact records, you can use the Data Uploader to bulk-apply one or more of the same Tags to each record when you import them.
Review Tag Data Uploads for additional information.
Data Maps
The Data Uploader uses Data Import Maps to identify all of the Data Fields in an external data file (for example, the contents of spreadsheet columns labelled First Name, Last Name, Address, etc.) so that those spreadsheet fields can be mapped to the corresponding data fields in Surefire.
Translations
Data Import Maps additionally allow for the application of Translations, where the contents of individual data records included in an external data file can be automatically altered as part of the import process such that their syntax matches your organization's standards. Translations are analogous to running an automated Search-and-Replace on your data during the import process.
Translations Use Case Example
Let's say you have a source datafile spreadsheet containing Contact Records (that have, say, Mortgage Deals included with them) that you want to import into Surefire.
In the spreadsheet, there's a column named "Contact Loan Type" where, for some Contact Records (i.e. rows), the term "FarmHomeAdministration" is entered. But that is not a value that you want ever imported into Surefire since it's not a Loan Type you ever use.
Using Translations, you can direct Surefire 's Data Uploader to replace that term during the upload process with something else (e.g. "Other"). Thus, once that Contact Record is added in Surefire e, for the associated Deal that also gets added, in the Surefire Data Field that's named "Loan Type," the value entered would be "Other."
Review for additional information.
SFTP
SFTP (Secure File Transfer Protocol) allows you to transfer files between systems securely.
Review SFTP in Data Management Upload for additional information.
Quality of Service (Qos) Alerts
Provides notifications for data transfer jobs.
Review QoS Alerts for additional information.
Manage Existing Data Maps
The Data Uploader allows users to save and manage multiple data import maps for re-use and cloning because users tend to import similar data sets on multiple occasions.
Review Manage Data Import Maps for additional information.
Create a Data Map
Data Map is the key driver of how any Data File Upload job is executed therefore, it is important to understand how to create and edit one.
Review for additional information.
Data Import Health Checks
When importing large data sets, your source data might not always directly correspond to how data records are divided and organized in Surefire. Thus, the system requires you to run a diagnostic test import, applying your selected Data Import Map to your source data to see how it will be parsed for import into Surefire, before you actually import the data into Surefire.
This allows you to see how the data will be imported and, if necessary, make changes to your data import mappings and/or translations before running the actual data upload job.
Review Data Upload Health Checks for additional information.
Data Import Duplication Checks
Whenever new data records are imported into Surefire, the system checks to ensure that you are not creating duplicate or conflicting records. The policies that govern these checks include several optional settings.
Data Upload Forensics Reports
After the completion of any Data File Upload Job in Surefire, the system generates an interactive report that includes several details about exactly how and how much of the source data was and was not entered into the system.
Review Data Import Duplication Checks for additional information.
Revert Surefire Data to Pre-Data Upload State
In cases when the results of a data upload job are not satisfactory, the system provides the option of reverting all Surefire records to the state they were in prior to that job being run.
Review Revert Surefire Data to Pre-Data Upload State for additional information.

Be as descriptive as possible while remaining concise; over time, a large number of upload jobs may accrue in your instance of . Be sure you can locate your jobs by name should you need to reference them in the future.

Deals are imported as components of Contact records. Users - the records you are importing are users that you want to create accounts for in Surefire; i.e. you will not be importing any contact records or Deals as part of this job.

You can either Create a New Data Import Map, or you can select a Data Import Map that's already been saved in Surefire.
Use the drop-down to select the folder in Surefire in which the Data Map you want to use has been stored.
(Optional) Narrow down the list of available Data Import Maps by selecting which product the map you want to use has been associated with.
(Optional) Further target your search for the Data Map you want to use by entering a search term or sorting the columns in the table by column header.

Click Apply next to the data map you want to apply.

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Data Upload Health Checks
A Health Check must be run before a Data Upload Job can be processed. A Health Check is a diagnostic test upload that applies your selected Data Import Map to your selected Source Datafile in order to generate a report showing how the contents of that file will be uploaded to Surefire.
Running a Health Check allows you to see how the data will be imported, giving you the opportunity, should you deem it necessary, to make changes to your data mappings, translations and even source data format before running your actual data file upload job.
Run a First-Time Health Check
Create or Select a Data File Upload Job.
Verify a Data Import Map has been selected.
If one has not been, then click the Start Mapping button, you are taken to the Apply Import Map screen and you must complete a data file upload job.
Select Run Health Check button.
The system indicates that the Health Check is processing.
Review the summary of your Data File Upload Job's health under the Data Health section.
In addition to details about the most recent Health Check run for this Data File Upload Job, you'll see the number of records (i.e. rows) included in your Source Data File that, as a result of running this File Upload Job as currently configured, the Health Check indicates will:
Upload Successfully (Good)
Upload, but with possible problems (Warning)
Not upload (Error)
Review and Interpret Health Check Results
Select View Check Results button to launch the Data Health Check Report.
Each row in the displayed table corresponds to a row in your source datafile.
Statuses are Good, Warning or Error.
In Warning and Error rows, the system describes the import issue in the Health Check Message column.
Health Status list at the top of the screen can be used to filter the displayed rows.
The values included in each cell of your source data file are displayed in the File Row Details column, separated by quotation marks.
Re-Run Health Check
After running a Health Check and reviewing its results, you decide you to make changes to your import data mappings or data translations, you can then apply the Health Check function again to see if your changes have improved the results of your test upload.
To run another Health Check on your Data File Upload Job, select Re-Run Health Check.
After the check is run, the Data Health section of the screen gets updated to reflect the results of your most recent Health Check.
The Data Health Check Report screen, accessed via clicking the View Check Results, also gets updated.

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Data Import Duplication Checks
When new data records are imported into Surefire as part of a Data File Upload Job, the system's Duplication Check engine is engaged, running a check to ensure that it is not creating duplicate or conflicting Contact, User or Deal records.
Duplication check policies are managed under Settings, Master Settings, Data Settings. You can find a detailed description of Data Duplication Management in Surefire here.
For the purposes of this example, which will provide a broad overview of Data Duplication functionality as it pertains to Data File Upload Jobs, we are discussing the API Input Channel.
API Input Channel
The API Input Channel of Surefire 's Data Duplication function, which is automatically activated and applied to all Data File Upload Jobs, is divided into three Duplication Policy Sets: Contact, User, and Deal. Contact Duplication Policies - Reviews the contents of Contact-specific data fields for incoming records against the contents of those same fields for all existing Contact records in Surefire.
Example Field Types are: Contact Name, Contact Email Address or Contact Source. User Duplications Policies - Reviews the contents of User-specific data fields for incoming records against the contents of those same fields for all existing User Accounts Surefire.
Example Field Types are: Company Name, User Email, or Username. Deal Duplication Policies - Reviews the contents of Deal-specific data fields for incoming records against the contents of those same fields for all Deals currently setup in Surefire.
Field Types will be Product-specific, but some examples (for a mortgage product) might be: File Number, Closing Date or Credit score.
Data Duplication Checks
For each Duplication Policy Set (Contact, User, and Deal), the system does up to 5 checks, in a prioritized order. For each of those checks, the system compares the contents of one or more incoming data fields (that have been selected for that check when the Policy was setup) against the contents of those same fields in all of Surefire.
The system must pass all of these checks (i.e. confirm that there is no matching data already in the system) before the new data record can be created in the system.
If you are importing a contact record. There might be two Data Duplication Checks setup as part of the Contact Data Duplication Policy:
Check 1 - Contact Last Name and Contact Birthday
Check 2 - Contact Email Address
In this scenario, the system first looks at the data record it's being asked to import, and confirm that there are no Contact Records already in Surefire that have both the same Contact Last Name and the same Contact Birthday (as the incoming record).
Assuming that this check is passed (i.e. that there are no matches), then the system moves on to the second check and confirms that no contacts in Surefire use the email address that is included in the data record that is being imported.
Should the system fail any check, the Contact Record will be updated with the information in the data upload.

Data Upload Forensics Report
After a Data File Upload Job has been processed, the system generates an interactive Post-Process Forensics Report. To review one of these reports,
Select a completed Data File Upload Job.
Select Post-Process Forensics Report.
Report Summary
The top section of the Post-Process Forensics Report pop up is a non interactive summary of the File Data Upload Job and its results.
Across the top of the Report Summary, the system lists the job's name, system-generated id, type, source, source data file name, process time, total rows present in the source data file and total rows processed.
Interactive Row-by-Row Details
The lower section shows your Data File Upload Job details on an operation-by-operation basis. It provides an option to drill down into how each row in your source data file was processed by the system when the job was run.
Select Inspect on any row on the table to see how each of the source data file is processed.
The Operation Drilldown Summary pane is populated with details about how the system processed the contents of that row in your source data file.
The summary is divided into two tabs: displays exactly what was written to Surefire (the User tab in the above pictured example) Raw Row from File, shows the raw data that was in this row of your source data file
In the Search field you can enter all or part of any data string that was included in your source data file. The system filters the list to show only those rows in your source data file that included that term.

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Import Contact Records
You can use the Data Uploader to import Contacts whose details have been stored in an external source, such as a spreadsheet or CSV text file.
Considerations Unique to Importing Contact Records
Ownership
Because all Contacts in Surefire contains a notion of Ownership (i.e. some User in the Organization must Own the relationship with that Contact), when importing Contact records, you will need to tell Surefire which user(s) own(s) those Contact records.
This information can be specified either when creating the Data File Upload Job (in the case when all Contact records being imported are to be assigned to the same, single user) or by mapping the assigned owners, as recorded in your source datafile, to the username field in Surefire (in cases where the source datafile includes a column indicating which Surefire Users own each entry, aka row, in the spreadsheet).
Deals
In Surefire, Deals are recorded as components of Contact Records. Thus, in the context of Data File Upload Jobs, Deals are imported by importing Contact Records that include Deals as component parts.
Review Import Deal Records for additional information.
Import Contact Records
Create a Data File Upload Job, setting the Upload Type to Contacts.
As part of creating a Contact Record Data File Upload Job, you must tell Surefire whether the owner of each contact record is included with each data record you are importing (i.e. as an entry in one of the columns for each row in your source data spreadsheet) or whether you are importing Contact records that should all be assigned to the same, single Surefire user:
When Contact Record Owners are Specified in your Source Datafile.
When there is an entry in one of the columns for each row in your source data spreadsheet that indicates which Surefire user owns the Contact whose details are entered in that row.
Select I will specify users in file to On When You Specify a Single Owner for All of the Contact Records You Are Importing
When you are importing Contact records that should all be assigned to the same, single Surefire user (i.e. now Surefire Users are listed as Contact Owners in your Source Datafile)
Select I will specify users in file to OFF, and then either click on the data field below to reveal a list of Users in your organization, or type in all or part of the name of a Surefire User.
Select the name of the Surefire user to which you want to assign the Contact Records you are importing.
Associate an existing Data Import Map with your Data File Upload Job or Create a New One.
A Contact Record Import Map must have the following three Surefire fields mapped to your source data:
Contact First Name
Contact Last Name
Contact Type
Associate a Product with your Data Import Map.
When importing Contact Records into Surefire, it is often the case that they have multiple Deals (for example, Deals for Mortgage Loans) associated with them that you want the Data Uploader to also import into Surefire. Since the Data Uploader is designed to only upload Deals for one product at a time, you must make that association when setting up your Data Import Map.
Run a Data Import Health Check (aka Test Upload) on your Data File Upload Job.
If necessary, alter your Data Import Map or Source Datafile to ensure your User Account Data is successfully imported.
Select Process Job.
Review Process Data File Upload Job process.

from which you can access the Data Import Map editor and its various tools.
How the Data Import Map editor is used differs slightly depending on whether it is going to be applied to external data files that contain User account details, Contact records or Deals.
To access the Data Import Map editor tool:
Go to CRM Settings, Data Management.
Select Manage Mappings

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Data Import Maps
Data Import Maps, Identify Attributes
Every Data Import Map needs to have some Identifying Attributes defined for it:
Name and Description
Enter a name to this Data Import Map. Be as descriptive as possible while remaining concise; over time, a large number of Data Import Maps may accrue in your instance of Surefire. Be sure you can locate your maps by name should you need to reference them in the future.
Describe this data import map in the Description filed. This is optional but highly recommend. For example, you might want to describe the source or type of the data you are importing. This context can help users know whether to re-use this or an altered version of this Data Import Map in the future.
Map Type (Import Contacts vs. Import Users)
Since the Surefire Data Uploader handles the upload of User and Contact records very differently (Contacts are assigned to users; Contacts might have Deals associated with them; Users are assigned to Surefire Organizational Units etc), the system requires that you specify which type of records this Data Import Map is going to be applied to.
Associate your Map with a Product
When importing User records into Surefire, you will most likely set this attribute to None, since Surefire User Accounts are not explicitly associated with Products or Deals.
However, when importing Contacts into Surefire, it is often the case that they have multiple Deals (for example, Deals for Mortgage Loans) associated with them that you want the Data Uploader to also import into Surefire. Since the Data Uploader is designed to only upload Deals for one product at a time, you must make that association here.
Folder
When a Data Import Map is saved to Surefire, a folder location must be specified. Choose the folder for either an org unit in Surefire (HQ, Region, Branch office etc) or a User.
API Tag
If you are creating a data map that's going to be employed for Data Upload Jobs that are initiated by third party APIs, you can enter the Header that's going to be included with those API calls, the header that will direct the system to use this Data Import Map, here.

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Data Import Maps
Data Import Maps, Create Mappings
Once you have entered your Data Import Map's identifying attributes, you are ready to create your mappings, i.e. associate the types of data in each column of your source data file (e.g. First Name, Address etc) with the appropriate data fields in the Surefire database.
Column to CRM Field vs. CRM Field to Column
The Surefire Data Uploader allows you to create mappings using either of two methodologies:
By choosing a column in your source data file and then associating it with a data field in Surefire or By choosing a source data field in Surefire and associating it with a column in your source data file.
Create your mappings on the CRM Field to Column tab when you are not using a Sample File (described below) but instead want to use an exhaustive, grouped-by-Field-Category list of all fields in Surefire as your starting point.
Create your mappings on the Column to CRM Field tab when you want to use the contents of your source data as your starting point and then either reference a Sample Dataset or Add Columns one-by-one.
You can toggle between the two tabs. Mappings made on one tab will be reflected in the other.
Adding Columns vs. Uploading a Sample File
(Column to CRM Field tab only)
When using the Column to CRM Field method described previoulsy there are two ways you can start creating your mappings: Add a Column or Use a Sample File.
Add a Column
Use this method when you are creating a map that is not based on an existing source datafile.
You might use this method when you are creating a generic map that will lay out what data fields you need populated in Surefire whenever this Data Import Map is employed. Then, later when the map is actually used, the Source Column names can be edited to exactly map the corresponding column headers to match whatever source datafile has been selected for use.
To Add a Column, click one of the Add Column Buttons:
A table is created with an initial row where you can begin to assign mappings (see below for details).
Continue using the Add Column buttons to add more rows (i.e. mappings) to the table.
Use a Sample File
Use this method when you are creating a map that is based on an existing source datafile. That is, you are creating a Data Import Map that is designed to tell the Surefire Data Uploader tool which columns in an existing source datafile whose contents you intend to import correspond to which Contact or User data record fields in the CRM.
To use a sample file, click either the Upload Sample File or Use a Sample File button.
The Use a Sample File screen is generated:
Click the Upload Sample File button to launch your operating system's file selector which you can use to locate the .xlsx, .csv or .json file containing the data for the User or Contact records you want to import into Surefire.
Once selected, the system reads your file and then creates a table where each row corresponds to a column in your source datafile.
Row previews, which show you the initial contents of your source datafile's various columns are also displayed and can be used to help you set your mapping associations (as outlined below).

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Data Import Maps
Data Import Maps, Assign Mappings
Once you have built your table in either the Column to CRM Field or CRM Field to Column tabs, it is time to start assigning mappings.
Regardless of which tab you are viewing, you can always filter to limit what contents of your table are displayed, either by entering a term in to the Filter by Source Column field at the top of the table (to display only Source Columns whose name matches your search term) or by setting the Show only mapped fields switch to ON.
Column to CRM Field
For each row in the table (which, recall, corresponds to a column in your source datafile), click the click to map link in the CRM Field column.
A screen is displayed whose title matches the contents of the Source Column entry for that row.
In the blank space in the pop up, type in all or part of the name of the Surefire Data field you want the contents of that Source Column in your source datafile mapped to.
A drop down menu is displayed containing a list of field names that match the text you entered.
Click on the name of the Surefire field that you want to map.
Once you've made your selection, click the Apply button.
The mapping is added to the table, with the row highlighted in green.
CRM Field to Column
For each row in the table (which, recall, corresponds to a User or Contact record field in Surefire ), click the click to map link in the Source Column column.
A pop up is displayed whose title matches the contents of the Surefire Field Name entry for that row.
In the blank space in the pop up, type in all or part of the name of the header for the column (in your source datafile) that contains the data you want mapped to this Surefire Field.
A drop down menu is displayed containing a list of column names that match the text you entered.
Click on the name of the column that contains the data you want to map to this Surefire data field.
Once you've made your selection, click the Apply button.
The mapping is added to the table, with the row highlighted in green.

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Data Import Maps
Data Import Maps, Mapping Requirements
Data Import Maps, Mapping Requirements Surefire includes the following mapping requirements before a Data Import Map can be saved:
User Account Imports
A User Record Import Map must have the following four Surefire fields mapped to your source data: User First Name, User Last Name, User Role and User Email.
Contact Record Imports
A Contact Record Import Map must have the following three Surefire fields mapped to your source data: Contact First Name, Contact Last Name and Contact Type.
One to Many Mappings Surefire includes the ability to create one to many mappings. This means that the same source data can be mapped to (and thus imported into) more than one field in Surefire at the same time.
A great example of when you might use this feature is when you are importing a contact who serves multiple purposed for your organization, for example someone who is both a buying agent and a co-brand marketing partner.
To setup a one-to-many mapping, follow the instructions included under the Column to CRM Field bullet in the Assign Mappings section above. Once you've mapped a Surefire field, instead of clicking apply, simply enter another search term into the the blank space in the pop up and make another selection from the options displayed in the drop down menu.
Special Cases
Importing certain data types into Surefire using the Data Uploader requires special care.
No Username Specified in Source Datafile
When importing user accounts, if no user name is specified in the source datafile, then the system will automatically create one by using the email address provided in the source datafile for that user record, but with the addition of a random three-digit number inserted before the "@."
Importing User Accounts to Specific Organizational Units (aka Branches)
Organizational Units (aka Branch Names) in Surefire are text sensitive. Thus, if you are importing user accounts into the Boston Branch, your import will fail if the contents of the source datafile's column that you've mapped to "Company Name" in Surefire read "boston branch" with lower case "b"s.

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Data Import Maps
Data Import Maps, Translations
Data Import Maps allow for the application of Translations, where the contents of individual source datafile entries (i.e. cells in your source datafile spreadsheet) can be automatically altered as part of writing them to Surefire during the import process.
Translations are analogous to running an automated Search and Replace on your source data during the upload process. Translations can only be configured after you have assigned your mappings as outlined above in this document.
Note that Translations only affect the data that's written to Surefire; the contents of your source datafile(s) remain unchanged.
Apply Translations
To Apply Translations to a Data Import Map:
For any Data Import Map where mappings have been assigned, while editing the map, go to the Translations tab.
(Optional) Set the Show only mapped field with data translations toggle switch to on to limit the contents of the displayed table to only those Source Column to Surefire Data Field mappings where Translations have already been applied.
Find the row in the table that includes the Source Column to Surefire Data Field mapping that you want to apply one or more Translations to.
That is, find the entry in the table that points to the column in your source datafile that includes entries (i.e. cell contents) that you might want to apply a text search-and-replace to before they're uploaded to Surefire.
For that row, click on the link in the Data Translations column of the table.
A Data Translations pop up is displayed for that Surefire Data Field.
To continue our Search-and-Replace analogy, in the field on the left, enter your search term. Then, in the field on the right, enter your replace term.
For all data in the column in our source data spreadsheet that we have mapped to the Surefire Contact Data Field "Contact Loan Type," whenever there is a value equal to "FarmerHomeAdministration," the Data Uploader will populate the Contact Loan Type field in Surefire with the following value: Other.
(Optional) Click the plus button to add an additional Translation to be applied to this mapping.
Delete any Translations that have been applied to this mapping by clicking on the trash can icon displayed at the far right of that Translation entry on the Data Translations pop up.
Click the Clear All button in the lower left of the Data Translations pop up to remove all Translations that have been applied to this mapping.
Click Save.
You are returned to the Edit Import Map screen.
The system indicates how many Translations you have applied to any of this Data Import Map's mappings.
Review Translations Applied to a Data Import Map
To review any Translations applied to a Data Import Map, simply find an existing data import map in the system, click on it to populate the right panel of the mappings screen and then click on the Translations tab.
Any Translations that have been applied to any of the mappings included with that Data Import Map are displayed.

Data Import Maps, Minimum Field Rules
For Contact Record import jobs, Surefire allows you to limit the importation of unwanted duplicate records by configuring your Data Import Maps with Minimum Field Rules.
These rules set the Minimum Required Fields (e.g. First Name, Last Name, Email) that an imported Entity Type (e.g. Contact, Co-Borrower, Listing Agent) must have populated in the external data file in order for Surefire to import that record (i.e. row in the external data file).

The Minimum Fields Rules pop up is displayed.
Use the Entity drop down menu to select the Entity Type (i.e. category of field types) that includes the type of fields you want the system to require to be be populated (i.e. have data in them) in order for Surefire to import the record.
Click on the Minimum Fields to Save drop down menu to select which specific field(s) will need to be populated in order for Surefire to import the record.
The contact associated with a given row in your external data file will not be imported into Surefire if this Data Import Map is applied if there is not entries in the columns for: Spouse Email, Spouse First Name and Spouse Last Name.

SFTP (Secure File Transfer Protocol) allows you to transfer files between systems securely.
When an SFTP has been provisioned for your organization, go to mapping templates and select more options, SFTP Configuration to enter the SFTP settings.
Each data mapping can be turned on for SFTP importing. Once on, additional fields are available for PGP (Pretty Good Privacy) encryption specification, File Name Pattern and File Extension.

QoS Alerts
This setting is available in mapping templates. Select more options , QoS Alerts to configure QoS Alerts.
After configuration the alerts provide:
Success notifications for jobs in Surefire:
Success status along with count of updated records.
Contain success status along with count of warning, errors, and ignored records.
Failure notifications for jobs in Surefire:
Contain the reason for failure including file extension mismatch and processing or decryption failures.
Jobs with .pgp (encyrypted), .csv and .json. file sizes exceeding max limit (100 MB) are not processed.
Jobs with .xlsx file sizes exceeding max limit (50 MB) are not processed.
Each data mapping can define the admin email address(es) to notify.
All successes and failures for upload jobs can also be viewed in Data Upload Health Checks.

Manage Data Import Maps Surefire Data Uploader uses Data Import Maps to associate the various data types included in the columns of an external data file (e.g. First Name, Last Name, Email Address etc.) with the corresponding data fields in Surefire so that the system will know how to correctly import the contents of that data file.
The contents of any unmapped columns in your data file will not be imported into Surefire. Surefire includes a number of simple Data Import Map Templates, stored in a Public folder, for you to reference and potentially copy and then alter for use in order to satisfy your organization's particular data import needs.
Data Import Maps can also be created from scratch, with or without the use of an example data file for reference. Additionally, they can be created as part of Creating a Data File Upload Job. Lastly, they can be created by copying and then altering an existing map, cloning.
In Surefire, Data Import Maps are listed and managed under CRM Settings, Data, Manage Mappings.
