CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Tag Data Uploads
When uploading multiple, like-categorized contact records, you can use the Data Uploader to, as part of the uploading process, bulk-apply one or more of the same Tags to each Contact record and/or (if named in your source datafile) Co-Contact or Deal Team Member Contact Records that you already have set up in Surefire.
This is accomplished by using Job Contact Tagging function.
If you created a spreadsheet containing contact information for 100 attendees of a trade show. You can use the Data Uploader to import these contacts into Surefire as individual Contact Records, you can use the Job Contact Tagging function in order to apply the tag Las Vegas Trade Show to each new record that gets created in Surefire.
Additionally, your spreadsheet contains details about attendees to the Trade Show also included references to Contacts you already have in Surefire.
For example, you met Chidi Smith at the trade show because your existing Surefire contact Eleanor Jones referred him to you. Thus, in the row in your spreadsheet that includes Chidi's contact details, there might be an entry under the column Referred By with Eleanor's name in it.
When you use the Data Uploader to import your Trade Show Contacts, you can use Job Contact Tagging to add a Tag to any existing Co-Contacts (Referred By, Spouse, Co-Brand Marketing Partner), you might direct the system to append a Tag to your existing contact Eleanor that with Related, LV Trade Show.
In another example, you set up a Deal with an attendee, Jason Mendoza, at the trade show. In the row in your spreadsheet that includes Jason's contact and deal details, there might be entries under the columns Buying Agent, Listing Agent, and Processor with the names of your Surefire contacts Derek Dawn, Kamila Al-Jamil and Chris Baker.
Because, when you use the Data Uploader to import your Trade Show Contacts you can use Job Contact Tagging to add a Tag to any Deal Team Members for whom you already have Contact Records in Surefire, you might direct the system to append a Tag to your existing contacts Derek, Kamila and Chris that says On Deal, LV Trade Show.
Overriding Mapped Tags
The Job Contact Tagging function is designed to override any mapped tags.
That is, if your source datafile happens to include columns for Tags that you have in fact mapped in your Data Import Map (to the Surefire Contact Record fields Contact Tag, Co-Contact Tag and/or Spouse Tag), but you also employ the Job Contact Tagging function in order to apply tags, then, in the case(s) where there is conflict (i.e. the system is directed, as part of the upload job, to apply one tag to a Contact in Surefire per your data import mapping and also apply a different tag to that Same Contact per the Job Contact Tagging function), then the tags defined in the Job Contact Tagging function take precedence and will be applied, while the ones that are included in your source datafile will not be applied.
Bulk Apply Tags to a Data Upload Job
Create or Select a Data File Upload Job.
Select your Data File Upload Job.
In the Job Contact Tagging section select Manage.
The Job Contact Tagging screen for this Data File Upload Job is displayed.
In each Entity field; Contacts, Co-Contacts and Deal Team Member you enter all or part of the name of a Tag.
Select an option from the list of existing tags.
You can add multiple tag(s)
To delete a tag click on the x in the tag name.
Select Save.
Review the number of tags you have applied to each entity type on the Data File Upload Job screen in the Job Contact Tagging section.
When you Process this Data File Upload Job, the imported Contact Records will include the tags you defined for the entity Contacts.
Additionally, for any rows in your source data file where a Co-Contact is defined (i.e. there is a column present named Referred By, Spouse, and/or Co-Brand Marketing Partner and , there are names of existing Contacts in Surefire ), that Co-Contact's Contact entry in Surefire will have the tags you defined for the entity Co-Contact in the previous steps, appended to it.
Finally, for any rows in your source data file where a Deal Team Member is defined (i.e. there is one or more columns present named for a Deal Team Member slot that has been created for one of your products in Surefire and in each of those columns, there are names of existing Contacts in Surefire ), that Deal Team Member's Contact entry in Surefire will have the tags you defined for the entity Deal Team Members in the previous steps, appended to it.

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Revert Surefire Data to Pre-Data Upload State
In cases when the results of a completed Data File upload job are not satisfactory, Surefire includes the option of reverting all Surefire Data to the state it was in prior to that job being run.
When a Data File Upload Job is processed, the system first creates a time-stamped backup snapshot of all of your Surefire Data.
Once the Job is completed, should you wish, you can use the Revert Status function to return your Surefire e data to the state it was in when the snapshot was taken.
However, applying the Revert Status function doesn't undo your Data File Upload Job. Rather it overwrites all of your Surefire Data with whatever Data was present at the time the backup snapshot was taken. This means that any changes or additions made to your Surefire data since the Data File Upload Job was run will also be undone.
To Revert Status
Select a Completed Data File Upload Job.
In the Completed section, select Revert Status.
In the Revert Job Status screen, type
I Understand.
Select Yes, revert!
Your Surefire Data is restored to the state it was in prior to that Data File Upload Job being run and the Job is returned to draft status as though it had just been created.
You must Run Health Check before the Job can be processed again.

CRM Master Settings
Data File Management
Data Settings in Master Settings
The Data Settings tab (formally the Data Duplication tab) in Master Settings allows Primary admins data management for Data Duplication, Data Health Check, Primary Deal and Data Health Check, Mailing Address. Data Duplication - Create and manage duplication policies that are set to ensure data records entered into Surefire do not create duplicate or conflicting contacts, users, or deal records.
Review Manage Data Duplication for additional information.
Data Health Check, Primary Deal -
Allows for the initiation of a “data health check” that checks for and updates, as necessary, the appropriate deal information into the Primary Deal slots for each user within an organization. As appropriate, the primary deal health check will populate the primary deal slot based on deals that are closed, have the newest (most recent) closing date, and are identified as first lien for each occupancy type (primary residence, secondary residence, and investment). Upon completion of the Primary Deal Data Health Check, the Admin will receive confirmation of success and will be able to download from the Data Health Check Log a report of deals and associated data that were updated to the primary deal slots.
Data Health Check, Mailing Address -
Allows for the initiation of a “data health check” that checks for and updates, as necessary, the mailing address for contacts, spouses, and/or co-contacts. The mailing address health check will update based on the product address of the deal that is closed with the newest (most recent) closing date, is identified as “first lien,” and is identified as primary residence for occupancy type. Upon completion of the Data Health Check, the Admin will receive confirmation of success and will be able to download a detailed report (contact ID, contact name, mailing address, deal closing date, deal address, deal file number) of contacts with mailing addresses that were updated. Download-able reports will be available in the Data Health Check log.

Standard internet protocols expect that the domain portion of an email address will match the name of the sending email server. So, emails sent to bill@mycontact.com from joe@mymortgage.com should come from the mymortgage.com server. The Internet will trust this two-party transaction. With Surefire, an email sent to bill@mycontact.com from joe@mymortgage.com will come from a topofmind.com server. This is called a third-party email transaction, and the internet does not trust this type of transaction because Surefire is spoofing the email address and sending it from a third-party server. The internet considers this spam.
However, because legitimate third-party email is used by many marketers sending emails to individuals who want to receive their email a work around is required. To accommodate this need, protocols have been developed to allow marketers to authorize third-party senders to send emails on their behalf. This authorization is provided by placing an SPF TXT record on the sender’s email server. With the SPF record in place the recipient’s email server pings the sender’s email server and ask if Surefire is authorized to send emails on behalf of the sender. The sender’s email server sends authorization, and the email is delivered. With no authorization the email may be diverted to spam.
So, if you are using a third-party sender, you must have the ability to control your email server so that you can add the correct SPF TXT record to your server. If you are using a public email address like gmail.com, hotmail.com, att.com, etc., you may not be able to add or edit the SPF TXT record attached to that server.
If your company has a website, we recommend that you use your company’s email server for your email. If not, then you will need to register a domain name and set up an email server for that name. So, if you are using joethemortgageguy@gmail.com, we recommend that you instead use something like joe@themortgageguy.com. When you set up your email server you should have your IT department or the support team at your hosting company add the correct SPF record for your domain. Please see SPF Record and Whitelisting Guide for Surefire Users for details on how to do this.
Always Choose a Top-Level Domain Name
When choosing a domain name, we recommend that you always use a Standard Top-Level Domain (TLD) Name. You should not use a generic Top-Level Domain (gTLD). A standard Top-Level Domain (TLD) is .com, .net, .org. A generic Top-Level Domain (gTLD) is a domain name like .mortgage, .consultant, .realtor. A high percentage of spam is generated from gTLD’s and may not trusted by the internet. If you use a gTLD you may experience email delivery issues.

CRM Master Settings
Email Deliverability
Sender Policy Framework (SPF) Record
To Ensure that Your Contacts Receive the eEmails that you send you must edit your SPF TXT record to read: Copy v=spf1  include: sendgrid.net -all Surefire is a third party e-mail service. To authorize Surefire to send emails on your behalf please add the reference include: sendgrid.net to your domains SPF TXT record in your account where your domain is registered.
The easiest way to do this is to copy the suggested SPF TXT record shown above and paste it over the existing SPF TXT record. Do not create a second SPF TXT record. Only one SPF record is allowed.
Reach out to your email registrar if you need further assistance with your SPF record.

CRM Master Settings
Email Deliverability
CNAMEs
Add these 5 CNAMEs to your DNS server and update your DMARC policy that was sent to your company admin at Email Set-up. If you are unsure if you were given this, please advise our Support Team, and we can get those CNAMEs for you.
DKIM
Internet protocols require that third-party email senders comply with DKIM (Domain Keys Identified Mail) protocols. DKIM allows the receiver to check that an email was indeed sent and authorized by the owner of that domain. This is done by adding a digital DK IM signature on emails. We add DKIM keys by adding CNAMEs to your DNS server.
Internet protocols also require that emails be sent from a server that matches the domain name in your email address. Also any image or video content in your emails must be hosted on the same server as the sending e-mail domain. This is called Domain Alignment. Because Surefire sends all emails from a SendGrid server, and host all image and video content sent via Surefire on our servers, we achieve domain alignment by adding CNAMEs to your DNS server
To find instructions on adding the CNAMEs to your account, please refer to your email registrar for further assistance.

The Return Address (Mail Envelope From)

Applies the policy based on the masked address used in the message's header.
Both Applies the policy based on either the Mail Envelope From or the Message Header From whichever matches. When both match, the specified value the Message Header From will be used.

Reasons for Delivery Issues
Many ISPs and e-mail filtering companies (Mimecast, SPAMCOP, Barracuda) have developed strategies to reduce the spam delivered to their clients. One of these strategies is to create blacklists of what they perceive are risky. When a sending email server is on their blacklist, all email from that server is blocked from reaching all of their clients. Unfortunately, sometimes even good actors that do not present risk are put on the list.
How do they create their blacklists? Spammers often purchase huge lists of email addresses for their solicitations. As a risk management strategy, the filtering companies will seed these lists with bogus email addresses, also known as spam traps. When one of these spam traps or bogus email addresses passes through their filter, they know it was part of a purchased list and automatically blacklist the sending server.
What happens if Top of Mind is blacklisted? When we learn of a problem, our team takes immediate steps for removal.
What should you do it you’re not receiving Top of Mind emails? Please submit a ticket by emailing Surefire support@ice.com immediately to let us know. If we determine emails are being blocked by one of the filtering companies, we will let you know, and you can follow steps in the next section. This issue likely only affects our clients who have contracted with a third-party email filtering service. If that is the case for you, it will be your responsibility to work with your email filtering partner to resolve this issue.
Will this affect emails that I send to my contacts? It is possible that recipients of emails you send through Surefire have subscribed to a spam filtering service, which may prevent delivery of the emails. If you find that is that case, then you will need to ask them to whitelist our servers with their spam filtering service as described on the attached document. Emails sent to you normal contacts with public email addresses like gmail.com, Hotmail.com, aol.com, att.com, or Verizon.com are less likely to be directly blocked. However, it is possible that the emails may be throttled. Email throttling controls the rate at which emails may be delivered to a specific server. If you send several thousand emails to the gmail.com server, they may have a limit on the number of emails from a specific sender that they will accept within a specified time frame. If that limit is reached subsequent emails are throttled, meaning that the delivery may be delayed up to 72 hours. There is nothing specific that can be done about throttling as throttling policies vary greatly among receiving email servers.

Email Distribution, Domain Suppression
The optional Email Distribution, Domain Suppression is designed to prevent emails from being sent to specific domains.
You can use this when:
A company requests to be removed entirely from your mailing lists.
You want to avoid sending emails to personal domains (e.g., gmail.com, yahoo.com) for compliance or targeting reasons.
You're managing B2B campaigns and want to exclude certain organizations.
Ensuring that your marketing communications aren’t sent to undesirable or unengaged recipients.
This feature is available upon request.
Admins can add and save domains. Additionally, admins can view and search for banned domains. Complete the following steps to setup Email Distribution, Domain Suppression:
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select the Email
Tab.
Slide the Domain Suppression toggle to turn on this feature.
Enter a domain name in the Add Suppressed Domains field.
You must enter domain names in their entirety (e.g. @mail.com, not just mail.com) to avoid unexpected domains to be suppressed
Avoid spaces or additional characters, which can lead to errors (e.g.,.@ca.com
Consider adding invalid or fake email domains (e.g., @test.com) to test
Click Save.
When this feature is engaged:
Contacts with email addresses with banned domains are suppressed and opted out from receiving emails.
Contact records email addresses with banned domains display in red.

CRM Master Settings
Update Company Branding
Here is a checklist of items to consider if you are an admin on an account and you need to update the account branding. These are things you need to make sure you are aware of with the change. This is not a full list, but is meant as a guide to help you through the process.
Any time you change the name of your company, contact your Account Manager. Here are some questions and information you can share with us.
What were the circumstances involved in the change?
Were you acquired?
Are you simply changing your branding or DBA?
Are there any users on the account who are no longer with the firm as part of this change?
If so, have we shut them off as a user and do we need to be aware of any arrangements you have made with them regarding their data in the CRM?
Are there any contractual considerations if the organization was purchased?
Is billing information the same?
Are there potentially new users we need to add to the account as part of this?
Is there any new leadership we need to meet?
There are many things to consider with a change like this, so it is always good for us to be in the loop.
Additional items you might want to be aware of in the account:
Did you make sure to update your logo?
Did you make sure to not only update the organization name, but also the “display name”?
Are there any relevant updates to be made to organization and display names of your branches?
Does any license information need to change? Remember license information can exist at both the organization and branch levels, as well as general license info vs state by state. Some of these license blurbs may mention an old company name, etc.
Did you update your user roster and contact information for each user? Often times email domains, websites, office lines, addresses etc. can change. Does the org hierarchy and branches remain the same? Remember to check signature blocks and disclaimers in the CRM, flyers, and Single Property Sites as well.
Does any of your content mention by name the old company name? We always recommend using a merge field for company name so it can change dynamically. But sometimes users don’t abide by this and type out a company name or include an image (specifically in flyers) relevant to the old company name. You may need your Account Manager to help query your content for any text mention of the old company, we can run internal queries on request for specific search strings.
Did you update your branding colors under account settings?

CRM Master Settings
Pretty Good Privacy Encryption
Pretty Good Privacy (PGP) is a data encryption and decryption program that provides cryptographic privacy and authentication for data communication. It’s widely used for securing emails, files, and other forms of digital communication.
A key is assigned to your organization for using PGP encryption. Administrators are able to view and download keys under
My Company, Company info, Encryption Keys tab.
PGP uses a combination of symmetric-key encryption and public-key encryption to ensure both speed and security. PGP encryption involves two keys.
The Public Key is shared with others to encrypt data. The sender encrypts the file using the recipient’s public key.
The Private Key is kept secret and used to decrypt data. The recipient decrypts the file using their private key.
This ensures that only the intended recipient can read the data file.
Requirement

Good to have
Not Allowed

These reports, once created, can be run manually or automatically with (optional) distribution, with their export-able results organized, filtered and visualized in a variety of ways.

Custom Reports
Custom Reports Metrics
Metrics are the attributes of the selected activity or event that you want to see totaled in the report. A report can have multiple metrics.
There are three types of metrics: Count of Rows - Total number of occurrences of this event or activity over the selected date range Average of - Average of the values for a field that you then select. Available selections depend on the activity or event you are generating a report for. Sum of - Sum of the values for a field that you then select. Available selections depend on the activity or event you are generating a report for.
You can add additional metrics by selecting Add Metric.
Delete a metric from this report by clicking next to that metric.
You can reorder metrics that are displayed in the report using to move each metric.

Reports
Custom Reports
Custom Reports Filters
For each filter, you first select the field, associated with the selected event or activity, you want to apply the filter to, then you select an operator, and then lastly, if the selected operator demands one, a value.
When selecting a field to apply a filter to, you can either scroll through the list menu or type all or part of the field name directly into the filter field.
Some examples of operators are: is equal to is not equal to contains does not contain starts with ends with is empty is not empty is any of is none of An example of using filters might be when you want to generate a report about Contacts (e.g. "Contacts Created") but limit the results of the report to only include Contacts living in Chicago and that have a spouse.

Reports
Custom Reports
Custom Reports Grouping
Grouping allows you to select by which attributes the events or activities included in your report are listed. A way to think of this might be column heading. For example, if you are generating a report about User Email activities and select the row grouping of User, your report would list Email activities by User.
In the Additional Grouping field, you can select Row Grouping from the list and add an item such as User Role. This adds an additional column to your report's data table, showing User Role.
Alternatively, in the Additional Grouping field you can select an additional Column Grouping. Continuing with our email metrics example, with this selection option, there are entries for each user for each metric, divided into multiple column sets, one for each type of User Role.

When you Add a Deal to a Contact, in addition to assigning it a Product, you also Assign a Sales Process.
Review Add a Deal, Create a Product, Assign a Sales Process for additional information.
The Sales Process is a series of Phases or Stages that a Deal progresses through as it moves through the pipeline on its way to closing.
Examples of the Phases in a Sales Process:
Received Application
Underwriting
Processing

Sales Process
Add a Sales Process
Go to Sales Settings, Sales Process.
Click + button at the top of the vertical panel on the left of the screen.
Complete the following fields: Sales Process Name - field required Sales Process Description - a brief summary about what the Sales Process applies to Include Anticipated Close Date - defaults to ON. If ON, every Deal with this Sales Process type will include a Close Date to assist in forecasting and reporting. Anticipated Close Date Label - if Include Anticipated Close Date is ON, use this field to customize what you want to call the Close Date label
Click Add New Phase.
The Phases make up the bulk of the Sales Process. These are the steps that a Deal must move through as it heads toward completion.
Enter a Name.
Enter a Description.
Enter a Percentage, this is the close probability percentage.
To help forecast future closed sales, you can assign a percentage to each Phase that indicates its probability of closing. (If you don't wish to use this field, you can keep it set to 0%.)
When you set the Close Percentage, the system will automatically force you to have each stage in sequence with earlier Phases having lower percentages of than higher Phases.
The system will not let you save a Sales Process if these percentages are out of order. (e.g. you have a Phase with a 10% Percentage after a Phase with 50% Percentage.)
Select Won or Lost in Phase Closed field.
You can also choose if a Phase indicates if a Deal is Won or Lost. Generally, you'd only have one Phase set to Won (e.g. Loan Funded). The Percentage of Won Phases will automatically be set to 100%.
For Lost Phases, you could add multiple Phases. such as:
Lost - Went with Competitor
Lost - Too Expensive
Lost - No Longer Needed
When a Deal is Lost, you can move it into its appropriate Lost Phase and it will fall off your Pipeline. Tracking the Phases with these types of reasons also makes it easier for you to identify why you are losing Deals.
Tags & Use Tags
When you click on a Sales Process in the Sales Process List, you will have the option to add Tags or Use Tags.
Enter a Tag name into the form box. If the tag already exists it will populate in the drop-down and you can select it. Alternatively click enter to create a new Tag. Once you do this it will automatically Save and apply to the Product.
To add or edit Use Tags, click on the Use Tags box to bring up the Use Tags Editor. This displays existing Use Tags as well as let you add more or remove existing.
Review Create a Tag and Manage Tags for additional information.

Sales Process
Assign a Sales Process
Every time you add a Deal, you must assign it a Sales Process. The Sales Process is a series of Phases or Stages that a Deal must move through as it progresses towards closing.
Go to Contacts, View Contacts or View Leads.
Find the Contact you want to add a deal for and click on their name.
Review Contacts for additional information.
In the Contact Details panel, select Deals tab.
Select a Product in the list.
This option will only be visible If you are using a Custom Product.
Select Add New Deal.
Use the Sales Process list to assign a Sales Process to this Deal.
Complete the Product details.
Select Create Deal.
When you Convert a Lead, i.e. the Contact is moving into the Deal Pipeline for serious sales opportunities with a higher chance of closing, you must also assign, along with a Product and Contact Type, a Sales Process.
Assign a Sales Process when Converting a Lead
Go to Contacts, View Contacts or View Leads.
Find the Lead Contact you want to convert and select on their name.
In the Contact Details panel, select Convert.
In the Convert Lead screen, use the Sales Process list to assign a Sales Process to the Deal you are creating that has spurred the conversion of this Lead.
Select Convert.

Sales Process
Change Deal Team Configuration for In-Process Videos
Purchase In-Process videos are available in the following configurations:
Standard (no description next to title): LO, Buying Agent, Listing Agent, Processor
No Listing Agent: LO, Buying Agent Processor
No Processor: LO, Buying Agent, Listing Agent
There are four slots available for branding the In-Process videos. These are typically the LO (user), listing agent, buying agent and processor. If an org wants to use an additional position, such as LOA, they will have to replace one of those four slots with the LOA position.
Replace the Standard Configuration
Clone the appropriate Landing Page.
Go to Media Library.
Select Assets.
Select Landing Pages.
Select on the applicable landing page .
Select Clone.
Choose the folder where you want to save the new Landing Page, and select Clone Landing Page.
Select to edit the landing page.
Go to the new folder and open the Landing Page you just created.
Rename the landing page by clicking on the gear button on the left side and save.
Click on Select Content Block near the top right of the screen and select the Content Block from the dropdown which has the Configurable Dynamic Video.
Map the fields to Deal Variables, then click Next. If Pro Series, you only need select the Product.
Select a Product (If application) loanStreetName = Address Line 1 loanCity = City loanState = State
Complete the Persons Appearing workflow screen: Borrower - Contact Co-borrower - Co-borrower LO - Myself
Other slots as applicable.
Only the slots for people appearing in the dynamic video you selected will appear here. In this sample, there is no Processor. In the No Listing Agent Sample, there will be no Listing Agent.
Click Next.
Select Preview and Save.
Locate the corresponding email collection and select.
Select Clone from the list, choose the folder and click Clone Collection.
Edit the Email Collection. Go to the folder, open the collection and rename it. Click the Save icon under the Collection Name.
In the body of the email, find the image that represents the landing page. Click to edit.
Click Next to Landing Page, then select the new landing page you just created. Click Apply.
Select your Domain.
Select Save.
Repeat this process for borrower and co-borrower versions of each of the in-process videos used.

's Calendar to record and manage appointments, reminders or tasks like scheduled phone calls.
To access your calendar, select Calendar in the main menu.
The Calendar looks similar to other common calender tools with entries displayed either in a Calendar grid or a List.
Calendar Search
Enter a term in the Search field in the upper left of the Calendar window to locate a specific Calendar entry.
Display Calendar Entry Types
Specify which Calendar entry Types to display by selecting the respective check boxes under My Calendars. Choose from:
Meetings
Calls
Tasks
Other
Add Calendar Entry
Select.
Select either Add a Meeting or Add a Task.
This launches the Add Meeting or Add Task windows respectively.
Review Add a Meeting or Add a Task From the Calendar View for additional information.
Choose View Type Use the View Type buttons, to select how your Calendar entries are displayed; either in Calendar (grid) or List (table) view. List view is convenient if you want to sort your Calendar entries by Name, Location, Time, Recurrence or Alert status.
Calendar Default Settings
Use the Calendar's Default Settings function to set the following default attributes: View Mode - Select from Calendar (grid) or List (table) view. View - Select whether the default view displays Calendar entries for a single day, a week at time, or for an entire month at a time. Duration - Select the default time duration (from 5 minutes up to 2 weeks) for a Calendar entry.
To open Calendar Default Settings, select on the Calendar screen.
Navigation
Use the Navigation to scroll backward and forward through the dates in your Calendar to display a desired day.
View Selection
Use View Selection to choose how to display your Calendar entries by:
Day
Week
Month

Calendar
Connect Calendar to MS Exchange
You can connect your Microsoft Exchange, Office 365 or Outlook Calendar with your Surefire Calendar allowing you to enter meetings and appointments, either manually or by using the Surefire system. Then they are automatically added to your MS Exchange Calendar.
This function does not support versions of Outlook prior to Outlook 2013, nor does the connection support Outlook access that requires VPN or two-factor authentication.
Review Microsoft Authentication Configuration for additional information.
Surefire Calendar entries are only synced with Exchange upon their creation; any changes made will not be reflected in your Exchange Calendar.
Go to My Account , My Profile.
Select Integrations tab.
Click Add New Integration.
Select MS Exchange Calendar.
Enter your MS Exchange Credentials.
Complete the fields on the MS Exchange Credentials screen.
Host
If the Exchange Web Server Host URL for your Exchange Server is not automatically populated by your company, you can find this URL by going into the advanced account settings in your MS Exchange Email client.
Exchange Email Address
Some Exchange setups might require you to use DOMAIN\username instead of your Email Address. For example, if your email is tsmith@patriots.com you would format your Exchange Email Address as PATRIOTS\tsmith ( note the use of backslash "\" and not forward slash).
Exchange Password
Test Meeting Name
This is the name of the meeting that Surefire will attempt to create in your MS Exchange calendar.
Click Test.
Open and check your MS Exchange Calendar to verify that your test meeting synced from Surefire.
Select Save in Surefire if the test run is successful.

Your tasks are displayed in the My Tasks window to the left of your calendar.
Click View All at the top to view your tasks in a detailed list view on a separate page.

Calendar
Add and Manage Tasks
Mark a Task Completed
When the Mark as Completed checkbox is selected, the task is completed and will no longer appear in your Task List. Completed tasks display a completion date.
There are a multiple ways you can mark a task completed:
Select Calendar, Tasks.
In My Tasks, click the check box next to the task that you want to mark as completed.
Click more options in the applicable task.
Select Mark as Completed.
Go to Calendar, Tasks, Detailed Tasks View.
Select the check box on the applicable Task.
Go to Calendar, Tasks, Detailed Tasks View.
Select more options
Select Complete Task.
When you complete a task in any of the described ways the Update Task Status screen appears.
In the Status filed select either: Completed or Skipped
In the Follow Up field select: Create follow up task - to add a follow up task Add contact note - adds a Notes for free form field that you can complete. Contacted Person - appears which updates the last contacted field and updates in the contact record.
Select Update Status.

Calendar
Add and Manage Tasks
Add a Meeting
Your Calendar contains two types of items: Meetings and Tasks. Meetings are typical calendar events that you would enter or accept in any calendar application.
Review Add and Manage Tasks for additional information.
You can Add a Meeting / Appointment to your Calendar in the following ways:
Click New Item, at the top of the Calendar screen and select Add a Meeting from the list.
Alternatively, in Calendar view, click Day/Time slot in the Calendar grid for the event time.
Event Details
Complete the details of your event:
All items with an * are required.
Enter Name* for the event.
In the Details field, enter a description.
Enter a location on the Where field.
Complete the Starts* field.
You can either enter the times directly using the following format: mm/dd/yyyy 01:45 pm, or you can use the an interactive calendar.
After you enter a Start* time, you can skip directly to selecting a Duration which automatically populates the Ends* field.
Complete the Ends* field.
Select the Duration from the list, between 5 minutes and 2 weeks.
Optionally, select All day event to set the start and end times to be 12 am on consecutive days (the first day being the date you entered in the Starts
* field). The Duration is automatically set to 1 day.
Click in the Recurrence field, the default is Only Once. This option does not make the event recur, however, you can create events that automatically recur in your calendar.
Select the Recurrence field list to see the following options:
Daily
Weekly
Biweekly
Monthly
Yearly Custom - If you select a Custom recurrence, seven buttons appear for each day of the week. Click the button corresponding to the day(s) of the week on which you want this event to recur.
Select Is Appointment?
An Appointment is an Event that a Surefire Contact gets invited to. This Event will then be associated in the history of that Contact.
Select Email Invite to My Inbox, if company turned on, to have an email appointment invite of your calendar/task sent to your personal email. Accept the invite to have it added to your personal calendar.
Review Calendar Invites for additional information.
Click Add.
If you do not select Add your meeting details are not saved.

Calendar
Calendar Invites
For users that are unable to integrate their mailboxes with Surefire, there is a feature that allows your Surefire admin the ability to allws users to send their appointments to their inbox so they can keep their calendars up-to-date.
Turn on Calendar Invite Emails
To turn on the calendar invite emails, update the Master Settings for your organization:
Go to CRM Settings, Master Settings.
Select General tab.
Turn on Email Calendar Invite to User for Appointments.
Create a New Appointment
Go to Dashboard.
Select Contacts.
Select the specific contact associated with the appointment.
Click to create a new appointment.
Update the appointment details.
Verify that Email Invite to My Inbox is allowed.
Select Add.
After you click Add, you will receive an email containing a calendar invite file.
Download and open the file using your calendar application to add it to your calendar.
Delete an Appointment
Navigate to Calendar, Calendar.
Select the meeting that you want to edit.
Select Delete.
Verify the Email Invite to My Inbox is turned on if you want the event update to be mailed to your in box.
Confirm the deletion by selecting
Yes, Delete it!
If you selected to have the calendar invite mailed to your inbox, you'll receive a calendar invite file (file type .ics). You may download this file to have the event removed from your calendar.
Review Add and Manage Tasks for additional information.

Calendar
Subscribe to Calendar
You can view and access your Surefire Calendar entries from other Calendar programs, such as Outlook or your phone's calendar app.
To view entries from your Surefire Calendar in an External Calendar:
Select Calendar.
Click.
In the Calendar Export screen that appears, copy the link in the Copy Link field.
Go to the other Calendar program that you want your Surefire Calendar entries to appear in.
This process outlines the steps followed with Outlook Calendar, however most Calendar software’s have the option to add another Calendar's entries by URL internet calendar.
In most Outlook programs, select File, Account Settings , Account Settings.
Select Internet Calendars tab.
Select New.
Paste the link copied previously.
Select Add.
Open the Outlook calendar.
Under Other Calendars section, a new entry for your just-added Surefire Calendar with a checkbox next to it displays.
Select the Surefire Calendar check box.
Entries from your Surefire Calendar will now appear in your Outlook Calendar. However, they are read-only which means you will not be able to make changes to them. Any changes must be made in Surefire

ECRM to Surefire - Self Migration
Mortgage Technology® currently offers two of the leading CRM solutions in the mortgage industry:
Encompass®
CRM and Surefire. Our goal is to streamline our R&D efforts on a singular, scalable marketing automation solution, Surefire. This allows us to accelerate innovation and provide the features your team needs to drive leads and close more loans. The processes described in this section are designed to support your self-migration from Encompass®
CRM (ECRM) to Surefire.
